Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
6 min
The Four Categories: Sabab, 'Illah, Shart, 'Alamah
Definition and distinction of the four categories related to rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria to classify any given muta'alliq (related thing) as sabab, 'illah, shart, or 'alamah and explain the distinction.

Core Idea
Sabab leads, 'illah causes, shart conditions, 'alamah signals—each relates differently to the ruling.

This passage introduces four categories of things that relate to legal rulings: sabab (reason), 'illah (effective cause), shart (condition), and 'alamah (sign). The commentary provides a clear decision tree to distinguish them based on their relationship to the ruling. Mastering this classification is essential for correct qiyas and legal reasoning in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Classification Framework
The commentary presents a sequential test: if the thing is internal to the ruling, it is a rukn (excluded here). If external, check if it is effective (mu'aththir) → 'illah; if it leads to the ruling in general → sabab; if the ruling depends on it → shart; otherwise → 'alamah.
This decision tree is the key to distinguishing the four categories.
2
Define Sabab Precisely
Sabab in usul is that which leads to the ruling in general. The passage excludes 'alamah (which merely indicates) and metaphorical causes (like an oath that leads to expiation) from this definition.
Sabab is a path, not the effective cause.
3
Distinguish Sabab from 'Illah
The obligation of the ruling is attributed to the 'illah because it is effective; the sabab is merely a means that leads to the ruling without being its effective cause.
Example: the entry of the time of prayer is a sabab for the obligation, but the time itself (as a divine command) is the 'illah.
4
Identify Shart and 'Alamah
A shart is something the ruling depends on; without it, the ruling does not exist (e.g., water for wudu). An 'alamah is a sign that indicates the ruling but does not cause or lead to it (e.g., dawn for Fajr prayer).
Distinguishing shart from sabab: shart is a prerequisite, sabab is a trigger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حقوق العباد فإنها أكثر من أن تحصى، نحو ضمان الدية وبدل التلف أو المغصوب وملك المبيع والثمن وملك الطلاق والنكاح وغير ذلك، فلما فرغ من بيان القسم الأول وهو الأحكام شرع في القسم الثاني وهو ما يتعلّق به الأحكام. فأربعة إلخ ووجه الضبط أن المتعلق إن كان داخلا في الشيء فهو ركن، وإلا فإن كان مؤثرا فيه فعلة، وإلا فإن كان موصلا إليه في الجملة فسبب وإلا فإن كان توقف الشيء عليه فشرط وإلا فهو علامة. ولما كان الركن داخلا في الشيء وهو هنا الحكم لم يعتبر في متعلقات الأحكام، فلم يبق إلا أربعة أقسام، والسبب في اللغة اسم لما يتوصل به إلى المقصود ولذا سمي الطريق سبباً؛ لأنه يتوصل به إلى المقصود في اصطلاح الأصوليين ما بينه المصنف بقوله: أما السبب إلخ. إلى الحكم: أي مفضياً إلى الحكم في الجملة واحترز به عن العلامة، فإنها لاتفضي إلى الحكم بل هي دالة عليه، وعن سبب مجازي؛ فإنه لا يكون طريقاً إلى الحكم كاليمين بالله فإنه سبب مجازي للكفارة. وجوب: أي وجوب الحكم، واحترز بهذا القيد عن العلة؛ لأن الحكم يضاف وجوبه إلى العلة لكونها مؤثرا فيه.
As for the rights of servants, they are too many to be enumerated, such as the guarantee of blood-money, compensation for destruction or usurped property, ownership of the sold item and its price, ownership of divorce and marriage, and other things. When he finished explaining the first section, which is the rulings, he began the second section, which is what relates to the rulings. So [he said] 'four, etc.' and the method of grasping it is that the related thing if it is internal to the thing, then it is a pillar (rukn); otherwise, if it is effective in it, then it is a cause ('illah); otherwise, if it leads to it in general, then it is a reason (sabab); otherwise, if the thing is dependent on it, then it is a condition (shart); otherwise, it is a sign (alamah). Since the pillar is internal to the thing, which here is the ruling, it is not considered among the things related to rulings, so only four categories remain. 'Sabab' in language is a name for what is used to reach the objective, therefore a road is called a sabab because it is used to reach the objective. In the terminology of the usul scholars, it is what the author defined with his statement: 'As for sabab, etc.' [He said] 'to the ruling': i.e., leading to the ruling in general, and by this he excludes the sign (alamah), because it does not lead to the ruling but rather indicates it; and he excludes the metaphorical cause, because it is not a path to the ruling, such as swearing by Allah, which is a metaphorical cause for expiation. 'Obligation': i.e., the obligation of the ruling, and by this restriction he excludes the cause ('illah), because the obligation of the ruling is attributed to the 'illah due to it being effective in it.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classification text in usul al-fiqh. It begins by stating that the rights of servants (huquq al-ibad) are too numerous to list, giving examples. Then it transitions to the second part of the book: the things related to rulings (muta'alliqat al-ahkam). The author introduces four categories: sabab (reason), 'illah (effective cause), shart (condition), and 'alamah (sign). The commentary explains the method of distinguishing them: if the thing is internal to the ruling, it is a rukn (pillar), which is not considered here since it is part of the ruling itself. If it is external, then: if it is effective (mu'aththir), it is 'illah; if it leads to the ruling in general, it is sabab; if the ruling depends on it, it is shart; otherwise, it is 'alamah. Then the commentary defines sabab precisely: in usul, sabab is that which leads to the ruling in general, excluding 'alamah (which merely indicates) and metaphorical causes (like oaths that lead to expiation indirectly). Additionally, sabab is distinguished from 'illah by the fact that the obligation of the ruling is attributed to the 'illah due to its effectiveness, whereas the sabab is merely a path without being the effective cause.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): In usul, sabab is that which leads to the ruling in general, as opposed to 'illah which is effective, and 'alamah which is merely indicative.
علة ('illah): The effective cause of the ruling; the obligation of the ruling is attributed to it because it is effective (mu'aththir).
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the ruling depends; without it the ruling does not exist, but it is not the cause.
علامة ('alamah): A sign that indicates the ruling but does not lead to it or cause it; e.g., the dawn is a sign for the time of Fajr prayer.
ركن (rukn): A pillar that is part of the ruling itself; here not considered among the muta'alliqat because it is internal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a sabab (reason) from an 'alamah (sign) according to this passage?
A) Sabab leads to the ruling, 'alamah merely indicates it
B) Sabab is effective, 'alamah is not
C) Sabab is a condition, 'alamah is a pillar
D) Sabab is internal, 'alamah is external

Key Takeaway
The sabab leads to the ruling in general, the 'illah is its effective cause, the shart is a condition for its existence, and the 'alamah merely indicates it.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Degrees of Sabab (Cause) in Hanafi Usul
Defining sabab and its degrees with application to oaths and conditional divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sabab (cause) in Hanafi usul, enumerate its lowest and highest degrees, and explain how oaths and conditional divorces are classified as metaphorical causes with a semblance of reality.

Core Idea
A sabab is a path to a ruling; its lowest degree is mere path, its highest degree includes the meaning of the illa.

This passage from the Chapter of Qiyas defines sabab and its degrees. Hanafi usul distinguishes between a real cause that inevitably produces its effect and a metaphorical cause that only potentially does so when a condition is fulfilled. Oaths and conditional divorces are prime examples of metaphorical causes because they do not directly obligate expiation or divorce—they only create a semblance of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and lowest degree of sabab
The passage states the lowest degree is that the sabab be a path (tariq) to the ruling. That is, it leads to the ruling but is not the direct cause.
Example: driving an animal that causes damage is a sabab, not the direct cause.
2
Identify the highest degree of sabab
The highest degree is when the sabab, while being a path, resembles the illa (effective cause) or contains the meaning of the illa.
Example: a conditional divorce resembles a cause in that it eventually brings about the divorce when the condition occurs.
3
Apply to oaths by Allah
An oath by Allah is called a metaphorical cause for expiation because the oath is made for fulfilling (al-birr), not for expiation. The expiation only becomes due upon violation.
So the oath is a path to expiation only potentially.
4
Understand the Hanafi concept of shubha al-haqiqa
Despite being metaphorical, the oath has a semblance of reality because the fulfilling is guaranteed by the penalty. This gives the oath a shadow of obligation.
Similarly, a conditional divorce has a semblance of reality because the condition attaches a shadow of obligation to the current marital bond.
5
Contrast with other positions
The passage notes that al-Shafi'i considers such causes to be in the meaning of the illa (more than metaphorical), while Zufar considers them pure metaphor without any semblance.
The Hanafi school takes the middle position.

Source Text

باب القياس
السبب وحكمه
لما يتلف بها، لكنه فيه معنى العلة. فأما اليمين بالله تعالى فسمّي سببا للكفارة مجازاً، وكذلك تعليق الطلاق والعتاق بالشرط؛ لأن أدنى درجات السبب أن يكون طريقاً واليمين تعقد للبر، وذلك قط لا يكون طريقاً للكفارة ولا للجزاء، لكنه يحتمل أن البر في اليمين بالله يؤول إليه فسمّي سببا مجازاً، وهذا عندنا والشافعي به جعله سبباً هو في معنى العلة، وعندنا لهذا المجاز شبهة الحقيقة
بها : أي بالدابة بوطيها في حالة السوق والقود لكنه أي كل واحد من السوق والقود ليس سببا حقيقياً. معنى العلة لأنه قد تخللت العلة بين القود والسوق والتلف، وهو فعل الدابة لكنه مضاف إلى القود والسوق؛ لأن الدابة في فعلها مجبور، بالخصوص إذا كانت لها سائق أو قائد فالعلة لا تصلح لأن يضاف إليها الحكم، فلابد أن يضاف إلى علة العلة وهو السبب هذا فيما يرجع إلى بدل المحل وهو ضمان الدية والقيمة، وأما فيما يرجع إلى جزاء المباشرة فلايكون الحكم مضافاً إلى علة العلة فلا يحرم عن الميراث ولا يجب عليه القصاص ولا الكفارة اليمين بالله تعالى بأن يقول: والله لأفعلن كذا. وكذلك: أي مثل اليمين بالله تعالى اليمين بغير الله تعالى وهي تعليق الطلاق والعتاق بالشرط. بالشرط: بأن يقول: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق، أو أنت حرّ، يسمّى سببا مجازا للجزاء، لا أنهما سببان حقيقان للكفارة والجزاء. طريقاً: إلى الحكم، وأعلى الدرجات أن يكون السبب مع كونه طريقاً شبيهاً بالعلة أو يكون فيه معنى العلة. واليمين سواء كانت بالله أو بغير الله ولا للجزاء في اليمين بغير الله؛ لأنه مانع من الحنث، وبدونه لا تجب الكفارة ولا ينزل الجزاء. . لكنه أي ،اليمين وتذكير الضمير على تأويل الحلف يؤول إليه إلخ أي أن يفضي إلى الحكم عند زوال المانع. سبباً مجازا باعتبار مايؤول إليه كتسمية العنب حمراً، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنِّي أَرَانِي أَعْصِرُ حَمْرا (يوسف: ٣٦)، والحاصل أن تعليق الطلاق والعتاق بالشرط قبل وقوع المعلّق عليه يسمّى سببا مجازا، والعلاقة أنه يؤول إلى السببية بأن يصير طريقا للوصول إلى الحكم عند وقوع المعلّق عليه، وليس بسبب حقيقي؛ إذ ربما لا يفضي إلى الحكم الذي هو الجزاء المرتب عليه بأن لا يقع المعلّق عليه، والسبب الحقيقي يفضي إلى الحكم، وكذا اليمين بالله. ثم إذا وجد المعلّق عليه يصير تلك الإيقاعات على حقيقة بخلاف اليمين بالله تعالى، ولهذا أفرد المصنف محليه اليمين بالله عن تعليق العناق والطلاق بالشرط. جعله أي اليمين بالله تعالى والتعليق سببا هو في معنى العلة؛ فإنه إذا وجد الحنث فالموجب للكفارة ليس إلا اليمين، وكذا إذا وجد المعلّق عليه فالموجب للجزاء ليس إلا التعليق، وهذا معنى العلة، ولكن لما كان الشرط مانعاً عن انعقاد العلة ولهذا يتأخر الحكم إلى وجود الحنث والمعلّق عليه قلنا: إنه سبب فيه معنى العلة، ونحن لا نجعله سبباً حقيقياً فضلا أن يكون فيه معنى العلة، بل عندنا مجاز محض يشبه الحقيقة وإليه أشار بقوله: وعندنا إلخ. حكماً: أي باعتبار كونه علة حقيقة من حيث الحكم كذا قيل ، والأوجه أن يقال: يشبه الحقيقة باعتبار أن اليمين سواء كانت بالله أو بغير الله إنما شرطت للبر، وإذا يفوت البر يلزم الكفارة أو الجزاء، فصار البر مضموناً بالجزاء، فصار لمضو من البر وهو الكفارة أو الجزاء شبهة الثبوت في الحال أي قبل فوات البر، فحصل لليمين شبهة الحقيقة، فكان اليمين هي سبب حقيقي للجزاء والكفارة، فافهم. خلافا لزفر محله : لأن عنده مجاز محض خال عن شبهة الحقيقة، فمذهبنا بين الإفراط الذي ذهب إليه الشافعي محله وبين التفريط الذي قال به زفر يبطل التعليق والتنجيز تفعيل من قولهم: ناجز يناجز أي نقذ ينفّذ، وأصله التعجيل، وصورته ما إذا قال لامرأته: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثلاثاً، ثم طلقها ثلاثا منجزةً أي غير بالشرط، فتزوجت بزوج آخر ودخل بها وطلقها ثم نكحت بالزوج الأول ثم دخلت الدار فعندنا يبطله. يبطله: أي التنجيز يبطل التعليق السابق عندنا، فبدخول الدار لم تطلق عندنا لفوات التعليق بالتنجيز، وتطلق عند زفر؛ لأن عنده قوله: "أنت طالق" وقت التعليق مجاز محض ليس له شبهة الحقيقة، بناء على أصله، فلا يطلب محلاً موجوداً يقوم به. نعم لا بدّ من المحل عند نزول التعليق بوجود الشرط حتى يقع الطلاق في ملكه، فإذا زال المحل بتنجيز الثلاث لم يبطل التعليق، فإذا نكحت بالزوج الأول ووجد المحل ثم دخلت الدار يقع الطلاق الشرط، ودليلنا ما بينه المصنف الله بقوله: لأن اليمين إلخ للبر : أي لتحقق المحلوف عليه من الفعل أو الترك، فإنه قبل الحلف كان مساوي الطرفين، فإذا حلف ترجّح أحد الجانبين وتأكد تحققه باليمين. مضموناً بالجزاء: بمعنى أنه لوفات البر لزم الجزاء في اليمين بغير الله تعالى كما يلزم الكفارة في اليمين بالله عزوجل تحقيقاً لما هو المقصود من اليمين من الحل والمنع مضمونا بالجزاء كان للجزاء شبهة الثبوت في الحال أي قبل قوات البر؛ إذ للضمان شبهة الثبوت قبل فوات المضمون. صار لما ضمن به إلخ والباء في قوله: "به" صلة الضمان والضمير يرجع إلى الموصول، و"البر" فاعل ضمن واللام في "للحال" بمعنى في، والوجوب بمعنى الثبوت، = كذا قيل: القائل صاحب غاية التحقيق. بوجود
Chapter of Qiyas. The cause and its ruling. For what is destroyed by it, but it contains the meaning of the cause. As for the oath by Allah the Exalted, it is called a cause for expiation metaphorically, and likewise the suspension of divorce and manumission by a condition; because the lowest degree of the cause is that it be a path, and the oath is contracted for fulfilling the oath, and that is never a path to expiation nor to penalty, but it is possible that the fulfilling of the oath in the oath by Allah leads to it, so it is called a cause metaphorically. This is according to us, and al-Shafi'i made it a cause that is in the meaning of the cause, while according to us this metaphor has a semblance of reality. ... It means: by the animal, by treading on it in the state of driving and leading, but each of driving and leading is not a real cause. The meaning of the cause is that the cause has intervened between leading/driving and destruction, and it is the action of the animal, but it is attributed to leading/driving; because the animal is compelled in its action, especially if it has a driver or leader. So the cause (illa) is not suitable for the ruling to be attributed to it, so it must be attributed to the cause of the cause, which is the sabab. This is regarding the compensation of the object, which is the guarantee of blood money and value. As for regarding the penalty of direct action, the ruling is not attributed to the cause of the cause, so he is not deprived of inheritance nor is retaliation nor expiation obligatory upon him. The oath by Allah the Exalted, such as saying: 'By Allah, I will do such and such.' Likewise: meaning like the oath by Allah the Exalted, the oath by other than Allah the Exalted, and that is the suspension of divorce and manumission by a condition. By a condition: such as saying: 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced,' or 'you are free.' It is called a metaphorical cause for the penalty, not that they are real causes for expiation and penalty. A path: to the ruling, and the highest degree is that the cause, while being a path, resembles the illa or contains the meaning of the illa. And the oath, whether by Allah or other than Allah, and there is no penalty in the oath by other than Allah because it prevents from the violation, and without it expiation is not obligatory nor does the penalty descend. But it (the oath) leads to it etc., meaning that it leads to the ruling when the preventer is removed. A metaphorical cause in consideration of what it leads to, like calling grapes 'wine' as in the verse of Allah: 'Indeed, I see myself pressing wine' (Quran 12:36). The conclusion is that the suspension of divorce and manumission by a condition before the occurrence of the suspended matter is called a metaphorical cause, and the relationship is that it leads to causality by becoming a path to reaching the ruling when the suspended matter occurs, and it is not a real cause, since perhaps it does not lead to the ruling which is the penalty linked to it, by the non-occurrence of the suspended matter. The real cause leads to the ruling, and likewise the oath by Allah. Then when the suspended matter occurs, those dispositions become real, unlike the oath by Allah the Exalted. For this reason, the author separated the subject of the oath by Allah from the suspension of manumission and divorce by a condition. He made it, i.e., the oath by Allah the Exalted and the suspension, a cause that is in the meaning of the illa; for if the violation occurs, the obligator of expiation is nothing but the oath, and likewise if the suspended matter occurs, the obligator of the penalty is nothing but the suspension. That is the meaning of the illa, but because the condition is a preventer from the actualization of the illa, and for this reason the ruling is delayed until the occurrence of the violation and the suspended matter, we said: It is a cause containing the meaning of the illa, but we do not make it a real cause, let alone that it contains the meaning of the illa. Rather, according to us, it is a pure metaphor that resembles reality, and to that the author pointed with his saying: 'and according to us' etc. Legally: meaning in consideration of it being a real illa from a legal perspective. It has been said, and the more appropriate is to say: It resembles reality because the oath, whether by Allah or other than Allah, is only stipulated for the fulfilling of the oath, and if the fulfilling is lost, expiation or penalty becomes obligatory. So the fulfilling becomes guaranteed by the penalty, so the substitute for the fulfilling, which is expiation or penalty, acquires a semblance of confirmation at the present time, i.e., before the loss of the fulfilling. Thus the oath acquires a semblance of reality, so the oath becomes a real cause for the penalty and expiation, so understand. Contrary to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, because according to him it is a pure metaphor devoid of semblance of reality. So our school is between the excess which al-Shafi'i went to and the deficiency which Zufar said. Tanziz nullifies the suspension. Tanziz is a verbal noun from 'najaza yunajizu', meaning 'to execute', originally meaning 'hastening'. Its example is when a man says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' then he divorces her thrice unconditionally, i.e., not by a condition. Then she marries another husband, he consummates with her and divorces her, then she marries the first husband, then enters the house. According to us, it nullifies it. It nullifies it: meaning tanziz nullifies the prior suspension according to us. So upon entering the house, she is not divorced according to us because the suspension is lost by the tanziz. And she is divorced according to Zufar because, according to him, his statement 'you are divorced' at the time of suspension is a pure metaphor without semblance of reality, based on his principle. So it does not require an existing locus to stand in. Rather, a locus is needed when the suspension descends with the occurrence of the condition so that divorce occurs in his ownership. So if the locus is removed by the unconditional triple divorce, the suspension is not nullified. So if she marries the first husband and the locus is found, then she enters the house, the conditional divorce occurs. Our proof is what the author explained with his saying: 'Because the oath is for fulfilling', etc.: meaning for the realization of the sworn matter of action or omission. For before the oath, both sides were equal. When he swears, one side becomes preponderant and its realization is emphasized by the oath. 'Guaranteed by the penalty': meaning that if the fulfilling is lost, the penalty becomes obligatory in the oath by other than Allah, just as expiation becomes obligatory in the oath by Allah Almighty, to realize the purpose of the oath—binding and prohibiting. When it is guaranteed by the penalty, the penalty acquires a semblance of confirmation at the present time, i.e., before the loss of the fulfilling; for a guarantee has a semblance of confirmation before the loss of the guaranteed. 'It became what is guaranteed by it' etc. The letter ba in 'bi-hi' is the particle of the guarantee, and the pronoun refers to the relative, and 'al-birr' is the subject of 'dumina', and the lam in 'li'l-hal' is in the meaning of 'fi', and 'al-wujub' means confirmation. Thus it has been said: the speaker is the author of Ghayat al-Tahqiq. With the existence.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Qiyas and deals with the definition and degrees of sabab (cause) in Hanafi legal theory. The author distinguishes between a real cause (sabab haqiqi) which inevitably leads to its effect, and a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) which only potentially leads to the ruling when a condition is fulfilled. The lowest degree of a cause is that it be a path (tariq) to the ruling. The highest degree is when the cause also resembles the illa (effective cause) or contains the meaning of the illa. The discussion focuses on two types of sabab: oaths (yamīn) and conditional dispositions (ta'līq) such as suspensive divorce and manumission. According to the Hanafi school, an oath by Allah is called a cause for expiation metaphorically because the oath itself does not directly cause expiation; rather, if one breaks the oath, expiation becomes due. Similarly, a conditional divorce (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced') is called a metaphorical cause for the penalty (the divorce) because the divorce only occurs upon entry. The real cause of the penalty is the violation or the fulfillment of the condition. However, one school (Imam al-Shafi'i) considers these as causes in the meaning of the illa, making them more than just metaphorical. The Hanafi position is that they are pure metaphor but with a semblance of reality (shubha al-haqiqa), because the oath is made to ensure compliance, and if compliance fails, the penalty attaches. This semblance gives the metaphorical cause a legal effect. Imam Zufar considered them pure metaphor without any semblance, leading to a different ruling in the case of tanziz (unconditional execution). The passage then explains the tanziz issue: If a man says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' then later divorces her thrice unconditionally (tanziz), she remarries and is divorced, then remarries the first husband and enters the house. According to the Hanafis, the unconditional divorce nullifies the prior conditional divorce, so she is not divorced upon entry. According to Zufar, the conditional divorce remains in effect, so she is divorced upon entry because, in his view, the conditional divorce is pure metaphor and does not require a subsisting marital bond at the time of the condition—it simply awaits a marital bond at the occurrence of the condition. The Hanafi proof is that the oath (and the conditional) creates a semblance of obligation in the present, so when the conditional divorce is issued, it attaches to the current marital relationship; if that relationship is later removed by an unconditional divorce, the conditional divorce is nullified.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause: a legal descriptor that serves as a path (tariq) to a ruling, but is not the direct effective cause (illa). It may be real or metaphorical.
تعليق (ta'līq): Suspensive disposition: a legal statement (e.g., divorce, manumission) that is conditional on a future event.
تنجيز (tanzīz): Unconditional execution: a legal disposition that is immediate and unconditional, such as an unconditional divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the lowest degree of sabab (cause)?
A) That it be the direct effective cause (illa).
B) That it be a path (tariq) to the ruling.
C) That it contain the meaning of the illa.
D) That it be a real cause (haqiqi).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, sabab is a path to a ruling; metaphorical causes like oaths and conditional divorces have a semblance of reality that gives them legal effect, but they are not real causes.

The Dispute Over Tanziz and the Legal Nature of Ta'līq
Dispute over tanziz nullifying ta'līq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tanziz nullifying prior ta'līq, explain the positions of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, and identify the key differences in their usul principles.

Core Idea
A prior conditional divorce is nullified by an unconditional divorce because the conditional had a shadow of obligation attached to the current marriage.

This passage continues the discussion of sabab, focusing on a practical dispute: if a man makes a conditional divorce, then later issues an unconditional divorce, which one prevails? The Hanafi school, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i give different answers based on their understanding of the nature of ta'līq (suspension). The passage uses this dispute to illustrate the thamarah al-khilaf of their usul positions.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A man says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced.' Then he divorces her thrice unconditionally. She remarries, is divorced, remarries the first husband, and then enters the house.
The question: does the conditional divorce take effect upon entry?
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the unconditional divorce nullifies the conditional one, so upon entry, no divorce occurs.
The reason: the conditional divorce had a semblance of reality (shubha haqiqa) attached to the current marital bond.
3
Identify Zufar's ruling
According to Zufar, the unconditional divorce does not nullify the conditional; if she later enters the house, the conditional divorce takes effect.
Zufar considers the conditional divorce as pure metaphor without any attachment to the current marriage.
4
Trace the usul basis
The Hanafi position is based on the concept of shubha al-haqiqa: the ta'līq has a shadow of obligation, so it attaches to the marriage as it exists at the time of the condition. Zufar's position is based on considering ta'līq as pure metaphor, so it does not attach until the condition occurs.
Al-Shafi'i, who considers ta'līq as a cause in the meaning of the illa, would likely agree with the Hanafi ruling but for a different reason (the ta'līq is more than a metaphor).
5
Identify the proof
The Hanafi proof: because the oath (and ta'līq) is for fulfilling, and the fulfilling becomes guaranteed by the penalty, the penalty acquires a semblance of confirmation at the present time. Hence, the ta'līq attaches to the current marriage.
This is the argument from the passage: 'It became what is guaranteed by it... so the penalty has a semblance of confirmation at the present time.'

السبب وحكمه
لما يتلف بها، لكنه فيه معنى العلة. فأما اليمين بالله تعالى فسمّي سببا للكفارة مجازاً، وكذلك تعليق الطلاق والعتاق بالشرط؛ لأن أدنى درجات السبب أن يكون طريقاً واليمين تعقد للبر، وذلك قط لا يكون طريقاً للكفارة ولا للجزاء، لكنه يحتمل أن البر في اليمين بالله يؤول إليه فسمّي سببا مجازاً، وهذا عندنا والشافعي به جعله سبباً هو في معنى العلة، وعندنا لهذا المجاز شبهة الحقيقة
بها : أي بالدابة بوطيها في حالة السوق والقود لكنه أي كل واحد من السوق والقود ليس سببا حقيقياً. معنى العلة لأنه قد تخللت العلة بين القود والسوق والتلف، وهو فعل الدابة لكنه مضاف إلى القود والسوق؛ لأن الدابة في فعلها مجبور، بالخصوص إذا كانت لها سائق أو قائد فالعلة لا تصلح لأن يضاف إليها الحكم، فلابد أن يضاف إلى علة العلة وهو السبب هذا فيما يرجع إلى بدل المحل وهو ضمان الدية والقيمة، وأما فيما يرجع الله تعالى وهي تعليق الطلاق والعتاق بالشرط. بالشرط: بأن يقول: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق، أو أنت حرّ، يسمّى سببا مجازا للجزاء، لا أنهما سببان حقيقان للكفارة والجزاء. طريقاً: إلى الحكم، وأعلى الدرجات أن يكون السبب مع كونه طريقاً شبيهاً بالعلة أو يكون فيه معنى العلة. واليمين سواء كانت بالله أو بغير الله ولا للجزاء في اليمين بغير الله؛ لأنه مانع من الحنث، وبدونه لا تجب الكفارة ولا ينزل الجزاء. . لكنه أي ،اليمين وتذكير الضمير على تأويل الحلف يؤول إليه إلخ أي أن يفضي إلى الحكم عند زوال المانع. سبباً مجازا باعتبار مايؤول إليه كتسمية العنب حمراً، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنِّي أَرَانِي أَعْصِرُ حَمْرا (يوسف: ٣٦)، والحاصل أن تعليق الطلاق والعتاق بالشرط قبل وقوع المعلّق عليه يسمّى سببا مجازا، والعلاقة أنه يؤول إلى السببية بأن يصير طريقا للوصول إلى الحكم عند وقوع المعلّق عليه، وليس بسبب حقيقي؛ إذ ربما لا يفضي إلى الحكم الذي هو الجزاء المرتب عليه بأن لا يقع المعلّق عليه، والسبب الحقيقي يفضي إلى الحكم، وكذا اليمين بالله. ثم إذا وجد المعلّق عليه يصير تلك الإيقاعات على حقيقة بخلاف اليمين بالله تعالى، ولهذا أفرد المصنف محليه اليمين بالله عن تعليق العناق والطلاق بالشرط. جعله أي اليمين بالله تعالى والتعليق سببا هو في معنى العلة؛ فإنه إذا وجد الحنث فالموجب للكفارة ليس إلا اليمين، وكذا إذا وجد المعلّق عليه فالموجب للجزاء ليس إلا التعليق، وهذا معنى العلة، ولكن لما كان الشرط مانعاً عن انعقاد العلة ولهذا يتأخر الحكم إلى وجود الحنث والمعلّق عليه قلنا: إنه سبب فيه معنى العلة، ونحن لا نجعله سبباً حقيقياً فضلا أن يكون فيه معنى العلة، بل عندنا مجاز محض يشبه الحقيقة وإليه أشار بقوله: وعندنا إلخ. حكماً: أي باعتبار كونه علة حقيقة من حيث الحكم كذا قيل ، والأوجه أن يقال: يشبه الحقيقة باعتبار أن اليمين سواء التعليق والتنجيز تفعيل من قولهم: ناجز يناجز أي نقذ ينفّذ، وأصله التعجيل، وصورته ما إذا قال لامرأته: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثلاثاً، ثم طلقها ثلاثا منجزةً أي غير بالشرط، فتزوجت بزوج آخر ودخل بها وطلقها Chapter of Qiyas. The cause and its ruling. For what is destroyed by it, but it contains the meaning of the cause. As for the oath by Allah the Exalted, it is called a cause for expiation metaphorically, and likewise the suspension of divorce and manumission by a condition; because the lowest degree of the cause is that it be a path, and the oath is contracted for fulfilling the oath, and that is never a path to expiation nor to penalty, but it is possible that the fulfilling of the oath in the oath by Allah leads to it, so it is called a cause metaphorically. This is according to us, and al-Shafi'i made it a cause that is in the meaning of the cause, while according to us this metaphor has a semblance of reality. ... It means: by the animal, by treading on it in the state of driving and leading, but each of driving and leading is not a real cause. The meaning of the cause is that the cause has intervened between leading/driving and destruction, and it is the action of the animal, but it is attributed to leading/driving; because the animal is compelled in its action, especially if it has a driver or leader. So the cause (illa) is not suitable for the ruling to be attributed to it, so it must be attributed to the cause of the cause, which is the sabab. This is regarding the compensation of the object, which is the guarantee of blood money and value. As for regarding the penalty of direct action, the ruling is not attributed to the cause of the cause, so he is not deprived of inheritance nor is retaliation nor expiation obligatory upon him. The oath by Allah the Exalted, such as saying: 'By Allah, I will do such and such.' Likewise: meaning like the oath by Allah the Exalted, the oath by other than Allah the Exalted, and that is the suspension of divorce and manumission by a condition. By a condition: such as saying: 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced,' or 'you are free.' It is called a metaphorical cause for the penalty, not that they are real causes for expiation and penalty. A path: to the ruling, and the highest degree is that the cause, while being a path, resembles the illa or contains the meaning of the illa. And the oath, whether by Allah or other than Allah, and there is no penalty in the oath by other than Allah because it prevents from the violation, and without it expiation is not obligatory nor does the penalty descend. But it (the oath) leads to it etc., meaning that it leads to the ruling when the preventer is removed. A metaphorical cause in consideration of what it leads to, like calling grapes 'wine' as in the verse of Allah: 'Indeed, I see myself pressing wine' (Quran 12:36). The conclusion is that the suspension of divorce and manumission by a condition before the occurrence of the suspended matter is called a metaphorical cause, and the relationship is that it leads to causality by becoming a path to reaching the ruling when the suspended matter occurs, and it is not a real cause, since perhaps it does not lead to the ruling which is the penalty linked to it, by the non-occurrence of the suspended matter. The real cause leads to the ruling, and likewise the oath by Allah. Then when the suspended matter occurs, those dispositions become real, unlike the oath by Allah the Exalted. For this reason, the author separated the subject of the oath by Allah from the suspension of manumission and divorce by a condition. He made it, i.e., the oath by Allah the Exalted and the suspension, a cause that is in the meaning of the illa; for if the violation occurs, the obligator of expiation is nothing but the oath, and likewise if the suspended matter occurs, the obligator of the penalty is nothing but the suspension. That is the meaning of the illa, but because the condition is a preventer from the actualization of the illa, and for this reason the ruling is delayed until the occurrence of the violation and the suspended matter, we said: It is a cause containing the meaning of the illa, but we do not make it a real cause, let alone that it contains the meaning of the illa. Rather, according to us, it is a pure metaphor that resembles reality, and to that the author pointed with his saying: 'and according to us' etc. Legally: meaning in consideration of it being a real illa from a legal perspective. It has been said, and the more appropriate is to say: It resembles reality because the oath, whether by Allah or other than Allah, is only stipulated for the fulfilling of the oath, and if the fulfilling is lost, expiation or penalty becomes obligatory. So the fulfilling becomes guaranteed by the penalty, so the substitute for the fulfilling, which is expiation or penalty, acquires a semblance of confirmation at the present time, i.e., before the loss of the fulfilling. Thus the oath acquires a semblance of reality, so the oath becomes a real cause for the penalty and expiation, so understand. Contrary to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, because according to him it is a pure metaphor devoid of semblance of reality. So our school is between the excess which al-Shafi'i went to and the deficiency which Zufar said. Tanziz nullifies the suspension. Tanziz is a verbal noun from 'najaza yunajizu', meaning 'to execute', originally meaning 'hastening'. Its example is when a man says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' then he divorces her thrice unconditionally, i.e., not by a condition. Then she marries another husband, he consummates with her and divorces her, then she marries the first husband, then enters the house. According to us, it nullifies it. It nullifies it: meaning tanziz nullifies the prior suspension according to us. So upon entering the house, she is not divorced according to us because the suspension is lost by the tanziz. And she is divorced according to Zufar because, according to him, his statement 'you are divorced' at the time of suspension is a pure metaphor without semblance of reality, based on his principle. So it does not require an existing locus to stand in. Rather, a locus is needed when the suspension descends with the occurrence of the condition so that divorce occurs in his ownership. So if the locus is removed by the unconditional triple divorce, the suspension is not nullified. So if she marries the first husband and the locus is found, then she enters the house, the conditional divorce occurs. Our proof is what the author explained with his saying: 'Because the oath is for fulfilling', etc.: meaning for the realization of the sworn matter of action or omission. For before the oath, both sides were equal. When he swears, one side becomes preponderant and its realization is emphasized by the oath. 'Guaranteed by the penalty': meaning that if the fulfilling is lost, the penalty becomes obligatory in the oath by other than Allah, just as expiation becomes obligatory in the oath by Allah Almighty, to realize the purpose of the oath—binding and prohibiting. When it is guaranteed by the penalty, the penalty acquires a semblance of confirmation at the present time, i.e., before the loss of the fulfilling; for a guarantee has a semblance of confirmation before the loss of the guaranteed. 'It became what is guaranteed by it' etc. The letter ba in 'bi-hi' is the particle of the guarantee, and the pronoun refers to the relative, and 'al-birr' is the subject of 'dumina', and the lam in 'li'l-hal' is in the meaning of 'fi', and 'al-wujub' means confirmation. Thus it has been said: the speaker is the author of Ghayat al-Tahqiq. With the existence.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Qiyas and deals with the definition and degrees of sabab (cause) in Hanafi legal theory. The author distinguishes between a real cause (sabab haqiqi) which inevitably leads to its effect, and a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) which only potentially leads to the ruling when a condition is fulfilled. The lowest degree of a cause is that it be a path (tariq) to the ruling. The highest degree is when the cause also resembles the illa (effective cause) or contains the meaning of the illa. The discussion focuses on two types of sabab: oaths (yamīn) and conditional dispositions (ta'līq) such as suspensive divorce and manumission. According to the Hanafi school, an oath by Allah is called a cause for expiation metaphorically because the oath itself does not directly cause expiation; rather, if one breaks the oath, expiation becomes due. Similarly, a conditional divorce (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced') is called a metaphorical cause for the penalty (the divorce) because the divorce only occurs upon entry. The real cause of the penalty is the violation or the fulfillment of the condition. However, one school (Imam al-Shafi'i) considers these as causes in the meaning of the illa, making them more than just metaphorical. The Hanafi position is that they are pure metaphor but with a semblance of reality (shubha al-haqiqa), because the oath is made to ensure compliance, and if compliance fails, the penalty attaches. This semblance gives the metaphorical cause a legal effect. Imam Zufar considered them pure metaphor without any semblance, leading to a different ruling in the case of tanziz (unconditional execution). The passage then explains the tanziz issue: If a man says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' then later divorces her thrice unconditionally (tanziz), she remarries and is divorced, then remarries the first husband and enters the house. According to the Hanafis, the unconditional divorce nullifies the prior conditional divorce, so she is not divorced upon entry. According to Zufar, the conditional divorce remains in effect, so she is divorced upon entry because, in his view, the conditional divorce is pure metaphor and does not require a subsisting marital bond at the time of the condition—it simply awaits a marital bond at the occurrence of the condition. The Hanafi proof is that the oath (and the conditional) creates a semblance of obligation in the present, so when the conditional divorce is issued, it attaches to the current marital relationship; if that relationship is later removed by an unconditional divorce, the conditional divorce is nullified.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause: a legal descriptor that serves as a path (tariq) to a ruling, but is not the direct effective cause (illa). It may be real or metaphorical.
تعليق (ta'līq): Suspensive disposition: a legal statement (e.g., divorce, manumission) that is conditional on a future event.
تنجيز (tanzīz): Unconditional execution: a legal disposition that is immediate and unconditional, such as an unconditional divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' and then unconditionally divorces her, and later she remarries him and enters the house, what is the ruling?
A) She is divorced because the condition occurred after the unconditional divorce was already executed.
B) She is not divorced because the unconditional divorce nullified the conditional one.
C) She is divorced three times because the conditional divorce was triggered again.
D) It depends on the intention of the husband.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that unconditional divorce nullifies a prior conditional divorce because the conditional had a semblance of reality attached to the current marriage.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition and Types of Shart in Hanafi Usul
Defining shart and its four types in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shart (condition) in Hanafi usul, distinguish it from sabab and 'alama, and classify conditions into four types using the attribution criterion.

Core Idea
A condition is that upon which a ruling's existence depends, not its obligation.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the term shart (condition) is a foundational concept that governs how rulings are contingent on prerequisites. This lesson unpacks its precise definition, how it differs from cause and sign, and the fourfold classification developed by the verifiers (muhaqqiqun). Understanding this taxonomy is essential for correctly deriving rulings and identifying when a condition is truly legally effective.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition
Locate the exact phrase defining shart: 'to which the ruling is attributed in terms of existence with it, not obligation by it.' Write it down.
The key is 'wujudan 'indahu la wujuban bihi' — existence depends on it, not obligation.
2
Distinguish from sabab and 'alama
The passage says the definition excludes sabab (cause) and 'alama (sign) because the ruling is not attributed to them in the same way. Clarify: a cause directly necessitates obligation, while a condition only enables existence.
For example, the sun's decline (zawal) is a sabab for Zuhr prayer's obligation; wudu is a shart for its validity.
3
Identify the four types of shart
The verifiers list: (1) pure condition, (2) condition containing the meaning of cause, (3) condition containing the meaning of consequence, (4) metaphorical condition. Read the description of each.
Memorize the Arabic terms: شرط محض, شرط فيه معنى العلة, شرط فيه معنى التبعية, شرط مجاز.
4
Apply the classification criterion
The passage provides a test: if the ruling's existence is not attributed to the condition, it is the fourth type (metaphorical). If a free act of the agent intervenes without connection, it is the third. Study how this works.
This criterion helps place any given condition into the correct category.
5
Illustrate with a Hanafi fiqh example
Use the condition of wudu for prayer: wudu is a shart mahd (pure condition) because prayer's validity depends on it, but prayer's obligation depends on time (sabab). The existence of prayer is attributed to wudu? Actually, wudu is a condition; the ruling (obligation) is not attributed to wudu.
This example shows how the definition applies practically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يضاف إليه الحكم احترز عن السبب والعلامة؛ لأن الحكم لا يضاف إليهما. وجوداً عنده إلخ: أي يتوقف وجود الشيء عليه بأن يوجد عند وجوده لا وجوبه واعلم أن الشرط على ماذكره المحققون على أربعة أقسام. الأول شرط محض، والثاني شرط فيه معنى العلة، والثالث شرط فيه معنى التبعية والرابع شرط مجازاً أي اسماً ومعنى لا حكماً، كأول الشرطين علق بمجموعهما الحكم. ووجه الضبط أن وجود الحكم إن لم يكن مضافاً إليه فهو الرابع، وإن كان تخلّل بينه وبين الحكم فعل فاعل مختار غير منسوب إليه وكان غير متصل به فهو الثالث، =
To which the ruling is attributed, distinguishing from cause and sign, because the ruling is not attributed to them. 'Existence with it' etc.: i.e., the existence of the thing depends on it, such that it exists at its existence, not its obligation. Know that condition according to the verifiers is of four types: First, pure condition. Second, a condition containing the meaning of cause. Third, a condition containing the meaning of consequence. Fourth, a condition metaphorically, i.e., nominally and in meaning not legally, like the first of two conditions upon whose combination the ruling is hung. And the way of classification is that if the existence of the ruling is not attributed to it, it is the fourth. If an act of a free agent not attributed to it intervenes between it and the ruling and is not connected to it, it is the third, =
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of shart (condition) in usul al-fiqh. The condition is that upon which the existence of a ruling depends (wujud 'indahu), not its obligation (wujub bihi). This distinguishes it from a cause (sabab) and a sign ('alama), because the ruling is attributed to those only in a certain sense. The verifiers (muhaqqiqun) categorize conditions into four types: (1) pure condition where the condition is solely a prerequisite; (2) condition with the meaning of cause, where the condition has some causal aspect; (3) condition with the meaning of consequence, where the condition is consequent; and (4) metaphorical condition, where the condition is called so only nominally and in meaning but not legally, such as when a ruling is tied to a combination of two conditions. The passage gives a criterion: if the ruling's existence is not attributed to the condition, it is the fourth type; if there is an intervening free act of the mukallaf that is not attributed to the condition and not connected, it is the third type.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): That upon which the existence of a ruling depends, but not its obligation.
الشرط المحض (al-shart al-mahd): A pure condition with no causal or consequential meaning.
الشرط المجاز (al-shart al-majaz): Metaphorical condition, where the condition is called so nominally and in meaning but not legally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the sharia definition of shart (condition)?
A) That upon which the obligation of a ruling depends.
B) That upon which the existence of a ruling depends, not its obligation.
C) That which necessitates a ruling by itself.
D) The same as a cause (sabab).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a shart (condition) is a prerequisite for a ruling's existence, not its obligation, and it is classified into four types based on attribution and connection.

Definition and Types of Legal Capacity (Ahliyyah)
Definition and classification of legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define legal capacity (ahliyyah), distinguish between its two types (ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada'), and explain their respective roles in Hanafi legal theory.

Core Idea
Legal capacity is the trust that makes humans alone subject to divine obligations.

Legal capacity (ahliyyah) is a foundational concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, determining who can bear rights and duties and who can perform legally effective acts. In this lesson, we explore the classical definition of ahliyyah, its two types, and the Quranic basis for human exclusivity. Understanding this distinction is essential for analyzing legal personality (dhimmah) and the conditions for valid transactions, worship, and criminal liability.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Read the Arabic definition of ahliyyah: 'كون الإنسان بحيث يصلح أن يكون محط نزول الأحكام الشرعية' – suitability of a human to be the locus of divine rulings. Note that it is a quality inherent to humans.
The definition uses 'صلاحية' (suitability), indicating it is a potential, not actual capacity.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 33:72: 'وَحَمَلَهَا الْإِنْسَانُ' (and he carried it). The 'trust' (أمانة) is interpreted as legal capacity. Only humans accepted this trust, excluding animals.
The word 'الإنسان' refers to the human species collectively.
3
Distinguish the two types
The passage divides capacity into: (1) أهلية الوجوب – capacity of obligation: the ability to have rights and duties in one's dhimmah, present from birth. (2) أهلية الأداء – capacity of performance: the ability to perform acts that produce legal effects, achieved with tamyiz and bulugh.
Ahliyyat al-wujub is passive (being assigned obligations); ahliyyat al-ada' is active (performing acts).
4
Apply the legal definition
Use the legal definition dissector: term = الأهلية, mahall (locus) = human, sabab (cause) = human nature, shart (condition for performance) = intellect, mani (preventer) = insanity/minority, athar (effect) = entitlement to rights and obligation.
This structure helps in analyzing other legal concepts.
5
Relate to dhimmah
Ahliyyat al-wujub is tied to dhimmah (legal personality). Every human has a dhimmah from birth, making them capable of owning property and incurring minimal obligations (e.g., zakat on behalf). Performance capacity requires additional conditions.
This distinction explains why a child can inherit but cannot sell property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان الأهلية الكلام في هذا ينقسم على قسمين الأهلية، والأمور المعترضة عليها. أي في بيان الأهلية [أنواع الأهلية] القسم الأول والثاني فصل في بيان الأهلية الأهلية نوعان: أهلية الوجوب وأهلية الأداء. الأهلية: وهي عبارة عن كون الإنسان أو الشخص بحيث يصلح أن يكون محط نزول الأحكام الشرعية أو التكليف، وقيل: هي عبارة عن صلاحية الإنسان لوجوب الحقوق المشروعة له، وعليه، وهذه الصلاحية أمانة حملها الإنسان، كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَحَمَلَهَا الْإِنْسَانُ ﴾ (الأحزاب: ۷۲)، ولذا خص بالتكليف من سائر الحيوانات التي ليس لها ذمة التكليف، وقد كان ظلوما جهولا وأهلية الأداء: إذا عرفت معنى الأهلية، فاعلم أن الأهلية على نوعين: النوع الأول أهلية نفس الوجوب وهو أن يكون قابلا لشغل الذمة، والنوع الثاني أهلية لوجوب الأداء.
Section on Explanation of Legal Capacity: The discussion on this divides into two parts: capacity and the matters that oppose it. That is, in explaining capacity [types of capacity] the first and second sections. Section on capacity: capacity is of two types: capacity of obligation and capacity of performance. Capacity: It is that the human or person is such that he is suitable to be the locus for the descent of legal rulings or obligation. And it is said: it is the suitability of the human for the obligation of rights prescribed for him and upon him. This suitability is a trust that the human carried, as God said: 'And he carried it' (33:72), and for this reason, he was singled out for obligation over other animals which do not have a capacity for obligation. And he was unjust and ignorant. Capacity of performance: When you know the meaning of capacity, know that capacity is of two types: the first type is the capacity of obligation itself, which is to be capable of occupying the dhimmah (legal personality), and the second type is capacity for the obligation of performance.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a concise definition of legal capacity (أهلية) from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. It begins by stating that the discussion of capacity divides into capacity itself and matters that oppose it. The author then defines capacity as the human's suitability to be the subject of divine legal rulings (أحكام شرعية) and obligations. A secondary definition adds that it is the suitability for the obligation of rights both for and against the person. This suitability is described as a trust (أمانة) that humans alone carry, citing Quran 33:72, which distinguishes humans from animals that lack a legal personality (ذمة). The passage then divides capacity into two types: (1) أهلية الوجوب (capacity of obligation) – the capacity to have rights and obligations established in one's dhimmah, and (2) أهلية الأداء (capacity of performance) – the capacity to perform legal acts effectively. This foundational distinction is central to Hanafi legal theory, determining issues like the validity of transactions and criminal liability.

Key Terms
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujub): Capacity of obligation: the capacity to have rights and duties attributed to one's legal personality (dhimmah), present in every human from birth until death.
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-ada'): Capacity of performance: the capacity to perform legally effective acts, which is attained with mental maturity (bulugh and rushd).
الذمة (al-dhimmah): Legal personality; the vessel for rights and obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada' according to Hanafi usul?
A) Ahliyyat al-wujub is for performance, ahliyyat al-ada' is for obligations.
B) Ahliyyat al-wujub is for obligations, ahliyyat al-ada' is for performance.
C) Both refer to the same capacity.
D) Ahliyyat al-wujub is for rituals, ahliyyat al-ada' is for transactions.

Key Takeaway
Legal capacity (ahliyyah) is a trust exclusive to humans, comprising the capacity to bear rights and duties (wujub) and the capacity to perform legal acts (ada').

Legal Capacity (Ahliyyah) – Definition and Core Concepts
Defining ahliyyah and introducing dhimma and gharad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahliyyah, distinguish between complete and incomplete dhimma, and apply the principle that obligation can be nullified by loss of purpose (gharad).

Core Idea
Legal capacity depends on a qualified dhimma; obligation is nullified when its purpose cannot be achieved.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi concept of legal capacity (ahliyyah). The passage defines ahliyyah in relation to the dhimma (legal personality) and introduces the crucial principle that obligations can become void if their intended purpose is unattainable. This foundational concept governs rulings on the fetus, the child, and the disbeliever.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and scope of ahliyyah
From the text, note that ahliyyah is the capacity to acquire obligations and rights. It is linked to having a dhimma. The text mentions that the fetus has a partial dhimma and the separated child a complete dhimma.
2
Understand the role of dhimma in obligations
Distinguish between complete dhimma (for the separated child/adult) and incomplete dhimma (for the fetus). A complete dhimma is the basis for full legal capacity.
3
Grasp the principle of nullification by loss of purpose (gharad)
The text states that an obligation can be nullified either by loss of its place (mahall) or by loss of its purpose (gharad). The example given is selling a free person (no place) vs. obligation on a child who cannot perform by choice (no purpose).
4
Apply the principle to the fetus example
The fetus has a partial dhimma, so rights like inheritance are established, but obligations are not imposed. After separation, a complete dhimma appears, making the child eligible for obligations, but the purpose of performance may still be lacking.
This sets the stage for the detailed rulings on child and disbeliever in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
فصل في بيان الأهلية
وإذا انفصل وظهرت له ذمة مطلقة كان أهلا للوجوب له وعليه، غير أن الوجوب عن الأم بسبب الولادة كما مر محله غير مقصود بنفسه، فجاز أن يبطل لعدم حكمه وغرضه، كما ينعدم لعدم محله ولهذا لم يجب على الكافر شيء من الشرائع التي هي الطاعات؛ لما لم يكن أهلاً لثواب الآخرة، ولزمه الإيمان؛ لما كان أهلا لأدائه حکمه، ووجوب
ولما لم يكن له ذمة كاملة كما مرّ، فلا يجب عليه شيء من الحقوق حتى لو اشترى له الولي شيئاً لا يجب عليه الثمن وإليه أشار بقوله: ولم يجب إلخ. كان أهلا إلخ والحاصل أن الجنين إذا لم ينفصل فله ذمة من وجه، حيث يثبت له الحقوق من الإرث والعتق ولا يجب عليه حق غيره، وإذا انفصل فله ذمة كاملة فيثبت له وعليه، ولما كان يرد عليه من أنه إذا حصل له ذمة كاملة فينبغي أن يكون حكمه كحكم البالغين، فيجب عليه ما كان عقوبة وجزاء أيضا، كما ذهب إليه بعض مشايخنا مثل قاضي الإمام أبي زيد وغيره، فدفعه بقوله: غير أن إلخ. غير مقصود بنفسه إلخ: يعني إنما المقصود والغرض الأصلي من نفس الوجوب حكمه وهو الأداء من اختيار، والصبي لا يتصوّر منه الأداء بالاختيار لعجزه، فيبطل الوجوب في الأفعال التي لا بد من أدائه باختيار؛ لفوات الغرض، والشيء كما يبطل بفوت المحل كبيع الحر وإعتاق البهيمة يبطل بفوت الغرض أيضا، فلا يلزم على الصبي ما لا يمكن أداؤه بالاختيار فلا يكون حكمه كحكم البالغين فلا يجب عليه ما يجب عليهم. وتفصيل المقام ما كان حقوق العباد من الغرم وضمان المتلفات والعوض كثمن المبيع ونفقة الزوجات والأقارب يلزم على الصبي، لأن الأداء بالاختيار في تلك الأمور ليس بضروري، ويكون أداء وليه كأدائه، وكأن الوجوب غير وما كان عقوبة وجزاء لم يجب عليه؛ لأن المقصود من العقوبات المؤاخذة بالفعل، وهو لايصلح لذلك، فالوجوب ههنا خال عن حكمه فيبطل والولي في ما يجب عليه العقوبة والجزاء لا يصلح أن يقوم مقامه، وكذا حقوق الله الخالصة كالصلاة والصوم لا يجب عليه أيضا؛ لأن الأداء بالاختيار أي بالنية ضروري فيها، والولي لا يصلح أن يكون أداؤه قائماً مقام أدائه فيبطل الوجوب بفوت الغرض، وسيأتي التفصيل فوق هذا. ولما فرغ عن خال عن الجواب شرع في تفريعات على قوله : فجاز أن يبطل لعدم حكمه وغرضه كما يبطل لعدم محله، فقال: ولهذا إلخ. أهلا لثواب الآخرة: يعني أن الغرض من الشرائع التي هي الطاعات كالصوم والصلاة والزكاة ثواب الآخرة، والكافر ليس أهلا لثواب الآخرة، فوجوب تلك الشرائع على الكافر خال عن الغرض فيبطل، فلا تجب عليه تلك الشرائع، واحترز بقوله : "التي هي الطاعات" عن الشرائع التي ليست بطاعات وليس الغرض منها ثواب الآخرة كالجزية والخراج، فإنها واجبة عليه، ولما كان يتوهم من عدم كونه أهلا للثواب أن لا يجب عليه الإيمان أيضاً دفعه بقوله: ولزمه إلخ. ولزمه الإيمان إلخ : يعني في وجوب الإيمان على الكافر لا يفوت الغرض من الإيمان ثواب الآخرة والكافر أهل للإيمان فإذا آمن يحصل له ثواب الآخرة، فلا يفوت الغرض، فيجب عليه الإيمان. ثم شرع في تفريع آخر وقال: ولم يجب إلخ.
ولم يجب على الصبي الإيمان قبل أن يعقل لعدم أهلية الأداء، وإذا عقل واحتمل الأداء قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان عليه دون أدائه، حتى صح الأداء من غير تكليف، وكان فرضاً كالمسافر يؤدّي الجمعة.
أداء الإيمان من الصبي العاقل
وأما أهلية الأداء فنوعان قاصر وكامل، أما القاصر فيثبت بقدرة البدن إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ،
أحدهما وثانيهما وهو لعدم أهلية الأداء: أي لا يثبت نفس الوجوب على الصبي لعدم الفائدة، الأداء لا يمكن منه أداء الإيمان باختيار لعدم العقل. عن الاختيار، والصبي بوجوب أصل الإيمان إلخ لأن الوجوب يتعلق بالأسباب وصلاحية الذمة، فالصبي العاقل أهل لأداء الإيمان، فلا يبطل نفس الوجوب في حقه لعدم فوات غرضه وهو الأداء، بخلاف سائر العبادات فإنها ليست بواجبة عليه لفوات غرض نفس الوجوب فيها؛ لأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب أن يقع الأداء عن الفرض، وأداء العبادات لا يقع عن الفرض؛ لأنه لو وقع صلاته فرضا لافترض عليه سائر الصلوات وفيه حرج عظيم، بخلاف الإيمان فإنه غير مكرّر، ولأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب الأداء على سبيل الإكمال والصبي لضعفه لا يحتمل أداء العبادات على وجه الكمال؛ لأن أدائها على وجه الكمال متعلّق بالبدن وهو ضعيف البدن، بخلاف الإيمان فإن أدائه لا يتعلق بالبدن؛ لأنه من أحكام النظرية التي تتعلق بالعقل، والعقل موجود فيه.
دون أدائه أي لا نقول: إن أداء الإيمان واجب على الصبي العاقل قبل البلوغ؛ لأن عقله لم يتكامل بعد؛ لأن كمال العقل إنما هو بعد البلوغ. فرضاً: لأن الإيمان لا يتنوع بين أن يكون فرضاً وأن يكون نفلا بل هو فرض، فلذا لا يلزم عليه تجديد الإقرار بعد البلوغ. يؤدّي الجمعة: فالمؤدّى يقع فرضاً مع أن وجوب الجمعة لم يكن ثابتاً قبل الأداء، هذا ما ذهب إليه القاضي أبو زيد وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وفخر الإسلام له، وقال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي * له: إن الوجوب غير ثابت في حق الصبي وإن عَقَلَ ما لم يتكامل عقله بالبلوغ. أما القاصر إلخ : اعلم أن الأداء يتعلق بقدرتين: قدرة فهم الخطاب وهي بالعقل، وقدرة العمل وهي بالبدن، فإذا تحقق القدرتان تحقق الأهلية الكاملة، وإذا انتفت أو ضعفت إحدى القدرتين تحقق الأهلية القاصرة، وإليه أشار بقوله "إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ فقبل البلوغ العقل والبدن كلاهما ناقصان، وهذا أحد القسمين من الأهلية القاصرة وأشار إلى ثانيهما بقوله: وكذلك إلخ.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Explanation of Legal Capacity. And when [the fetus] separates and an absolute dhimma appears for him, he becomes eligible for obligation for him and upon him, except that the obligation from the mother due to birth, as its place has passed, is not intended by itself, so it is permissible that it becomes null due to lack of its ruling and purpose, just as it becomes null due to lack of its place. And because of this, nothing of the laws (shara'i') that are acts of obedience is obligatory upon the disbeliever, because he is not eligible for the reward of the afterlife, but faith is incumbent upon him because he is eligible to perform its ruling. And since he does not have a complete dhimma as previously mentioned, nothing of rights is obligatory upon him; even if the guardian buys something for him, the price is not obligatory upon him. And to this he pointed with his statement: 'And it is not obligatory, etc.' He was eligible, etc. The summary is that the fetus, if not separated, has a dhimma in one aspect, where rights like inheritance and manumission are established for him, but no right of another is obligatory upon him. And when separated, he has a complete dhimma, so obligations are established for him and upon him. And since it could be objected that if he has a complete dhimma, his ruling should be like that of adults, so what is punishment and recompense should also be obligatory upon him, as some of our scholars held, like Qadi Imam Abu Zaid and others, he repelled this with his statement: 'except that it is not intended by itself, etc.' Meaning: the intended and primary purpose of obligation itself is its ruling, which is performance by choice. And the child cannot be imagined to perform by choice due to his incapacity. So obligation becomes null in actions that necessarily require performance by choice, due to the loss of purpose. And just as a thing becomes null due to the loss of its place, like selling a free person or emancipating an animal, it also becomes null due to the loss of purpose. So what cannot be performed by choice is not incumbent upon the child, so his ruling is not like that of adults, so what is obligatory upon them is not obligatory upon him. The detail of the matter: what pertains to rights of servants like penalty, liability for damages, and compensation (like price of sale, maintenance of wives and relatives) is incumbent upon the child, because performance by choice in those matters is not essential, and the guardian's performance stands in place of his performance, as if the obligation is not [fully?]. And what is punishment and recompense is not obligatory upon him, because the purpose of punishments is to hold accountable for the act, and he is not suitable for that. So obligation here is devoid of its ruling and becomes null. And the guardian, in what is punishment and recompense, cannot stand in his place. Similarly, purely divine rights like prayer and fasting are also not obligatory upon him, because performance by choice (i.e., with intention) is essential in them, and the guardian's performance cannot stand in place of his performance. So obligation becomes null due to loss of purpose. And details will come later. When he finished from 'خال عن' the answer, he began to elaborate on his statement: 'So it is permissible that it becomes null due to lack of its ruling and purpose, just as it becomes null due to lack of its place.' So he said: 'And because of this, etc.' 'Eligible for reward of the afterlife': meaning that the purpose of the laws that are acts of obedience like fasting, prayer, and zakat is reward of the afterlife. And the disbeliever is not eligible for reward of the afterlife, so the obligation of those laws upon the disbeliever is devoid of purpose, so it becomes null, so those laws are not obligatory upon him. And he made an exception with his statement 'which are acts of obedience' from laws that are not acts of obedience and whose purpose is not reward of the afterlife, like jizya and kharaj, for they are obligatory upon him. And since it could be imagined from his lack of eligibility for reward that faith should also not be obligatory upon him, he repelled this with his statement: 'and it is incumbent upon him, etc.' 'And faith is incumbent upon him, etc.': meaning that in the obligation of faith upon the disbeliever, the purpose of faith (reward of the afterlife) is not lost, and the disbeliever is eligible for faith. So if he believes, he attains reward of the afterlife, so the purpose is not lost, so faith is obligatory upon him. Then he began another elaboration and said: 'And it is not obligatory, etc.' And faith is not obligatory upon the child before he understands (ya'qilu) due to lack of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'). And when he understands and can potentially perform, we say that the essence of faith is obligatory upon him, not its performance, so that performance is valid without obligation, and it was obligatory like the traveler performing Friday prayer. Performance of faith from the rational child. As for capacity for performance, there are two types: deficient (qasir) and complete (kamil). As for the deficient, it is established by bodily ability when it is deficient before puberty. One of them and the second: it is due to lack of capacity for performance: meaning that the obligation itself is not established upon the child due to lack of benefit; performance of faith cannot be performed by choice due to lack of reason. [...] Regarding the obligation of the essence of faith, etc., because obligation is connected to causes and the suitability of the dhimma. So the rational child is eligible to perform faith, so the obligation itself is not nullified in his case due to lack of loss of its purpose (performance), unlike other acts of worship, for they are not obligatory upon him due to loss of the purpose of obligation itself; because the purpose of obligation itself is that performance occurs as an obligation (fard). And performance of acts of worship does not occur as an obligation because if his prayer occurred as an obligation, then all other prayers would be obligatory upon him, and that would be a great hardship. Unlike faith, for it is not repeated. And because the purpose of obligation itself is performance in a complete manner, and the child, due to his weakness, cannot bear performing acts of worship perfectly, because their complete performance is connected to the body, and he is weak in body. Unlike faith, for its performance is not connected to the body, because it is from the rulings of theoretical reason that pertain to the intellect, and the intellect is present in him. 'Not its performance' i.e., we do not say that the performance of faith is obligatory upon the rational child before puberty, because his intellect is not yet complete; completeness of intellect is only after puberty. 'It was obligatory' because faith does not vary between being an obligation (fard) and being supererogatory (nafl), but it is an obligation. Therefore, renewal of the declaration after puberty is not required of him. 'Like the traveler performing Friday prayer': the performed act occurs as an obligation even though the obligation of Friday prayer was not established before performance. This is the view of Qadi Abu Zaid, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and Fakhr al-Islam. But Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi held that obligation is not established in the case of the child, even if he understands, as long as his intellect has not become complete by puberty. As for the deficient [type], etc.: Know that performance depends on two abilities: the ability to understand address, which is by intellect, and the ability to act, which is by body. So if both abilities are realized, complete capacity is realized. If one of the abilities is absent or weak, deficient capacity is realized. And to this he pointed with his statement 'when it is deficient before puberty, so before puberty both intellect and body are deficient. This is one of the two divisions of deficient capacity, and he pointed to the second with his statement: 'and similarly, etc.'
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the topic of legal capacity (ahliyyah) from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. It explains the ruling regarding the fetus (janin), the child (sabi), and the disbeliever (kafir) concerning the obligation of various laws. The author first discusses that when a fetus is born separately, it acquires a complete dhimma (legal personality), making it eligible for obligations. However, the obligation that existed on the mother due to pregnancy is not intended by itself and thus can become void if its purpose (gharad) is lost. The principle is that an obligation can be nullified either by the loss of its place (mahall) or by the loss of its purpose (gharad). For the child, obligations that require performance by choice (e.g., acts of worship) are not obligatory because the child cannot perform them by choice. However, financial obligations like damages and maintenance are incumbent because the guardian can perform them on his behalf. For the disbeliever, acts of obedience that are purely worship (e.g., prayer, fasting, zakat) are not obligatory because their purpose is reward in the afterlife, and the disbeliever is not eligible for that reward. But faith (iman) is obligatory because the disbeliever is eligible for faith and can attain reward through it. The passage then discusses the child's obligation of faith: before he understands (ya'qilu), faith is not obligatory. When he understands, the essence of faith (asl al-iman) becomes obligatory, but its performance (ada') is not obligatory because the child's intellect and body are deficient. This is compared to the traveler performing Friday prayer: the prayer counts as an obligation even though the obligation was not previously established upon him. The passage concludes by defining two types of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'): deficient (qasirah) and complete (kamilah). Deficient capacity arises when one or both of the necessary abilities (intellect and body) are weak or absent, as occurs before puberty. The Hanafi school holds that complete capacity is only achieved after puberty and sanity. An internal ikhtilaf is noted: Qadi Abu Zaid and others hold that the obligation of faith is established on the rational child, while Imam Sarakhsi holds that obligation is not established until the intellect is complete at puberty.

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity to acquire obligations and rights
ذمة (dhimma): Legal personality; complete for adult, partial for fetus
غرض (gharad): Purpose or rationale of an obligation
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-ada'): Capacity to perform obligations through valid acts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is daily prayer not obligatory on a child before puberty?
A) Because the child lacks a dhimma entirely.
B) Because the purpose of prayer (performance by choice with intention) cannot be achieved by the child.
C) Because prayer is not required until one reaches the age of 15.
D) Because the guardian can pray on behalf of the child.

Key Takeaway
Legal capacity hinges on a qualified dhimma; obligations that require personal intentional performance are not incumbent on those who cannot fulfill that purpose.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
5 min
Obligations on the Disbeliever: Worship vs. Faith
Explaining why worship is not obligatory on the disbeliever but faith is

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why acts of worship (like prayer) are not obligatory on a disbeliever according to the Hanafi school, while faith (iman) is, using the concept of gharad.

Core Idea
Worship's purpose is afterlife reward; disbelievers are ineligible, so the obligation falls away. Faith's purpose is attainable, so it remains obligatory.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the obligations of a disbeliever (kafir). The key principle is that an obligation is only valid if its intended purpose (gharad) can be achieved. Acts of worship (prayer, fasting, zakat) aim for reward in the hereafter, but the disbeliever, by virtue of his state, is not eligible for that reward. Therefore, these worship obligations are nullified. Faith (iman), however, is obligatory because the disbeliever can attain its reward if he believes. The passage also notes exceptions like jizya and kharaj, which are not acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on acts of worship for the disbeliever
The text states that 'nothing of the laws that are acts of obedience is obligatory upon the disbeliever'. Note that this is specific to acts of obedience (ta'at) like prayer, fasting, zakat.
2
Understand the reasoning using gharad
The purpose of these acts is reward in the afterlife. The disbeliever is not eligible for that reward (because he rejects faith). Therefore, the obligation is nullified due to loss of purpose.
This is an application of the general principle from Lesson 1.
3
Differentiate acts of worship from other obligations
The passage makes an exception: 'which are acts of obedience'. Obligations like jizya and kharaj (taxes) are not acts of obedience; their purpose is worldly, so they are obligatory on the disbeliever.
4
Explain why faith (iman) is obligatory
Faith's purpose is reward in the afterlife, but the disbeliever is eligible to attain it if he believes. Thus, the obligation of faith remains valid.
The text contrasts faith with other acts: faith is not an act of obedience in the same sense? Actually iman is the foundation.
