باب القياس
فصل في بيان الأهلية
وإذا انفصل وظهرت له ذمة مطلقة كان أهلا للوجوب له وعليه، غير أن الوجوب عن الأم بسبب الولادة كما مر محله غير مقصود بنفسه، فجاز أن يبطل لعدم حكمه وغرضه، كما ينعدم لعدم محله ولهذا لم يجب على الكافر شيء من الشرائع التي هي الطاعات؛ لما لم يكن أهلاً لثواب الآخرة، ولزمه الإيمان؛ لما كان أهلا لأدائه حکمه، ووجوب
ولما لم يكن له ذمة كاملة كما مرّ، فلا يجب عليه شيء من الحقوق حتى لو اشترى له الولي شيئاً لا يجب عليه الثمن وإليه أشار بقوله: ولم يجب إلخ. كان أهلا إلخ والحاصل أن الجنين إذا لم ينفصل فله ذمة من وجه، حيث يثبت له الحقوق من الإرث والعتق ولا يجب عليه حق غيره، وإذا انفصل فله ذمة كاملة فيثبت له وعليه، ولما كان يرد عليه من أنه إذا حصل له ذمة كاملة فينبغي أن يكون حكمه كحكم البالغين، فيجب عليه ما كان عقوبة وجزاء أيضا، كما ذهب إليه بعض مشايخنا مثل قاضي الإمام أبي زيد وغيره، فدفعه بقوله: غير أن إلخ. غير مقصود بنفسه إلخ: يعني إنما المقصود والغرض الأصلي من نفس الوجوب حكمه وهو الأداء من اختيار، والصبي لا يتصوّر منه الأداء بالاختيار لعجزه، فيبطل الوجوب في الأفعال التي لا بد من أدائه باختيار؛ لفوات الغرض، والشيء كما يبطل بفوت المحل كبيع الحر وإعتاق البهيمة يبطل بفوت الغرض أيضا، فلا يلزم على الصبي ما لا يمكن أداؤه بالاختيار فلا يكون حكمه كحكم البالغين فلا يجب عليه ما يجب عليهم. وتفصيل المقام ما كان حقوق العباد من الغرم وضمان المتلفات والعوض كثمن المبيع ونفقة الزوجات والأقارب يلزم على الصبي، لأن الأداء بالاختيار في تلك الأمور ليس بضروري، ويكون أداء وليه كأدائه، وكأن الوجوب غير وما كان عقوبة وجزاء لم يجب عليه؛ لأن المقصود من العقوبات المؤاخذة بالفعل، وهو لايصلح لذلك، فالوجوب ههنا خال عن حكمه فيبطل والولي في ما يجب عليه العقوبة والجزاء لا يصلح أن يقوم مقامه، وكذا حقوق الله الخالصة كالصلاة والصوم لا يجب عليه أيضا؛ لأن الأداء بالاختيار أي بالنية ضروري فيها، والولي لا يصلح أن يكون أداؤه قائماً مقام أدائه فيبطل الوجوب بفوت الغرض، وسيأتي التفصيل فوق هذا. ولما فرغ عن خال عن الجواب شرع في تفريعات على قوله : فجاز أن يبطل لعدم حكمه وغرضه كما يبطل لعدم محله، فقال: ولهذا إلخ. أهلا لثواب الآخرة: يعني أن الغرض من الشرائع التي هي الطاعات كالصوم والصلاة والزكاة ثواب الآخرة، والكافر ليس أهلا لثواب الآخرة، فوجوب تلك الشرائع على الكافر خال عن الغرض فيبطل، فلا تجب عليه تلك الشرائع، واحترز بقوله : "التي هي الطاعات" عن الشرائع التي ليست بطاعات وليس الغرض منها ثواب الآخرة كالجزية والخراج، فإنها واجبة عليه، ولما كان يتوهم من عدم كونه أهلا للثواب أن لا يجب عليه الإيمان أيضاً دفعه بقوله: ولزمه إلخ. ولزمه الإيمان إلخ : يعني في وجوب الإيمان على الكافر لا يفوت الغرض من الإيمان ثواب الآخرة والكافر أهل للإيمان فإذا آمن يحصل له ثواب الآخرة، فلا يفوت الغرض، فيجب عليه الإيمان. ثم شرع في تفريع آخر وقال: ولم يجب إلخ.
ولم يجب على الصبي الإيمان قبل أن يعقل لعدم أهلية الأداء، وإذا عقل واحتمل الأداء قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان عليه دون أدائه، حتى صح الأداء من غير تكليف، وكان فرضاً كالمسافر يؤدّي الجمعة.
أداء الإيمان من الصبي العاقل
وأما أهلية الأداء فنوعان قاصر وكامل، أما القاصر فيثبت بقدرة البدن إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ،
أحدهما وثانيهما وهو لعدم أهلية الأداء: أي لا يثبت نفس الوجوب على الصبي لعدم الفائدة، الأداء لا يمكن منه أداء الإيمان باختيار لعدم العقل. عن الاختيار، والصبي بوجوب أصل الإيمان إلخ لأن الوجوب يتعلق بالأسباب وصلاحية الذمة، فالصبي العاقل أهل لأداء الإيمان، فلا يبطل نفس الوجوب في حقه لعدم فوات غرضه وهو الأداء، بخلاف سائر العبادات فإنها ليست بواجبة عليه لفوات غرض نفس الوجوب فيها؛ لأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب أن يقع الأداء عن الفرض، وأداء العبادات لا يقع عن الفرض؛ لأنه لو وقع صلاته فرضا لافترض عليه سائر الصلوات وفيه حرج عظيم، بخلاف الإيمان فإنه غير مكرّر، ولأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب الأداء على سبيل الإكمال والصبي لضعفه لا يحتمل أداء العبادات على وجه الكمال؛ لأن أدائها على وجه الكمال متعلّق بالبدن وهو ضعيف البدن، بخلاف الإيمان فإن أدائه لا يتعلق بالبدن؛ لأنه من أحكام النظرية التي تتعلق بالعقل، والعقل موجود فيه.
دون أدائه أي لا نقول: إن أداء الإيمان واجب على الصبي العاقل قبل البلوغ؛ لأن عقله لم يتكامل بعد؛ لأن كمال العقل إنما هو بعد البلوغ. فرضاً: لأن الإيمان لا يتنوع بين أن يكون فرضاً وأن يكون نفلا بل هو فرض، فلذا لا يلزم عليه تجديد الإقرار بعد البلوغ. يؤدّي الجمعة: فالمؤدّى يقع فرضاً مع أن وجوب الجمعة لم يكن ثابتاً قبل الأداء، هذا ما ذهب إليه القاضي أبو زيد وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وفخر الإسلام له، وقال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي * له: إن الوجوب غير ثابت في حق الصبي وإن عَقَلَ ما لم يتكامل عقله بالبلوغ. أما القاصر إلخ : اعلم أن الأداء يتعلق بقدرتين: قدرة فهم الخطاب وهي بالعقل، وقدرة العمل وهي بالبدن، فإذا تحقق القدرتان تحقق الأهلية الكاملة، وإذا انتفت أو ضعفت إحدى القدرتين تحقق الأهلية القاصرة، وإليه أشار بقوله "إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ فقبل البلوغ العقل والبدن كلاهما ناقصان، وهذا أحد القسمين من الأهلية القاصرة وأشار إلى ثانيهما بقوله: وكذلك إلخ.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Explanation of Legal Capacity. And when [the fetus] separates and an absolute dhimma appears for him, he becomes eligible for obligation for him and upon him, except that the obligation from the mother due to birth, as its place has passed, is not intended by itself, so it is permissible that it becomes null due to lack of its ruling and purpose, just as it becomes null due to lack of its place. And because of this, nothing of the laws (shara'i') that are acts of obedience is obligatory upon the disbeliever, because he is not eligible for the reward of the afterlife, but faith is incumbent upon him because he is eligible to perform its ruling. And since he does not have a complete dhimma as previously mentioned, nothing of rights is obligatory upon him; even if the guardian buys something for him, the price is not obligatory upon him. And to this he pointed with his statement: 'And it is not obligatory, etc.' He was eligible, etc. The summary is that the fetus, if not separated, has a dhimma in one aspect, where rights like inheritance and manumission are established for him, but no right of another is obligatory upon him. And when separated, he has a complete dhimma, so obligations are established for him and upon him. And since it could be objected that if he has a complete dhimma, his ruling should be like that of adults, so what is punishment and recompense should also be obligatory upon him, as some of our scholars held, like Qadi Imam Abu Zaid and others, he repelled this with his statement: 'except that it is not intended by itself, etc.' Meaning: the intended and primary purpose of obligation itself is its ruling, which is performance by choice. And the child cannot be imagined to perform by choice due to his incapacity. So obligation becomes null in actions that necessarily require performance by choice, due to the loss of purpose. And just as a thing becomes null due to the loss of its place, like selling a free person or emancipating an animal, it also becomes null due to the loss of purpose. So what cannot be performed by choice is not incumbent upon the child, so his ruling is not like that of adults, so what is obligatory upon them is not obligatory upon him. The detail of the matter: what pertains to rights of servants like penalty, liability for damages, and compensation (like price of sale, maintenance of wives and relatives) is incumbent upon the child, because performance by choice in those matters is not essential, and the guardian's performance stands in place of his performance, as if the obligation is not [fully?]. And what is punishment and recompense is not obligatory upon him, because the purpose of punishments is to hold accountable for the act, and he is not suitable for that. So obligation here is devoid of its ruling and becomes null. And the guardian, in what is punishment and recompense, cannot stand in his place. Similarly, purely divine rights like prayer and fasting are also not obligatory upon him, because performance by choice (i.e., with intention) is essential in them, and the guardian's performance cannot stand in place of his performance. So obligation becomes null due to loss of purpose. And details will come later. When he finished from 'خال عن' the answer, he began to elaborate on his statement: 'So it is permissible that it becomes null due to lack of its ruling and purpose, just as it becomes null due to lack of its place.' So he said: 'And because of this, etc.' 'Eligible for reward of the afterlife': meaning that the purpose of the laws that are acts of obedience like fasting, prayer, and zakat is reward of the afterlife. And the disbeliever is not eligible for reward of the afterlife, so the obligation of those laws upon the disbeliever is devoid of purpose, so it becomes null, so those laws are not obligatory upon him. And he made an exception with his statement 'which are acts of obedience' from laws that are not acts of obedience and whose purpose is not reward of the afterlife, like jizya and kharaj, for they are obligatory upon him. And since it could be imagined from his lack of eligibility for reward that faith should also not be obligatory upon him, he repelled this with his statement: 'and it is incumbent upon him, etc.' 'And faith is incumbent upon him, etc.': meaning that in the obligation of faith upon the disbeliever, the purpose of faith (reward of the afterlife) is not lost, and the disbeliever is eligible for faith. So if he believes, he attains reward of the afterlife, so the purpose is not lost, so faith is obligatory upon him. Then he began another elaboration and said: 'And it is not obligatory, etc.' And faith is not obligatory upon the child before he understands (ya'qilu) due to lack of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'). And when he understands and can potentially perform, we say that the essence of faith is obligatory upon him, not its performance, so that performance is valid without obligation, and it was obligatory like the traveler performing Friday prayer. Performance of faith from the rational child. As for capacity for performance, there are two types: deficient (qasir) and complete (kamil). As for the deficient, it is established by bodily ability when it is deficient before puberty. One of them and the second: it is due to lack of capacity for performance: meaning that the obligation itself is not established upon the child due to lack of benefit; performance of faith cannot be performed by choice due to lack of reason. [...] Regarding the obligation of the essence of faith, etc., because obligation is connected to causes and the suitability of the dhimma. So the rational child is eligible to perform faith, so the obligation itself is not nullified in his case due to lack of loss of its purpose (performance), unlike other acts of worship, for they are not obligatory upon him due to loss of the purpose of obligation itself; because the purpose of obligation itself is that performance occurs as an obligation (fard). And performance of acts of worship does not occur as an obligation because if his prayer occurred as an obligation, then all other prayers would be obligatory upon him, and that would be a great hardship. Unlike faith, for it is not repeated. And because the purpose of obligation itself is performance in a complete manner, and the child, due to his weakness, cannot bear performing acts of worship perfectly, because their complete performance is connected to the body, and he is weak in body. Unlike faith, for its performance is not connected to the body, because it is from the rulings of theoretical reason that pertain to the intellect, and the intellect is present in him. 'Not its performance' i.e., we do not say that the performance of faith is obligatory upon the rational child before puberty, because his intellect is not yet complete; completeness of intellect is only after puberty. 'It was obligatory' because faith does not vary between being an obligation (fard) and being supererogatory (nafl), but it is an obligation. Therefore, renewal of the declaration after puberty is not required of him. 'Like the traveler performing Friday prayer': the performed act occurs as an obligation even though the obligation of Friday prayer was not established before performance. This is the view of Qadi Abu Zaid, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and Fakhr al-Islam. But Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi held that obligation is not established in the case of the child, even if he understands, as long as his intellect has not become complete by puberty. As for the deficient [type], etc.: Know that performance depends on two abilities: the ability to understand address, which is by intellect, and the ability to act, which is by body. So if both abilities are realized, complete capacity is realized. If one of the abilities is absent or weak, deficient capacity is realized. And to this he pointed with his statement 'when it is deficient before puberty, so before puberty both intellect and body are deficient. This is one of the two divisions of deficient capacity, and he pointed to the second with his statement: 'and similarly, etc.'
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the topic of legal capacity (ahliyyah) from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. It explains the ruling regarding the fetus (janin), the child (sabi), and the disbeliever (kafir) concerning the obligation of various laws. The author first discusses that when a fetus is born separately, it acquires a complete dhimma (legal personality), making it eligible for obligations. However, the obligation that existed on the mother due to pregnancy is not intended by itself and thus can become void if its purpose (gharad) is lost. The principle is that an obligation can be nullified either by the loss of its place (mahall) or by the loss of its purpose (gharad). For the child, obligations that require performance by choice (e.g., acts of worship) are not obligatory because the child cannot perform them by choice. However, financial obligations like damages and maintenance are incumbent because the guardian can perform them on his behalf. For the disbeliever, acts of obedience that are purely worship (e.g., prayer, fasting, zakat) are not obligatory because their purpose is reward in the afterlife, and the disbeliever is not eligible for that reward. But faith (iman) is obligatory because the disbeliever is eligible for faith and can attain reward through it. The passage then discusses the child's obligation of faith: before he understands (ya'qilu), faith is not obligatory. When he understands, the essence of faith (asl al-iman) becomes obligatory, but its performance (ada') is not obligatory because the child's intellect and body are deficient. This is compared to the traveler performing Friday prayer: the prayer counts as an obligation even though the obligation was not previously established upon him. The passage concludes by defining two types of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'): deficient (qasirah) and complete (kamilah). Deficient capacity arises when one or both of the necessary abilities (intellect and body) are weak or absent, as occurs before puberty. The Hanafi school holds that complete capacity is only achieved after puberty and sanity. An internal ikhtilaf is noted: Qadi Abu Zaid and others hold that the obligation of faith is established on the rational child, while Imam Sarakhsi holds that obligation is not established until the intellect is complete at puberty.

Key Terms
شرائع التي هي الطاعات (shara'i' allati hiya al-ta'at): Laws that are acts of obedience, e.g., prayer, fasting, zakat
ثواب الآخرة (thawab al-akhirah): Reward in the afterlife; purpose of acts of worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is faith (iman) obligatory on the disbeliever according to this passage?
A) Because faith is an act of obedience like prayer.
B) Because the purpose of faith (reward in afterlife) can be achieved if he believes.
C) Because faith is a condition for jizya.
D) Because the disbeliever is held accountable for everything.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of an act depends on its purpose being achievable; worship's purpose (reward) is unattainable for a disbeliever, so the obligation is nullified.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Obligation of Faith on the Rational Child – Types of Ahliyyat al-Ada'
Explaining the obligation of faith on the rational child and introducing capacity types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the obligation of faith for a rational child (sabiyy 'aqil), distinguish the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf, and define the two types of ahliyyat al-ada' (deficient and complete).

Core Idea
The essence of faith is obligatory on a rational child, but not its performance; this differs from other acts of worship due to faith's uniqueness and the child's intellectual capacity.

This lesson delves into the obligation of faith (iman) on a child who has reached the age of reason (ya'qilu). The passage presents a nuanced Hanafi view: the essence of faith (asl al-iman) is obligatory, but its actual performance (ada') is not required because the child's intellect is not complete. This leads to an internal ikhtilaf (disagreement) among Hanafi scholars, notably between Qadi Abu Zaid (and others) and Imam Sarakhsi. The lesson also introduces the two types of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'): deficient (qasirah) and complete (kamilah), defined by the presence and strength of intellectual and physical abilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on faith for a child before understanding (ya'qilu)
The text first states that faith is not obligatory on the child before he understands. Then it discusses the rational child (ya'qilu).
2
Understand the obligation of the essence (asl) vs. performance (ada')
For the rational child, the essence of faith (asl al-iman) is obligatory, but its performance (ada') is not. The reason given is that the child's intellect is not complete; he cannot perform faith perfectly (or he could, but it's not required because if performance were obligatory, it would necessitate renewal at puberty, causing hardship).
3
Explore the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
The author presents two views: (1) Qadi Abu Zaid, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, Fakhr al-Islam hold that faith is obligatory in essence (and performance is not obligatory but valid as fard). (2) Imam Sarakhsi holds that obligation is not established until complete intellect at puberty.
The passage seems to favor the first view.
4
Define the two types of ahliyyat al-ada'
The text concludes by dividing capacity for performance into deficient (qasir) and complete (kamil). Deficient arises when one of the two abilities (intellect or body) is weak or absent, as in the child before puberty. Complete requires both strong intellect and body.
This classification sets the foundation for understanding when obligations become fully incumbent.

فصل في بيان الأهلية
وإذا انفصل وظهرت له ذمة مطلقة كان أهلا للوجوب له وعليه، غير أن الوجوب عن الأم بسبب الولادة كما مر محله غير مقصود بنفسه، فجاز أن يبطل لعدم حكمه وغرضه، كما ينعدم لعدم محله ولهذا لم يجب على الكافر شيء من الشرائع التي هي الطاعات؛ لما لم يكن أهلاً لثواب الآخرة، ولزمه الإيمان؛ لما كان أهلا لأدائه حکمه، ووجوب
ولما لم يكن له ذمة كاملة كما مرّ، فلا يجب عليه شيء من الحقوق حتى لو اشترى له الولي شيئاً لا يجب عليه الثمن وإليه أشار بقوله: ولم يجب إلخ. كان أهلا إلخ والحاصل أن الجنين إذا لم ينفصل فله ذمة من وجه، حيث يثبت له الحقوق من الإرث والعتق ولا يجب عليه حق غيره، وإذا انفصل فله ذمة كاملة فيثبت له وعليه، ولما كان يرد عليه من أنه إذا حصل له ذمة كاملة فينبغي أن يكون حكمه كحكم البالغين، فيجب عليه ما كان عقوبة وجزاء أيضا، كما ذهب إليه بعض مشايخنا مثل قاضي الإمام أبي زيد وغيره، فدفعه بقوله: غير أن إلخ. غير مقصود بنفسه إلخ: يعني إنما المقصود والغرض الأصلي من نفس الوجوب حكمه وهو الأداء من اختيار، والصبي لا يتصوّر منه الأداء بالاختيار لعجزه، فيبطل الوجوب في الأفعال التي لا بد من أدائه باختيار؛ لفوات الغرض، والشيء كما يبطل بفوت المحل كبيع الحر وإعتاق البهيمة يبطل بفوت الغرض أيضا، فلا يلزم على الصبي ما لا يمكن أداؤه بالاختيار فلا يكون حكمه كحكم البالغين فلا يجب عليه ما يجب عليهم. وتفصيل المقام ما كان حقوق العباد من الغرم وضمان المتلفات والعوض كثمن المبيع ونفقة الزوجات والأقارب يلزم على الصبي، لأن الأداء بالاختيار في تلك الأمور ليس بضروري، ويكون أداء وليه كأدائه، وكأن الوجوب غير وما كان عقوبة وجزاء لم يجب عليه؛ لأن المقصود من العقوبات المؤاخذة بالفعل، وهو لايصلح لذلك، فالوجوب ههنا خال عن حكمه فيبطل والولي في ما يجب عليه العقوبة والجزاء لا يصلح أن يقوم مقامه، وكذا حقوق الله الخالصة كالصلاة والصوم لا يجب عليه أيضا؛ لأن الأداء بالاختيار أي بالنية ضروري فيها، والولي لا يصلح أن يكون أداؤه قائماً مقام أدائه فيبطل الوجوب بفوت الغرض، وسيأتي التفصيل فوق هذا. ولما فرغ عن خال عن الجواب شرع في تفريعات على قوله : فجاز أن يبطل لعدم حكمه وغرضه كما يبطل لعدم محله، فقال: ولهذا إلخ. أهلا لثواب الآخرة: يعني أن الغرض من الشرائع التي هي الطاعات كالصوم والصلاة والزكاة ثواب الآخرة، والكافر ليس أهلا لثواب الآخرة، فوجوب تلك الشرائع على الكافر خال عن الغرض فيبطل، فلا تجب عليه تلك الشرائع، واحترز بقوله : "التي هي الطاعات" عن الشرائع التي ليست بطاعات وليس الغرض منها ثواب الآخرة كالجزية والخراج، فإنها واجبة عليه، ولما كان يتوهم من عدم كونه أهلا للثواب أن لا يجب عليه الإيمان أيضاً دفعه بقوله: ولزمه إلخ. ولزمه الإيمان إلخ : يعني في وجوب الإيمان على الكافر لا يفوت الغرض من الإيمان ثواب الآخرة والكافر أهل للإيمان فإذا آمن يحصل له ثواب الآخرة، فلا يفوت الغرض، فيجب عليه الإيمان. ثم شرع في تفريع آخر وقال: ولم يجب إلخ.
ولم يجب على الصبي الإيمان قبل أن يعقل لعدم أهلية الأداء، وإذا عقل واحتمل الأداء قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان عليه دون أدائه، حتى صح الأداء من غير تكليف، وكان فرضاً كالمسافر يؤدّي الجمعة.
أداء الإيمان من الصبي العاقل
وأما أهلية الأداء فنوعان قاصر وكامل، أما القاصر فيثبت بقدرة البدن إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ،
أحدهما وثانيهما وهو لعدم أهلية الأداء: أي لا يثبت نفس الوجوب على الصبي لعدم الفائدة، الأداء لا يمكن منه أداء الإيمان باختيار لعدم العقل. عن الاختيار، والصبي بوجوب أصل الإيمان إلخ لأن الوجوب يتعلق بالأسباب وصلاحية الذمة، فالصبي العاقل أهل لأداء الإيمان، فلا يبطل نفس الوجوب في حقه لعدم فوات غرضه وهو الأداء، بخلاف سائر العبادات فإنها ليست بواجبة عليه لفوات غرض نفس الوجوب فيها؛ لأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب أن يقع الأداء عن الفرض، وأداء العبادات لا يقع عن الفرض؛ لأنه لو وقع صلاته فرضا لافترض عليه سائر الصلوات وفيه حرج عظيم، بخلاف الإيمان فإنه غير مكرّر، ولأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب الأداء على سبيل الإكمال والصبي لضعفه لا يحتمل أداء العبادات على وجه الكمال؛ لأن أدائها على وجه الكمال متعلّق بالبدن وهو ضعيف البدن، بخلاف الإيمان فإن أدائه لا يتعلق بالبدن؛ لأنه من أحكام النظرية التي تتعلق بالعقل، والعقل موجود فيه.
دون أدائه أي لا نقول: إن أداء الإيمان واجب على الصبي العاقل قبل البلوغ؛ لأن عقله لم يتكامل بعد؛ لأن كمال العقل إنما هو بعد البلوغ. فرضاً: لأن الإيمان لا يتنوع بين أن يكون فرضاً وأن يكون نفلا بل هو فرض، فلذا لا يلزم عليه تجديد الإقرار بعد البلوغ. يؤدّي الجمعة: فالمؤدّى يقع فرضاً مع أن وجوب الجمعة لم يكن ثابتاً قبل الأداء، هذا ما ذهب إليه القاضي أبو زيد وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وفخر الإسلام له، وقال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي * له: إن الوجوب غير ثابت في حق الصبي وإن عَقَلَ ما لم يتكامل عقله بالبلوغ. أما القاصر إلخ : اعلم أن الأداء يتعلق بقدرتين: قدرة فهم الخطاب وهي بالعقل، وقدرة العمل وهي بالبدن، فإذا تحقق القدرتان تحقق الأهلية الكاملة، وإذا انتفت أو ضعفت إحدى القدرتين تحقق الأهلية القاصرة، وإليه أشار بقوله "إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ فقبل البلوغ العقل والبدن كلاهما ناقصان، وهذا أحد القسمين من الأهلية القاصرة وأشار إلى ثانيهما بقوله: وكذلك إلخ.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Explanation of Legal Capacity. And when [the fetus] separates and an absolute dhimma appears for him, he becomes eligible for obligation for him and upon him, except that the obligation from the mother due to birth, as its place has passed, is not intended by itself, so it is permissible that it becomes null due to lack of its ruling and purpose, just as it becomes null due to lack of its place. And because of this, nothing of the laws (shara'i') that are acts of obedience is obligatory upon the disbeliever, because he is not eligible for the reward of the afterlife, but faith is incumbent upon him because he is eligible to perform its ruling. And since he does not have a complete dhimma as previously mentioned, nothing of rights is obligatory upon him; even if the guardian buys something for him, the price is not obligatory upon him. And to this he pointed with his statement: 'And it is not obligatory, etc.' He was eligible, etc. The summary is that the fetus, if not separated, has a dhimma in one aspect, where rights like inheritance and manumission are established for him, but no right of another is obligatory upon him. And when separated, he has a complete dhimma, so obligations are established for him and upon him. And since it could be objected that if he has a complete dhimma, his ruling should be like that of adults, so what is punishment and recompense should also be obligatory upon him, as some of our scholars held, like Qadi Imam Abu Zaid and others, he repelled this with his statement: 'except that it is not intended by itself, etc.' Meaning: the intended and primary purpose of obligation itself is its ruling, which is performance by choice. And the child cannot be imagined to perform by choice due to his incapacity. So obligation becomes null in actions that necessarily require performance by choice, due to the loss of purpose. And just as a thing becomes null due to the loss of its place, like selling a free person or emancipating an animal, it also becomes null due to the loss of purpose. So what cannot be performed by choice is not incumbent upon the child, so his ruling is not like that of adults, so what is obligatory upon them is not obligatory upon him. The detail of the matter: what pertains to rights of servants like penalty, liability for damages, and compensation (like price of sale, maintenance of wives and relatives) is incumbent upon the child, because performance by choice in those matters is not essential, and the guardian's performance stands in place of his performance, as if the obligation is not [fully?]. And what is punishment and recompense is not obligatory upon him, because the purpose of punishments is to hold accountable for the act, and he is not suitable for that. So obligation here is devoid of its ruling and becomes null. And the guardian, in what is punishment and recompense, cannot stand in his place. Similarly, purely divine rights like prayer and fasting are also not obligatory upon him, because performance by choice (i.e., with intention) is essential in them, and the guardian's performance cannot stand in place of his performance. So obligation becomes null due to loss of purpose. And details will come later. When he finished from 'خال عن' the answer, he began to elaborate on his statement: 'So it is permissible that it becomes null due to lack of its ruling and purpose, just as it becomes null due to lack of its place.' So he said: 'And because of this, etc.' 'Eligible for reward of the afterlife': meaning that the purpose of the laws that are acts of obedience like fasting, prayer, and zakat is reward of the afterlife. And the disbeliever is not eligible for reward of the afterlife, so the obligation of those laws upon the disbeliever is devoid of purpose, so it becomes null, so those laws are not obligatory upon him. And he made an exception with his statement 'which are acts of obedience' from laws that are not acts of obedience and whose purpose is not reward of the afterlife, like jizya and kharaj, for they are obligatory upon him. And since it could be imagined from his lack of eligibility for reward that faith should also not be obligatory upon him, he repelled this with his statement: 'and it is incumbent upon him, etc.' 'And faith is incumbent upon him, etc.': meaning that in the obligation of faith upon the disbeliever, the purpose of faith (reward of the afterlife) is not lost, and the disbeliever is eligible for faith. So if he believes, he attains reward of the afterlife, so the purpose is not lost, so faith is obligatory upon him. Then he began another elaboration and said: 'And it is not obligatory, etc.' And faith is not obligatory upon the child before he understands (ya'qilu) due to lack of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'). And when he understands and can potentially perform, we say that the essence of faith is obligatory upon him, not its performance, so that performance is valid without obligation, and it was obligatory like the traveler performing Friday prayer. Performance of faith from the rational child. As for capacity for performance, there are two types: deficient (qasir) and complete (kamil). As for the deficient, it is established by bodily ability when it is deficient before puberty. One of them and the second: it is due to lack of capacity for performance: meaning that the obligation itself is not established upon the child due to lack of benefit; performance of faith cannot be performed by choice due to lack of reason. [...] Regarding the obligation of the essence of faith, etc., because obligation is connected to causes and the suitability of the dhimma. So the rational child is eligible to perform faith, so the obligation itself is not nullified in his case due to lack of loss of its purpose (performance), unlike other acts of worship, for they are not obligatory upon him due to loss of the purpose of obligation itself; because the purpose of obligation itself is that performance occurs as an obligation (fard). And performance of acts of worship does not occur as an obligation because if his prayer occurred as an obligation, then all other prayers would be obligatory upon him, and that would be a great hardship. Unlike faith, for it is not repeated. And because the purpose of obligation itself is performance in a complete manner, and the child, due to his weakness, cannot bear performing acts of worship perfectly, because their complete performance is connected to the body, and he is weak in body. Unlike faith, for its performance is not connected to the body, because it is from the rulings of theoretical reason that pertain to the intellect, and the intellect is present in him. 'Not its performance' i.e., we do not say that the performance of faith is obligatory upon the rational child before puberty, because his intellect is not yet complete; completeness of intellect is only after puberty. 'It was obligatory' because faith does not vary between being an obligation (fard) and being supererogatory (nafl), but it is an obligation. Therefore, renewal of the declaration after puberty is not required of him. 'Like the traveler performing Friday prayer': the performed act occurs as an obligation even though the obligation of Friday prayer was not established before performance. This is the view of Qadi Abu Zaid, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and Fakhr al-Islam. But Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi held that obligation is not established in the case of the child, even if he understands, as long as his intellect has not become complete by puberty. As for the deficient [type], etc.: Know that performance depends on two abilities: the ability to understand address, which is by intellect, and the ability to act, which is by body. So if both abilities are realized, complete capacity is realized. If one of the abilities is absent or weak, deficient capacity is realized. And to this he pointed with his statement 'when it is deficient before puberty, so before puberty both intellect and body are deficient. This is one of the two divisions of deficient capacity, and he pointed to the second with his statement: 'and similarly, etc.'
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the topic of legal capacity (ahliyyah) from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. It explains the ruling regarding the fetus (janin), the child (sabi), and the disbeliever (kafir) concerning the obligation of various laws. The author first discusses that when a fetus is born separately, it acquires a complete dhimma (legal personality), making it eligible for obligations. However, the obligation that existed on the mother due to pregnancy is not intended by itself and thus can become void if its purpose (gharad) is lost. The principle is that an obligation can be nullified either by the loss of its place (mahall) or by the loss of its purpose (gharad). For the child, obligations that require performance by choice (e.g., acts of worship) are not obligatory because the child cannot perform them by choice. However, financial obligations like damages and maintenance are incumbent because the guardian can perform them on his behalf. For the disbeliever, acts of obedience that are purely worship (e.g., prayer, fasting, zakat) are not obligatory because their purpose is reward in the afterlife, and the disbeliever is not eligible for that reward. But faith (iman) is obligatory because the disbeliever is eligible for faith and can attain reward through it. The passage then discusses the child's obligation of faith: before he understands (ya'qilu), faith is not obligatory. When he understands, the essence of faith (asl al-iman) becomes obligatory, but its performance (ada') is not obligatory because the child's intellect and body are deficient. This is compared to the traveler performing Friday prayer: the prayer counts as an obligation even though the obligation was not previously established upon him. The passage concludes by defining two types of capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'): deficient (qasirah) and complete (kamilah). Deficient capacity arises when one or both of the necessary abilities (intellect and body) are weak or absent, as occurs before puberty. The Hanafi school holds that complete capacity is only achieved after puberty and sanity. An internal ikhtilaf is noted: Qadi Abu Zaid and others hold that the obligation of faith is established on the rational child, while Imam Sarakhsi holds that obligation is not established until the intellect is complete at puberty.

Key Terms
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-ada'): Capacity to perform obligations; two types: qasir (deficient) and kamil (complete)
أصل الإيمان (asl al-iman): The essence of faith, i.e., internal conviction and acceptance
قاصر (qasir): Deficient; lacking one or both of the two abilities for complete capacity
كامل (kamil): Complete; having both strong intellect and physical ability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence of the view that the essence of faith is obligatory on a rational child?
A) The child must perform all religious duties immediately.
B) The child's faith counts as a fard and does not need renewal at puberty.
C) The child is not considered a Muslim until puberty.
D) The child must repeat the shahada daily.

Key Takeaway
The essence of faith is obligatory on a rational child, but performance is not required due to incomplete intellect; this is an area of internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Deficient Legal Capacity of a Discerning Minor
Defines deficient legal capacity and applies it to a discerning minor, with a dispute on iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define deficient legal capacity, identify its four categories of actions, and distinguish the Hanafi position on a discerning minor's iman from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The discerning minor's acts are valid but not obligatory—except iman, which is valid and counts as his obligation.

In Hanafi usul, legal capacity (ahliyyah) is divided into capacity for obligation and capacity for performance. This passage focuses on the latter, particularly the deficient capacity (ahliyyah qasira) of a discerning minor. The author explains that while acts like prayer are valid but not obligatory for such a minor, iman is unique: both valid and considered his obligatory faith, with worldly consequences. We will unpack the reasoning and the Shafi'i disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
Understand the difference between the essence of obligation (asl al-wujub) and its performance (ada') in the context of iman for a discerning minor.
The passage says 'قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان عليه دون أدائه' – we say the essence of iman is obligatory, not its performance.
2
Trace the analogy
Examine how the author compares a minor's iman to a traveler performing Friday prayer: both are valid as obligations even if not originally obligatory before performance.
The comparison highlights that iman, like Jumu'ah for a traveler, can be performed and count as fard without prior obligation.
3
Differentiate deficient vs complete capacity
Identify the two components of capacity (intellect and body) and how their deficiency produces deficient capacity. Note the two cases: before puberty and mentally deficient adult (ma'tuh).
Deficient capacity arises when either intellect or body is incomplete.
4
Classify the minor's actions
The passage enumerates four categories of actions for a discerning minor: iman, purely beneficial transactions, acts of worship, and risk-bearing transactions. List each and their ruling.
Use the text: 'وتبتني على الأهلية القاصرة صحة الأداء...' and the subsequent divisions.
5
Examine the dispute with Shafi'i
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the worldly rulings of a minor's iman. Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) and which position is relied upon.
The Hanafi position: iman valid in both worlds; Shafi'i: only in afterlife.

باب القياس
فصل في بيان الأهلية
ولم يجب على الصبي الإيمان قبل أن يعقل لعدم أهلية الأداء، وإذا عقل واحتمل الأداء قلنا بوجوب أصل الإيمان عليه دون أدائه، حتى صح الأداء من غير تكليف، وكان فرضاً كالمسافر يؤدّي الجمعة.

وأما أهلية الأداء فنوعان قاصر وكامل، أما القاصر فيثبت بقدرة البدن إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ، وهو لعدم أهلية الأداء: أي لا يثبت نفس الوجوب على الصبي لعدم الفائدة، الأداء لا يمكن منه أداء الإيمان باختيار لعدم العقل. عن الاختيار، والصبي بوجوب أصل الإيمان إلخ لأن الوجوب يتعلق بالأسباب وصلاحية الذمة، فالصبي العاقل أهل لأداء الإيمان، فلا يبطل نفس الوجوب في حقه لعدم فوات غرضه وهو الأداء، بخلاف سائر العبادات فإنها ليست بواجبة عليه لفوات غرض نفس الوجوب فيها؛ لأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب أن يقع الأداء عن الفرض، وأداء العبادات لا يقع عن الفرض؛ لأنه لو وقع صلاته فرضا لافترض عليه سائر الصلوات وفيه حرج عظيم، بخلاف الإيمان فإنه غير مكرّر، ولأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب الأداء على سبيل الإكمال والصبي لضعفه لا يحتمل أداء العبادات على وجه الكمال؛ لأن أدائها على وجه الكمال متعلّق بالبدن وهو ضعيف البدن، بخلاف الإيمان فإن أدائه لا يتعلق بالبدن؛ لأنه من أحكام النظرية التي تتعلق بالعقل، والعقل موجود فيه.

دون أدائه أي لا نقول: إن أداء الإيمان واجب على الصبي العاقل قبل البلوغ؛ لأن عقله لم يتكامل بعد؛ لأن كمال العقل إنما هو بعد البلوغ. فرضاً: لأن الإيمان لا يتنوع بين أن يكون فرضاً وأن يكون نفلا بل هو فرض، فلذا لا يلزم عليه تجديد الإقرار بعد البلوغ. يؤدّي الجمعة: فالمؤدّى يقع فرضاً مع أن وجوب الجمعة لم يكن ثابتاً قبل الأداء، هذا ما ذهب إليه القاضي أبو زيد وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وفخر الإسلام له، وقال الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي له: إن الوجوب غير ثابت في حق الصبي وإن عَقَلَ ما لم يتكامل عقله بالبلوغ. أما القاصر إلخ : اعلم أن الأداء يتعلق بقدرتين: قدرة فهم الخطاب وهي بالعقل، وقدرة العمل وهي بالبدن، فإذا تحقق القدرتان تحقق الأهلية الكاملة، وإذا انتفت أو ضعفت إحدى القدرتين تحقق الأهلية القاصرة، وإليه أشار بقوله "إذا كانت قاصرة قبل البلوغ فقبل البلوغ العقل والبدن كلاهما ناقصان، وهذا أحد القسمين من الأهلية القاصرة وأشار إلى ثانيهما بقوله: وكذلك إلخ.

وكذلك بعد البلوغ فيمن كان معتوها؛ لأنه بمنزلة الصبي؛ لأنه عاقل لم يعتدل عقله، وتبتني على الأهلية القاصرة صحة الأداء، وعلى الأهلية الكاملة الأداء، وتوجه الخطاب عليه وعلى هذا قلنا إنه صح من الصبي العاقل الإسلام منه وصح وجوب وما يتمحض منفعته من التصرفات كقبول الهبة والصدقة وصح منه أداء العبادات أيضاً البدنية من غير عهدة وملك برأي الولي ما يتردّد بين النفع والضرر كالبيع ونحوه وذلك باعتبار أن نقصان رأيه انجبر برأي الولي، أي الصبي كان معتوها هو السفيه، فبدنه كامل ولكن عقله ناقص، كما أشار إليه : لأنه بمنزلة الصبي إلخ. صحة الأداء: بمعنى أنه لو أدّى يكون صحيحاً وإن لم يجب عليه. وعلى الأهلية الكاملة إلخ: فإذا بلغ وعقل يلزم عليه الأداء ويتوجه عليه خطاب الشارع؛ لأن أهليته حينئذ صارت كاملة بكمال العقل والبدن. ثم لما كان وقت اعتدال العقول في أفراد الإنسان متفاوتاً لا يمكن إدراكه إلا بعد تجربة عظيمة أقام الشرع البلوغ الذي عنده يعتدل العقول في الأغلب مقام الاعتدال تيسيراً. وعلى هذا أي على أن صحة الأداء تبتني على الأهلية القاصرة. إنه صح إلخ : في أحكام الدنيا والآخرة بلا لزوم عليه، وعند الشافعي الله لا يصح إيمانه قبل البلوغ في أحكام الدنيا، فيرث أباه الكافر ولاتبين منه المشرك كة؛ لأنه ضرر، وإن صح في أحكام الآخرة فيثاب على إيمانه وهذا هو القسم الأول الذي هو حق حسن لا يحتمل غيره. وما يتمحض منفعته إلخ وهذا قسم ثان، وهو ما كان من غير حقوق الله تعالى ولكن فيه نفع محض للصبي، فيصح مباشرة الصبي من غير رضاء الولي وإذنه. العبادات البدنيه إلخ وهذا قسم ثالث، وهو ما كان دائراً بين كونه حسناً في زمان وقبيحاً في زمان، كالصلاة والصوم من العبادات البدنية، فيصح من الصبي أداؤها من غير وجوب عليه، وفي صحة الأداء بلا لزوم عليه نفع من حيث يعتاد أداؤها، فلايشق ذلك بعد البلوغ، ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: "مروا صبيانكم بالصلاة إذا بلغوا سبعاً، واضربوهم إذا بلغوا عشراً". [المسند للإمام أحمد، رقم: ٦٦٨٩] يتردد بين النفع والضرر إلخ وهذا هو القسم الرابع من المعاملات الدائرة بين النفع والضرر كالبيع، فإنه إن كان رابحا كان نافعاً، وإن كان خاسراً كان ضاراً، والصبي لا يميز بين الضار والنافع، ولا يعتبر فيه رأيه، فلا بد أن ينضم إليه رأي الولي.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Explanation of Legal Capacity. Faith is not obligatory upon a child before he attains reason due to lack of capacity to perform. When he reasons and is capable of performance, we say that the essence of faith is obligatory upon him, not its performance, so that performance is valid without obligation, and it counts as an obligation, like a traveler performing Friday prayer. As for capacity to perform, it is of two types: deficient and complete. The deficient is established by bodily capacity when it is deficient before puberty...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on legal capacity (ahliyyah) focusing on the discerning minor. The author clarifies the Hanafi position that the essence of iman (faith) becomes obligatory upon a discerning minor, but its performance is not obligatory. This is because iman is not repeatable and does not depend on bodily strength; thus, if he declares faith before puberty, it is valid and counts as his obligatory iman, so he does not need to renew it after puberty. This contrasts with other acts of worship (e.g., prayer, fasting), which are not obligatory for the minor because they require bodily perfection and repetition, leading to hardship. The passage then divides ahliyyat al-ada' into deficient (qasira) and complete (kamila). Deficient capacity arises when either intellect or body is incomplete, such as before puberty or in a mentally deficient adult (ma'tuh). Upon this deficient capacity, the validity of performance is built: actions performed by such a person are valid but not obligatory. The text then categorizes actions of a discerning minor into four types: (1) iman, valid in both worldly and afterlife rulings without being obligatory; (2) purely beneficial transactions (e.g., accepting gifts), valid without guardian's permission; (3) acts of worship like prayer and fasting, valid and encouraged but not obligatory; (4) transactions with potential profit/loss (e.g., sale), valid only with guardian's consent due to the minor's lack of judgment. The passage also notes a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i who holds that a minor's iman is valid only for the afterlife, not for worldly rulings.

Key Terms
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-ada'): Legal capacity to perform acts; divided into deficient (qasira) and complete (kamila)
الصبي العاقل (al-sabi al-aqil): A minor who has attained discernment (tamyiz) but has not yet reached puberty
القاصر (al-qasir): Deficient capacity; occurs when either intellect or body is incomplete before puberty or due to mental deficiency

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a discerning minor's declaration of faith (iman) before puberty?
A) Valid in both worldly and afterlife rulings and counts as his obligatory faith.
B) Valid only after puberty.
C) Valid but must be repeated after puberty.
D) Not valid until he reaches full responsibility.

Key Takeaway
The discerning minor's deficient capacity makes his acts valid without obligation, but iman is unique: its essence is obligatory and it carries worldly consequences per the Hanafi school.

Classification of Impediments: Samāwī and Muktasab
Definition and classification of impediments to legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify impediments (ʿawāriḍ) as heavenly (samāwī) or acquired (muktasab) and state their effect on legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Core Idea
Impediments to legal capacity are either divinely decreed or humanly acquired, suspending or removing obligation or performance.

Legal capacity is not absolute; it can be affected by various states. The great Hanafi scholars categorized these states as 'impediments' (ʿawāriḍ) to capacity. In this passage, the author provides a clear taxonomy: some impediments are beyond human control (heavenly), while others arise from human action or circumstance (acquired). Understanding this classification is key to knowing when rulings are lifted, shortened, or remain intact.

Guided Path
1
Define ʿāriḍ (impediment)
Understand the linguistic and technical meaning: something that turns a person away from proceeding, like a cloud blocking sunlight. Relate it to legal capacity.
The term comes from 'araḍa, meaning to appear and obstruct.
2
Identify the two types of capacity affected
Differentiate between ahliyyat al-wujūb (capacity for obligation) and ahliyyat al-adāʾ (capacity for performance). Note which impediments remove which type.
Death removes obligation capacity; sleep removes performance capacity.
3
List the heavenly impediments (samāwī)
Memorize the ten heavenly impediments: childhood, insanity, idiocy, forgetfulness, sleep, unconsciousness, slavery, illness, menstruation, postnatal bleeding, death.
These are imposed by the Lawgiver without human choice.
4
Subclassify acquired impediments (muktasab)
Distinguish between impediments from oneself (e.g., ignorance, intoxication) and from others (coercion with or without compulsion).
Acquired impediments originate from human action or external compulsion.
5
Apply the taxonomy to a scenario
Given a state like travel or illness, determine whether it is heavenly or acquired and its effect on capacity.
Travel is acquired from oneself; illness is heavenly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ عن بيان الأهلية شرع في بيان الأمور المعترضة على الأهلية على الأهلية: فتمنع تلك الأمور الأهلية عن بقائها على حالها، فبعضها يزيل أهلية الوجوب كالموت وبعضها تزيل أهلية الأداء كالنوم والإغماء، وبعضها تغيراً في بعض الأحكام مع بقاء أهلية الوجوب والأداء كالسفر كذا قيل العوارض: جمع عارضة من عرض له كذا أي إذا ظهر له أمر يصدّه عن المضي على ما كان فيه، ويسمّى السحاب عارضاً لمنعه أثر الشمس وشعاعها، ولما كان لهذه الأمور تأثير في تغير الأحكام التي تتعلّق بأهلية الوجوب أو أهلية الأداء، وكانت تمنع الأحكام عن الثبوت توجب ستميت بالعوارض سماوي وهو ما ثبت من قبل صاحب الشرع بلا اختيار العبد فيه، ولهذا نسب إلى السماء. عوارض سماوية الصغر والجنون والعته والنسيان والنوم والإغماء والرق والمرض والحيض والنفاس والموت، وأما المكتسب فنوعان منه ومن غيره، أما الذي منه فالجهل والسفه فإنه حصل من المكلف والسكر والهزل والخطأ والسفر، وأما الذي من غيره فالإكراه بما فيه إلجاء وبما ليس فيه إلجاء.
When he finished explaining legal capacity, he began explaining the impediments to legal capacity: for those matters prevent legal capacity from remaining as it is. Some of them remove the capacity for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub) like death, some remove the capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada') like sleep and unconsciousness, and some change some rulings while maintaining the capacity for obligation and performance like travel. So it is said: al-awāriḍ (impediments) is the plural of 'āriḍa from 'araḍa lahu kadhā, i.e., when something appears that turns him away from proceeding as he was. The cloud is called 'āriḍ because it blocks the effect of the sun and its rays. Since these matters have an effect on changing the rulings related to capacity for obligation or capacity for performance, and they prevent rulings from being established, they necessitate being called impediments. Heavenly is what is established by the Lawgiver without the choice of the servant, and hence it is attributed to the sky. Heavenly impediments: childhood, insanity, idiocy, forgetfulness, sleep, unconsciousness, slavery, illness, menstruation, postnatal bleeding, and death. As for the acquired, they are of two types: from oneself and from others. As for from oneself: ignorance, foolishness, since it occurs from the legally responsible person, intoxication, jest, mistake, and travel. As for from others: coercion, including that which involves compulsion and that which does not involve compulsion.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification section (usul definition). The author explains the concept of 'awāriḍ (impediments) that affect legal capacity (ahliyyah). He first describes how impediments can wholly or partially remove capacity: death removes capacity for obligation entirely, sleep removes capacity for performance temporarily, and travel modifies certain rulings (e.g., prayer shortened) without removing underlying capacity. The etymology of 'āriḍ is given as something that obstructs, like a cloud blocking the sun. Impediments are then divided into two main categories: heavenly (sāmiṅ) – those beyond human control, imposed by the Lawgiver – and acquired (muktasab). Ten heavenly impediments are listed: infancy, insanity, idiocy, forgetfulness, sleep, unconsciousness, slavery, illness, menstruation, postnatal bleeding, and death. Acquired impediments are further subdivided: those originating from the person himself (ignorance, foolishness, intoxication, jest, mistake, travel) and those from others (coercion, both with and without compulsion). This classification serves as a foundational taxonomy for understanding how various states affect a person's legal capacity in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
عارض سماوي (ʿāriḍ samāwī): An impediment originating from divine decree without human choice, such as infancy, insanity, death.
عارض مكتسب (ʿāriḍ muktasab): An impediment acquired through human action or circumstance, such as ignorance, intoxication, travel.
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujūb): Capacity for obligation; the capability to have rights and duties imposed.
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-adāʾ): Capacity for performance; the capability to legally perform acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a heavenly impediment (ʿāriḍ samāwī)?
A) Sleep
B) Coercion
C) Death
D) Menstruation

Key Takeaway
Impediments to legal capacity are systematically divided into heavenly (beyond human control) and acquired (from oneself or others), each with specific effects on obligation and performance capacity.

Legal Effects of Insanity (Junūn) on Capacity
Detailed ruling on how insanity affects legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between statements and actions to derive the legal capacity of a continuously insane person, and identify which obligations are dropped and which remain.

Core Idea
Insanity voids statements but not actions; only obligations droppable by adults under excuses are waived.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on insanity (junūn) as an impediment to legal capacity. The source text from al-Husami defines insanity and distinguishes between statements (invalid) and actions (valid). You will learn the criterion for which obligations are dropped and which remain, using the concept of 'yaḥtamil al-suqūṭ'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the medical definition of insanity
Read the definition: insanity is a brain disease that causes irrational actions without lethargy. Understand that it is given precedence over childhood because the initial state of minority resembles insanity.
The definition establishes the cause (sabab) for legal rulings.
2
Distinguish between statements and actions
The text states that statements (e.g., divorce, manumission, gift) are invalid because they depend on reason which insanity negates. Actions, however, are physical and cannot be denied; they remain valid for liability.
This distinction is key: statements require 'aql, actions are tangible.
3
Apply the criterion of 'yaḥtamil al-suqūṭ' to obligations
Obligations that can be dropped from an adult due to excuses (e.g., hudud, kaffarat, ibadat) are waived. Obligations that cannot be dropped except by performance or waiver of the right-holder (e.g., damages, maintenance, diya) remain.
This criterion limits the effect of insanity on duties.
4
Determine the condition of continuity (imtidād)
The ruling applies only when insanity is continuous (mumtadd). Intermittent insanity may require different treatment.
Continuity is a condition (shart) for these rulings.
5
Derive the final ruling
Combine the above: statements invalid; actions valid for liability; only droppable obligations are waived; continuity is required.
This is the complete legal effect of continuous insanity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ عن تقسيم العوارض شرع في أحكامها فقال الجنون: وهو آفة تحلّ بالدماغ بحيث يبعث على أفعال خلاف مقتضى العقل من غير فتور في عامة أطرافه وضعف في أعضائه، وإنما قدّمه على الصغر؛ لأن حكم الصغر في أوّل أحواله كحكم الجنون. عن الأقوال: أي لا يعتبر أقواله كالطلاق والعتاق والهبة فلا يتعلّق بأقواله حكم، ويكون وجود قوله كعدمه حتى لا ينفذ بإجازة الولي واحترز به من الأفعال، فإن أتلف مال إنسان يؤخذ بضمانه على الكمال؛ لأن الأقوال لا تعتبر وجودها بدون العقل والمجنون لا عقل له، بخلاف الأفعال حيث توجد حساً لا مردّ لها. يحتمل السقوط عن البالغ بالأعذار كالحدود والكفارات والقصاص، فإنها تحتمل السقوط عن البالغ بالشبهات، وكذا يسقط به العبادات المتحمّلة للسقوط مثل الصوم والصلاة وسائر العبادات واحترز بقوله "يحتمل السقوط" عن المضار التي لا تحتمل السقوط إلا بالأداء أو بإسقاط من له الحق كضمان المتلفات ونفقة الأقارب، ووجوب الدية والإرش، فإنها لا تسقط بالجنون كما لاتسقط بالصباء، هذا إذا كان الجنون ممتدا.
And when he finished the division of impediments, he began their rulings and said: Insanity (junūn) is a disease that affects the brain such that it drives actions contrary to the dictates of reason without lethargy in most limbs and weakness in organs. He gave it precedence over childhood because the ruling of childhood in its initial state is like that of insanity. 'Regarding statements': i.e., his statements are not considered, such as divorce, manumission, gift. No ruling attaches to his statements, and his utterance is like non-existence, to the extent that it is not executed even with the permission of the guardian. He excluded actions. For if he destroys someone's property, he is held fully liable for its guarantee, because statements have no consideration without reason, and the insane person has no reason, unlike actions which exist physically and cannot be denied. 'What can be dropped from an adult due to excuses': such as hudud (fixed penalties), kaffarat (expiation), and qisas (retaliation), for they can be dropped from an adult due to doubts. Similarly, acts of worship that admit of being dropped, like fasting, prayer, and all other acts of worship, are dropped by insanity. He guarded by his words 'what can be dropped' against the harms that cannot be dropped except by performance or by the one having the right dropping them, such as guarantee of destroyed property, maintenance of relatives, and the obligation of diya (blood money) and arsh (compensation), for they are not dropped by insanity just as they are not dropped by minority. This is when insanity is continuous.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed ruling (hukm) regarding insanity (junūn) as an impediment. The author gives a medical definition: insanity is a brain disease causing irrational actions without lethargy. It is given precedence over infancy because the initial state of minority resembles insanity. The key ruling is that the statements (aqwāl) of an insane person are invalid: divorce, emancipation, and gifts are void. Actions (afʿāl), however, are considered; if he damages property, he must compensate fully, as actions are tangible. The passage then distinguishes between harms that can be dropped (e.g., criminal penalties, acts of worship like fasting) those that cannot be dropped (e.g., compensation for damages, maintenance). This distinction relies on the criterion of whether the obligation can normally be dropped by an adult under excuses (like doubts). Only those that can be dropped are removed from the insane person. Continuous insanity (mumtadd) is a condition for these rulings. This shows the Hanafi method of balancing the principle of harm removal (rafʿ al-ḥaraj) with the necessity of protecting rights.

Key Terms
جنون (junūn): Insanity: a brain disease causing irrational actions without lethargy; a heavenly impediment.
حجر (ḥajr): Incapacity or restriction on legal acts; here it applies to the statements of the insane.
يحتمل السقوط (yaḥtamil al-suqūṭ): A harm (or obligation) that can be dropped; e.g., hudud can be waived by shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a continuously insane person destroys someone's property, what is the ruling?
A) He is not liable because he is insane.
B) He must compensate fully for the damage.
C) He is liable only if he is lucid at the time.
D) The guardian must pay from his own wealth.

Key Takeaway
Continuous insanity invalidates statements but not actions; only obligations that can be excused for adults are waived, while liability for damages remains.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Al-Junun (Insanity) as a Heavenly Impediment: Hanafi Usul Rulings
Defining insanity and its legal effects in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule on insanity to determine which obligations are removed and which verbal acts are interdicted.

Core Idea
Insanity cancels obligations that can be dropped but not financial liabilities; all verbal acts are void.

In Hanafi usul, insanity (junun) is classified as a heavenly impediment ('arid samawi) that affects legal capacity (ahliyyah). This passage from a classical text defines insanity and outlines its two key effects: interdiction on verbal statements (hajr 'an al-aqwal) and selective removal of obligations. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly assessing the legal status of acts performed by an insane person.

Guided Path
1
Define insanity
Identify the Hanafi definition: an affliction of the brain that impels actions contrary to reason. Note that it is a heavenly impediment, not acquired.
The definition emphasizes the physical cause (brain affliction) and the behavioral result (actions contrary to reason).
2
Distinguish verbal statements from actions
Understand that verbal acts (divorce, manumission, gift) are void because they require reason. Actions (like destroying property) are still considered and incur liability.
The rationale: verbal statements have no legal effect without reason; actions have sensory existence and cannot be ignored.
3
Identify which obligations are removed
Insanity cancels obligations that can be dropped due to excuses (e.g., worship, hudud, kaffarat, qisas). It does not remove obligations that must be fulfilled or waived by the right-holder (e.g., financial compensation, maintenance, blood money).
The condition 'extended insanity' (mumtadd) is required for comprehensive removal.
4
Apply the rule to concrete cases
Practice applying the rule: e.g., an insane person divorces (void), but if he destroys property, he must compensate.
This step solidifies the distinction between verbal and physical acts.

باب القياس ۲۷۳ عوارض سماوية الصغر والجنون والعته والنسيان والنوم والإغماء والرق والمرض والحيض والنفاس والموت، وأما المكتسب فنوعان منه ومن غيره، أما الذي منه فالجهل والسفه فإنه حصل من المكلف والسكر والهزل والخطأ والسفر، وأما الذي من غيره فالإكراه بما فيه إلجاء وبما ليس فيه إلجاء. وأما الجنون فإنه يوجب الحجر عن الأقوال، ويسقط به ما كان ضرراً يحتمل السقوط، وإذا امتدّ فصار لزوم الأداء يؤدّي إلى الحرج، فيبطل القول بالأداء .... الصغر وهو وإن كان بأصل الخلقة ولكن ماهية الإنسان قد يعرف من غير صغر، ولذا لم يعرض آدم عليه وحواء عليها فعد من العوارض والإغماء إلخ وإن كان الإغماء والجنون من أقسام المرض، ولكن لما كانا مختصين بأحكام كثيرة يحتاج إلى بيانها أفردهما بالذكر فنوعان أحدهما ما هو حاصل منه، وثانيهما ماهو حاصل من غيره. فالجهل: وإنما جعل من المكتسبة وإن لم يكن للعبد فيه اختيار؛ لأن العبد قادر على إزالته بتحصيل العلم، فكان ترك التحصيل بالاختيار مع القدرة عليه بمنزلة اختيار الجهل وكسبه بالاختيار. والسفه في اللغة عبارة عن الخفة والاضطراب في العقل والفرق بين السفه والعته على ما قلنا ظاهر. إلجاء: أي اضطرار للمكره إلى إتيانه ما أكره عليه، فأقسام المكتسب سبعة. ولما فرغ عن تقسيم العوارض شرع في أحكامها فقال الجنون: وهو آفة تحلّ بالدماغ بحيث يبعث على أفعال خلاف مقتضى العقل من غير فتور في عامة أطرافه وضعف في أعضائه، وإنما قدّمه على الصغر؛ لأن حكم الصغر في أوّل أحواله كحكم الجنون. عن الأقوال: أي لا يعتبر أقواله كالطلاق والعتاق والهبة فلا يتعلّق بأقواله حكم، ويكون وجود قوله كعدمه حتى لا ينفذ بإجازة الولي واحترز به من الأفعال، فإن أتلف مال إنسان يؤخذ بضمانه على الكمال؛ لأن الأقوال لا تعتبر وجودها بدون العقل والمجنون لا عقل له، بخلاف الأفعال حيث توجد حساً لا مردّ لها. يحتمل السقوط عن البالغ بالأعذار كالحدود والكفارات والقصاص، فإنها تحتمل السقوط عن البالغ بالشبهات، وكذا يسقط به العبادات المتحمّلة للسقوط مثل الصوم والصلاة وسائر العبادات واحترز بقوله "يحتمل السقوط" عن المضار التي لا تحتمل السقوط إلا بالأداء أو بإسقاط من له الحق كضمان المتلفات ونفقة الأقارب، ووجوب الدية والإرش، فإنها لا تسقط بالجنون كما لاتسقط بالصباء، هذا إذا كان الجنون ممتدا.
Chapter of Qiyas. 273. Heavenly impediments: infancy, insanity, imbecility, forgetfulness, sleep, fainting, slavery, illness, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, death. As for acquired impediments, they are of two types: from oneself and from others. From oneself: ignorance and foolishness, since they arise from the obligated person; intoxication, jest, mistake, travel. From others: coercion, including compulsion and non-compulsion. As for insanity, it imposes interdiction regarding verbal statements, and it cancels that which is a harm that can possibly be removed. And when it extends, so that the persistence of performance leads to hardship, then the ruling of performance is invalidated. ... Infancy: although it is part of original creation, the essence of a person can be known without infancy, so Adam and Eve were not subject to it, thus it is counted among impediments. Fainting etc. although fainting and insanity are types of illness, but since they have many specific rulings needing explanation, they are mentioned separately. Two types: one that arises from oneself, and the other from others. Ignorance: it is considered acquired even though the servant has no choice in it, because the servant is able to remove it by acquiring knowledge, thus leaving off acquisition with ability is tantamount to choosing ignorance and acquiring it by choice. Foolishness linguistically denotes lightness and disturbance in the mind. The difference between foolishness and imbecility is apparent. 'Ilja': compulsion of the coerced to do that which he is coerced into. So the types of acquired impediments are seven. When he finished dividing impediments, he began their rulings: insanity is an affliction descending upon the brain such that it impels actions contrary to reason without languor in most limbs or weakness in organs. He gave precedence to it over infancy because the ruling of infancy in its initial state is like the ruling of insanity. 'Regarding verbal statements': his statements are not considered, like divorce, manumission, gift; no ruling attaches to his statements, and his statement is like non-existent, not even enacted by guardian's permission. He excludes actions: if he destroys someone's property, he is held liable for full compensation because verbal statements are not considered without reason, and the insane have no reason, unlike actions which exist sensorily and cannot be denied. 'Can possibly be removed from an adult by excuses': like hadd penalties, expiations, retaliation; they can be removed from an adult by doubts. Likewise, it removes acts of worship that can be removed like fasting, prayer, and all acts of worship. By saying 'can possibly be removed', he excludes harms that cannot be removed except by performance or by the right-bearer waiving them, like liability for destroyed property, maintenance of relatives, obligation of blood-money and damages: these are not removed by insanity just as they are not removed by infancy. This is if the insanity is extended.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of impediments ('awārid) and the specific ruling for insanity (junūn). The author first divides impediments into heavenly (like infancy, insanity) and acquired (like ignorance, coercion). Acquired impediments are further divided into those arising from oneself (e.g., ignorance, foolishness) and from others (coercion). The commentary then focuses on insanity, defining it as an affliction of the brain that causes actions contrary to reason. Insanity imposes interdiction (hajr) on verbal statements—such as divorce, manumission, and gifts—rendering them void and unattachable to any legal effect, even with guardian permission. However, actions (like destroying property) still incur liability because they are physically real and cannot be ignored. The ruling on obligations: insanity cancels those that can be dropped (like worship and hudud penalties) but not those that must be fulfilled or waived by the right-holder (like financial compensation, maintenance, blood-money). This is conditional upon the insanity being extended (mumtadd); non-extended insanity may have different rulings. The passage also explains why ignorance is considered 'acquired' even if not chosen: because one has the ability to remove it through learning, so neglecting to learn is tantamount to choosing ignorance.

Key Terms
العوارض (al-ʿawāriḍ): الأحوال الطارئة على المكلف التي تمنع أو تغير الحكم التكليفي أو الوضعي
الحجر عن الأقوال (al-ḥajr ʿan al-aqwāl): منع المجنون من نفوذ أقواله كالطلاق والعتاق والهبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an insane person destroys someone's property, what is the ruling?
A) No liability because there is no intent.
B) Full liability because actions are considered.
C) Half liability because he is insane.
D) No liability unless he has a guardian.

Key Takeaway
Insanity removes only those obligations that can be dropped by excuses, and all verbal acts are void.

The Principle of Extension (Imtidad) and Its Limits
Determining when insanity is considered extended and its effect on worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify insanity into extended and non-extended types and state the Hanafi rule regarding the obligations of prayer, fasting, and zakat.

Core Idea
Extended insanity removes both the obligation and its performance; non-extended accidental insanity is excused by istihsan.

In Hanafi usul, the effect of insanity on worship depends on its duration. The text defines 'imtidad' as encompassing specific periods: a month for fasting, a day and night for prayer, a year for zakat. When insanity extends beyond these limits, the obligation falls entirely. This rule is derived from the principle of prevention of hardship (haraj). This lesson unpacks the classification and the default ruling.

Guided Path
1
Classify by duration and origin
Identify the two classification axes: duration (extended vs non-extended) and origin (original vs accidental). The text provides these categories as key to determining the ruling.
2
Apply the limit values
For fasting: the entire month must be encompassed. For prayer: exceed one day and night. For zakat: the full year (Muhammad) or most of the year (Abu Yusuf) must be encompassed.
These limits are threshold concepts; insubstantial periods do not trigger cancellation.
3
Rule for extended insanity
Extended insanity cancels both the obligation of performance (ada) and the original obligation (wujub) because performance leads to hardship and the purpose of obligation is performance.
This is by consensus (ittifaq).
4
Rule for non-extended accidental insanity
Non-extended accidental insanity does not cancel; istihsan overrides qiyas, analogizing to sleep/fainting. The default qiyas would hold obligations, but istihsan excuses.
This is the position of the three Hanafi imams.
5
Identify the slippery case
Non-extended original insanity (reaching puberty insane) has a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This is a separate issue (covered in the next lesson).
Be mindful of this subtle distinction.

وينعدم الوجوب أيضا لانعدامه. وحدّ الامتداد في الصوم أن يستوعب الشهر، وفي الصلوات أن يزيد على يوم وليلة، وفي الزكاة أن يستوعب الحول عند محمد حلبه، وأقام أبو يوسف له أكثر الحول مقام كلّه تيسيراً، وانعدامه أي الأداء والحاصل إذا كثر الجنون بأن امتد فلا وجوب للأداء عليه، فإنه يفضي إلى الحرج ولا نفس الوجوب عليه أيضا؛ لأن الغرض من نفس الوجوب الأداء، فإذا سقط الأداء بطل نفس الوجوب أيضا لفوات الغرض، وتفصيل هذا المقام أن الجنون إما ممتدّ أو غير ممتدّ، وكل منهما أما أصلي بأن بلغ مجنوناً أو طار بعد البلوغ فتلك الأقسام كلها مانعة؛ لوجوب العبادات كلها عند الشافعي وزفر حملها ، وهو القياس؛ لأن أهلية من الشهر، ولاقضاء ما فاته من الصلوات، فحكمه حكم الصباء، وعند محمد الله ليس بمسقط، فيلزمه قضاء ما مضى من الشهر وقضاء ما فاته من الصلوات قياساً على الجنون العارضي، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وقيل: الاختلاف على العكس، فتفكر في هذا المقام فإنه من مزال الأقدام. أن يستوعب الشهر حتى لو أفاق في جزء من الشهر ليلا أو نهاراً يجب عليه القضاء في ظاهر الرواية، وعن شمس الأئمة الحلواني أنه لو أفاق في أول ليلة من رمضان فأصبح مجنوناً ثم استوعب باقي الشهر لا يجب عليه القضاء، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن الليل لايصام فيه، فالإفاقة والجنون فيه سواء يوم وليلة ولكن محمد يعتبر الصلاة حتى ما لم تصر الصلاة ستاً لا يسقط عنه القضاء، والشيخان يعتبران الساعات حتى لو جُنّ قبل الزوال ثم أفاق في اليوم الثاني بعد الزوال لا قضاء عليه عندهما؛ لأن هذا الوقت باعتبار الساعات زاد على يوم وليلة، وعنده عليه القضاء ما لم يمتد إلى وقت العصر حتى الصلاة والصوم. وجب
And the obligation also becomes non-existent due to its non-existence. The limit of extension in fasting is that it encompasses the entire month; in prayers, that it exceeds one day and night; in zakat, that it encompasses the entire year according to Muhammad (his opinion), and Abu Yusuf treated most of the year as standing for all of it as a facilitation. And its non-existence means the performance. The conclusion: when insanity becomes frequent, i.e., extended, there is no obligation of performance upon him because it leads to hardship, and also not the obligation itself because the purpose of the obligation itself is performance, so if performance falls, the obligation itself becomes void due to loss of purpose. The detail of this matter: insanity is either extended or non-extended. Each is either original (i.e., he reached puberty insane) or accidental (occurring after puberty). All these categories are preventative of all obligations of worship according to al-Shafi'i and Zufar, and they say it is analogy, because legal capacity for performance is lost with loss of reason, and without capacity, obligation is not established. The extended, whether original or accidental, cancels all acts of worship by consensus. As for non-extended, if it is accidental, it is not canceling of acts of worship according to our three Imams by istihsan and analogy with sleep and fainting. If it is original (i.e., reached puberty insane), it is canceling according to Abu Hanifa (his opinion), such that if he regains sanity before the end of Ramadan after reaching puberty insane, or before the completion of a day and night from the time of puberty, he is not required to make up what passed of the month, nor what he missed of prayers. His ruling is like that of infancy. According to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), it is not canceling, so he must make up what passed of the month and what he missed of prayers, by analogy with accidental insanity, and this is the apparent narration. It is said the difference is opposite, so ponder this station for it is a slippery place. That it encompasses the month: even if he regains sanity in part of the month, at night or day, he must make up according to the apparent narration. From Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: that if he regains sanity on the first night of Ramadan and then becomes insane in the morning and the rest of the month is encompassed, he does not have to make up, and this is correct because night is not for fasting, so recovery and insanity are the same in it. A day and night: but Muhammad considers prayer so that as long as the prayer does not become six, he does not drop the make-up. The two shaykhs consider hours: if he became insane before noon and then regained sanity on the second day after noon, there is no make-up according to them because this time, in terms of hours, exceeds a day and night. According to him, he must make up if it does not extend to the time of Asr such that the prayer becomes six, then it enters the limit of repetition. And in zakat, that it encompasses etc.: because as long as the second does not enter, zakat does not enter the limit of repetition. For facilitation and to remove hardship from the obligated person: so if insanity ceases after eleven months have passed, zakat is obligatory according to Muhammad, whether it was original or accidental, because the extension for cancellation of obligation according to him is the completion of the year; if the year is not completed and insanity ceases before completion of the year, zakat is due. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not obligatory due to the obligation ceasing after extension. And analogize to this the extension of prayer and fasting.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of 'imtidad' (extension) of insanity and its effect on the obligation of acts of worship. The author establishes that when insanity becomes extended, the obligation of performance (adā') falls because it would lead to hardship (ḥaraj), and consequently the original obligation (wujūb) also ceases because its purpose is performance. The limit for extension differs: for fasting, encompassing the entire month; for prayers, exceeding one day and night; for zakat, encompassing the full year according to Imam Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf considers most of the year sufficient for facility. Then the passage distinguishes between extended (mumtadd) and non-extended insanity, and between original (aṣlī, i.e., since puberty) and accidental (ṭāri'). Extended insanity of either type cancels all worship by consensus. Non-extended accidental insanity does not cancel worship according to the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) by istihsan, analogizing to sleep/fainting. Non-extended original insanity (reached puberty insane) cancels worship according to Abu Hanifa, treating it like infancy; but Muhammad holds it does not cancel, requiring make-up (qaḍā). There is also a nuance: if one reaches puberty insane and then recovers during Ramadan, Abu Hanifa says no qaḍā for passed days; Muhammad says qaḍā required. For extension measurement in prayer, Muhammad considers the number of prayers (if six prayers pass, making-up is required), while the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider hours (if more than a day and night pass, no qaḍā). For zakat, Muhammad requires extension for full year to cancel; Abu Yusuf considers most of the year as extension for cancellation.

Key Terms
الامتداد (al-imtidād): استمرار الجنون مدة معينة بحيث يفضي إلى الحرج في الأداء
أصلي وطارئ (aṣlī wa ṭāri’): الأصلي: الجنون المقارن للبلوغ، والطارئ: الحادث بعد البلوغ
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāya): الرواية المشهورة عن الإمام محمد في كتبه الستة

Key Takeaway
Extended insanity cancels both the obligation and its performance; non-extended accidental insanity does not cancel by istihsan.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Non-Extended Original Insanity
The Hanafi disagreement on whether non-extended original insanity cancels worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding non-extended original insanity and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Non-extended original insanity divides the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa treats it like infancy (no qada), while Muhammad requires qada by analogy to accidental insanity.

Among the Hanafi imams, there is a key disagreement on whether a person who reaches puberty insane and then recovers must make up missed worship. Abu Hanifa considers this original insanity canceling, like infancy, because the person never had legal capacity. Muhammad, however, analogizes to accidental insanity and requires qada. This lesson explores the arguments and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific case
Non-extended original insanity: a boy reaches puberty while insane, then recovers within the limits of non-extension (e.g., before the end of Ramadan).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
It cancels; no qada required. This view treats original insanity like infancy.
Abu Hanifa's dalil: legal capacity never existed from the start.
3
State Muhammad's position
It does not cancel; qada required. This is reported as zahir al-riwaya.
Muhammad's dalil: qiyas to accidental insanity.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa: original insanity means the person never had capacity; Muhammad: the condition is similar to accidental and the obligation attaches at puberty.
The text also mentions a contrary narration that flips the positions, calling it a slippery place.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a boy reaches puberty insane and recovers during Ramadan: Abu Hanifa says no qada; Muhammad says qada. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view according to Halwani and later tarjih.
The practical consequence is whether missed acts are waived.

Source Text
