العوارض المكتسبة لما فرغ من العوارض السماوية شرع في العوارض المكتسبة. الجهل: وهو بسيط وحد بأنه عدم العلم عما من شأنه العلم، فالتقابل بين الجهل والعلم تقابل الملكة والعدم، ومركب وحد بأنه اعتقاد جازم غير مطابق للواقع مع اعتقاد المطابقة، وهو عيب لا يمكن إزالته بالتعلم، وإنما عدّ الجهل من العوارض وإن كان أصليا لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا (النحل: ۷۸)؛ لأنه أمر زائد على حقيقة الإنسان مفارق ثابت في حال دون حال، وإنما عدّ من المكتسبة وإن كان بلا اختيار العبد في أصل الخلقة لتقصيره في اكتساب العلم؛ لأنه كان قادراً على إزالته بتحصيل العلم، فجعل ترك تحصيله واستمراره على الجهل بمنزلة اكتساب الجهل باختياره. وضوح الدليل لأن الآيات الدالة على وحدانيــــة الصانع وصفات كماله ونعوت جلاله ظاهرة، ولنعم ماقيل: 'ففي كل شيء له شاهد، يدل على أنه واحـــــد'، ولنعم ما قال الأعرابي: 'البعرة تدلّ على البعير، وأثر الإقدام على المسير، فالسماء ذات أبراج والأرض ذات فجاج تدلان على الصانع اللطيف الخبير، فالإنكار بعد ذلك جحود. كما قال تعالى: ﴿وَجَحَدُوا بِهَا وَاسْتَيْقَنَتْهَا أَنْفُسُهُمْ ظُلْماً وَعُلُوا (النمل:١٤)، وكذا الأدلة على رسالة الرسل وهي المعجزات القاهرة والبينــــات البــاهرة لائحة كانت محسوسات في زمانهم. وأما بالنسبة إلى من بعدهم فمتواترة قرناً بعد قرن إلى يومنا هذا، فإنكارها إنكار المحسوس وهو مكابرة، فلايكون عذراً في أحكام الآخرة فيعذب. وأما في أحكام الدنيا فيصلح عذراً، حتى من التزم عقد الذمـــة فـــإن جهله حينئذ يدفع عذاب القتل والحبس في الدنيا، فعند أبي حنيفة اليه ديانة الكافر أي اعتقاده في الأحكام القابلة للتبدل عقلاً كبيع الخمر وغيره مما ثبت خلافه في الإسلام دافعة للتعرض حتى لو باشر ما اعتقده لا يتعرض لــــه بوجه، فلا يجد بشرب الخمر ؛ لانا أمرنا أن نتركهم وما يدينون، وكذا دافعة لدليل الشرع بمعنى أن دينه يمنع بلوغ دليل الشرع إليه، فلا يثبت الخطاب في حقه كأنه غير نازل في حقه وهذا ليس للتخفيف بل للاستدراج، وهـ التقريب إلى العذاب بحيث لا يشعر، وعند الشافعي حاليه رافعة للتعرض فقط. وهذا النوع من الجهل أشد. في صفات الله تعالى: كجهل المعتزلة في إنكار الصفات كقولهم إنه عالم بلا علم وقادر بلا قدرة، ولا فرق بين قول القائل: ليس 'عالم وبين قولهم لا علم له. وجهل المشبهة في قولهم إن صفاته تعالى حادثة قابلة للزوال كصفات الخلق. و في أحكام الآخرة كجهل المعتزلة بسؤال المنكر والنكير وعذاب القبر والميزان، فهذا القسم من الجهل لا يصلح عذراً؛ لأنه مخالف للدليل الواضح الذي لا شبهة فيه سمعاً وعقلاً. أما السمع فكثير من الآيــات والأحاديث الصحيحة دالة على صفاته من العلم والقدرة وغيرهما. قال تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ﴾ (الشورى: ۱۱)، وعلى ثبوت عذاب القبر والميزان وسؤال المنكر والنكير كما روى البخاري والمسلم وأصحاب السنن الأربعة، أما العقل فهو أن المحدثات كما دلّت على وجود الصانع تعالى دلّت على كونه عليماً قديراً وغير ذلـــك مـــن الصفات، وإنما هو محلّ الحوادث حادث ، فلايجوز أن تكون صفاته تعالى حادثة لاستلزام حدوث الذات، فكان ما ذهب إليه أهل الهوى باطلاً وجهلاً بعد وضوح الدليل، فلا يصلح عذراً في الآخرة كجهل الكفر. وجهل الباغي: عطف على قوله 'جهل صاحب الهوى'، والباغي هو الخارج عن طاعة الإمام الحق معتقداً أنــــه على الحق والإمام على الباطل، متمسكاً بقوله تعالى : وإِنِ الْحُكْمُ إِلَّا لِلَّه (الأنعام:٥٧)، وبقوله: ﴿وَمَنْ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَاراً خَالِداً فِيهَا (النساء:١٤) كالخارجين عن إطاعة علي - كرم الله وجهه بالتأويلات الفاسدة، فهذا الجهل أيضاً لا يصلح عذراً.
Acquired hindrances: After finishing celestial hindrances, he began acquired hindrances. Ignorance: simple ignorance defined as absence of knowledge of what is knowable, so the opposition between ignorance and knowledge is the opposition of possession and privation; compound ignorance defined as a firm belief that does not correspond to reality with a belief of correspondence, and it is a defect that cannot be removed by learning. Ignorance is counted among hindrances even though it is original, because of His statement: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers while you knew nothing' (an-Nahl 78); because it is an additional matter beyond the essence of man, separable, existing in some states and not others. It is counted among the acquired hindrances even though it is not by the servant's choice in original creation, due to his negligence in acquiring knowledge; because he was able to remove it by obtaining knowledge, so his leaving off acquiring it and persisting in ignorance is treated as if he acquired ignorance by choice. The clarity of the proof: because the verses indicating the oneness of the Creator and His attributes of perfection and majesty are manifest. How excellent is what was said: 'In everything there is a witness for Him, indicating that He is one.' How excellent is what the Bedouin said: 'The dung indicates the camel, and the footprint indicates the traveler; so the sky with its constellations and the earth with its valleys indicate the All-subtle, All-aware Creator.' So denial after that is obdurate rejection. As He said: 'And they denied them, while their souls were certain thereof, out of wrongdoing and arrogance' (an-Naml 14). Likewise the proofs for the message of the messengers, which are overwhelming miracles and brilliant signs, were manifest and sensibly perceived in their time. As for those after them, they are mutawatir generation after generation up to this day. Denying them is denying the sensible, which is obdurate rejection, so it is not an excuse in the rulings of the Hereafter, so he is punished. As for the rulings of this world, it is an excuse, so that one who has entered into a pact of dhimma — his ignorance at that time averts the punishment of killing and imprisonment in this world. According to Abu Hanifa, the religion of the disbeliever — that is, his belief in rulings that are subject to rational change like selling wine and other things whose opposite is established in Islam — is repelling confrontation, so that even if he does what he believes, he is not confronted at all; he is not punished for drinking wine because we are commanded to leave them and their religion. It is also repelling the evidence of the Law in the sense that his religion prevents the evidence of the Law from reaching him, so the address is not established in his regard as if it had not come down in his regard. This is not for leniency but for drawing him gradually (istidraj), bringing him closer to punishment without his awareness. According to al-Shafi'i, it is only repelling confrontation. And this type of ignorance is more severe. Regarding the attributes of Allah: like the ignorance of the Mu'tazila in denying attributes, such as their saying that He is knowing without knowledge and powerful without power. There is no difference between one saying 'He is not knowing' and their saying 'He has no knowledge.' And the ignorance of the Mushabbiha in their saying that His attributes are originated and subject to perishing like the attributes of creatures. And regarding the rulings of the Hereafter: like the ignorance of the Mu'tazila about the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, and the Balance. This category of ignorance is not a valid excuse because it contradicts the clear proof that is beyond doubt, both transmitted and rational. As for the transmitted: many verses and authentic hadith indicate His attributes of knowledge and power and others. He said: 'There is nothing like unto Him' (ash-Shura 11), and regarding the affirmation of the punishment of the grave, the Balance, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir as reported by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and the authors of the four Sunan. As for the rational: that contingent things as they indicate the existence of the Creator indicate that He is Knowing, Powerful, and other attributes. And the one who is the locus of events is originated, so it is not permissible that His attributes be originated because that would necessitate the origination of the Essence. So what the people of vain desire have held is false and ignorance after the clarity of the proof, so it is not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, like the ignorance of disbelief. And the ignorance of the rebel: it is a conjunction to his statement 'the ignorance of the follower of vain desire'. The rebel is the one who goes out of obedience to the true Imam, believing that he is upon the truth and the Imam upon falsehood, clinging to His statement: 'Indeed, the judgment is only for Allah' (al-An'am 57), and to His statement: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will admit him into a fire, abiding eternally therein' (an-Nisa 14), like those who went out of obedience to Ali (may Allah honor his face) with corrupt interpretations. So this ignorance also is not a valid excuse.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on a usul al-fiqh text, explaining the concept of 'acquired hindrances' (العوارض المكتسبة) with a focus on ignorance (الجهل). The commentator first distinguishes between simple ignorance (lack of knowledge) and compound ignorance (false belief). Ignorance is considered an acquired hindrance because a person could have removed it by seeking knowledge, even though it is originally innate. The passage then presents proof from the Quran (an-Nahl 78) that humans are born without knowledge, but they are expected to learn. The commentator emphasizes the clarity of proofs for God's existence and attributes, so denying them is obdurate rejection (جحود). Such ignorance is not an excuse in the Hereafter, but in worldly matters it may be an excuse. For example, a dhimmi who commits an act according to his own religion (like selling wine) is not punished by the Islamic state because his ignorance of the Islamic ruling is accepted. This is the Hanafi position: the unbeliever's religion repels both punishment and the law's address (due to the law not reaching him). The Shafi'i position is that it only repels punishment but does not prevent the law from addressing him. The passage then describes severe types of ignorance: the ignorance of theologians like Mu'tazila who deny God's attributes, and the ignorance of rebels (bughah) who fight against a just Imam based on misinterpretation. These types are not valid excuses in the Hereafter because the proofs are clear both from revelation and reason. The commentator cites Quranic verses and hadith to support the correct beliefs. In summary, this passage establishes the usul principle that ignorance after clear proof is not a defense, but ignorance in worldly matters due to lack of access to Islamic law may be excused temporarily, according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الجهل البسيط (al-jahl al-basīṭ): Simple ignorance: absence of knowledge of something knowable.
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): Compound ignorance: firm belief that does not match reality, with the belief that it matches.
العارض المكتسب (al-ʿāriḍ al-muktasab): Acquired hindrance: a condition that arises due to the servant's choice or negligence, such as ignorance, as opposed to celestial hindrances (like idiocy).
الجحود (al-juḥūd): Obdurate rejection: knowing something to be true but denying it out of arrogance or wrongdoing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul passage, why is ignorance classified as an acquired hindrance (ʿāriḍ muktasab) even though humans are born ignorant?
A) Because ignorance is always voluntary.
B) Because a person can remove it by seeking knowledge, and persisting in ignorance is treated as acquisition.
C) Because ignorance is a celestial hindrance like insanity.
D) Because compound ignorance cannot be removed by learning.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance is an acquired hindrance because humans are able to learn and are commanded to seek knowledge; persistence in ignorance after clear proof is blameworthy and not excused in the Hereafter.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

The Legal Effect of Ignorance: Worldly Excuse vs. Hereafter Accountability
Discusses the legal effect of ignorance in worldly and otherworldly matters with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the effect of a non-Muslim's ignorance in worldly matters and identify the types of ignorance that are not excused in the Hereafter.

Core Idea
In worldly matters, a non-Muslim's ignorance of Islamic law can excuse them, but in matters of creed after clear proof, ignorance is never an excuse.

This lesson continues on ignorance, now focusing on its legal consequences. The passage explains that while ignorance may serve as an excuse in this world for non-Muslims who have not received the daʿwa, it does not excuse in the Hereafter when the proofs are clear. We examine the Hanafi stance on dhimmi’s ignorance, the Shafi'i objection, and the severe ignorance of theological deviants and rebels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two realms: dunya and akhirah
Ignorance has different effects in worldly punishments vs. otherworldly accountability.
The passage distinguishes between أحكام الدنيا and أحكام الآخرة.
2
State the Hanafi position on non-Muslim ignorance
Abu Hanifa holds that the non-Muslim's religion repels both punishment and the law's address; i.e., the law does not reach them.
Based on the principle 'اتركوهم وما يدينون' (leave them and their religion).
3
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that ignorance only repels punishment but does not prevent the law from addressing the person.
Thus, the act is still forbidden but not punishable in this world.
4
Understand the wisdom: istidraj not leniency
The Hanafi view is not to be lenient but to gradually draw the non-Muslim to punishment without awareness.
This is a key difference in understanding the intent behind the ruling.
5
Recognize severe ignorance that is not excused
Ignorance in matters of creed (attributes, eschatology) after clear proofs, and rebellion against a just Imam, are not excused in the Hereafter.
These are forms of compound ignorance with juhud.

غير مطابق للواقع مع اعتقاد المطابقة، وهو عيب لا يمكن إزالته بالتعلم، وإنما عدّ الجهل من العوارض وإن كان أصليا لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُونِ أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئًا واحـــــد'، ولنعم ما قال الأعرابي: 'البعرة تدلّ على البعير، وأثر الإقدام على المسير، فالسماء ذات أبراج والأرض ذات فجاج تدلان على الصانع اللطيف الخبير، فالإنكار بعد ذلك جحود. كما قال تعالى: ﴿وَجَحَدُوا بِهَا وَاسْتَيْقَنَتْهَا أَنْفُسُهُمْ ظُلْماً وَعُلُوا (النمل:١٤)، وكذا الأدلة على رسالة الرسل وهي المعجزات القاهرة والبينــــات البــاهرة لائحة كانت محسوسات في زمانهم. وأما بالنسبة إلى من بعدهم فمتواترة قرناً بعد قرن إلى يومنا هذا، فإنكارها إنكار المحسوس وهو مكابرة، فلايكون عذراً في أحكام الآخرة فيعذب. وأما في أحكام الدنيا فيصلح عذراً، حتى من التزم عقد الذمـــة فـــإن جهله حينئذ يدفع عذاب القتل والحبس في الدنيا، فعند أبي حنيفة اليه ديانة الكافر أي اعتقاده في الأحكام القابلة للتبدل عقلاً كبيع الخمر وغيره مما ثبت خلافه في الإسلام دافعة للتعرض حتى لو باشر ما اعتقده لا يتعرض لــــه بوجه، فلا يجد بشرب الخمر ؛ لانا أمرنا أن نتركهم وما يدينون، وكذا دافعة لدليل الشرع بمعنى أن دينه يمنع بلوغ دليل الشرع إليه، فلا يثبت الخطاب في حقه كأنه غير نازل في حقه وهذا ليس للتخفيف بل للاستدراج، وهـ التقريب إلى العذاب بحيث لا يشعر، وعند الشافعي حاليه رافعة للتعرض فقط. وهذا النوع من الجهل أشد. في صفات الله تعالى: كجهل المعتزلة في إنكار الصفات كقولهم إنه عالم بلا علم وقادر بلا قدرة، ولا فرق بين قول القائل: ليس 'عالم وبين قولهم لا علم له. وجهل المشبهة في قولهم إن صفاته تعالى حادثة قابلة للزوال كصفات الخلق. و في أحكام الآخرة كجهل المعتزلة بسؤال المنكر والنكير وعذاب القبر والميزان، فهذا القسم من الجهل لا يصلح عذراً؛ لأنه مخالف للدليل الواضح الذي لا شبهة فيه سمعاً وعقلاً. أما السمع فكثير من الآيــات والأحاديث الصحيحة دالة على صفاته من العلم والقدرة وغيرهما. قال تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ﴾ (الشورى: ۱۱)، وعلى ثبوت عذاب القبر والميزان وسؤال المنكر والنكير كما روى البخاري والمسلم وأصحاب السنن الأربعة، أما العقل فهو أن المحدثات كما دلّت على وجود الصانع تعالى دلّت على كونه عليماً قديراً وغير ذلـــك مـــن الصفات، وإنما هو محلّ الحوادث حادث ، فلايجوز أن تكون صفاته تعالى حادثة لاستلزام حدوث الذات، فكان ما ذهب إليه أهل الهوى باطلاً وجهلاً بعد وضوح الدليل، فلا يصلح عذراً في الآخرة كجهل الكفر. وجهل الباغي: عطف على قوله 'جهل صاحب الهوى'، والباغي هو الخارج عن طاعة الإمام الحق معتقداً أنــــه على الحق والإمام على الباطل، متمسكاً بقوله تعالى : وإِنِ الْحُكْمُ إِلَّا لِلَّه (الأنعام:٥٧)، وبقوله: ﴿وَمَنْ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ يُدْخِلْهُ نَاراً خَالِداً فِيهَا (النساء:١٤) كالخارجين عن إطاعة علي - كرم الله وجهه بالتأويلات الفاسدة، فهذا الجهل أيضاً لا يصلح عذراً.
Acquired hindrances: After finishing celestial hindrances, he began acquired hindrances. Ignorance: simple ignorance defined as absence of knowledge of what is knowable, so the opposition between ignorance and knowledge is the opposition of possession and privation; compound ignorance defined as a firm belief that does not correspond to reality with a belief of correspondence, and it is a defect that cannot be removed by learning. Ignorance is counted among hindrances even though it is original, because of His statement: 'And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers while you knew nothing' (an-Nahl 78); because it is an additional matter beyond the essence of man, separable, existing in some states and not others. It is counted among the acquired hindrances even though it is not by the servant's choice in original creation, due to his negligence in acquiring knowledge; because he was able to remove it by obtaining knowledge, so his leaving off acquiring it and persisting in ignorance is treated as if he acquired ignorance by choice. The clarity of the proof: because the verses indicating the oneness of the Creator and His attributes of perfection and majesty are manifest. How excellent is what was said: 'In everything there is a witness for Him, indicating that He is one.' How excellent is what the Bedouin said: 'The dung indicates the camel, and the footprint indicates the traveler; so the sky with its constellations and the earth with its valleys indicate the All-subtle, All-aware Creator.' So denial after that is obdurate rejection. As He said: 'And they denied them, while their souls were certain thereof, out of wrongdoing and arrogance' (an-Naml 14). Likewise the proofs for the message of the messengers, which are overwhelming miracles and brilliant signs, were manifest and sensibly perceived in their time. As for those after them, they are mutawatir generation after generation up to this day. Denying them is denying the sensible, which is obdurate rejection, so it is not an excuse in the rulings of the Hereafter, so he is punished. As for the rulings of this world, it is an excuse, so that one who has entered into a pact of dhimma — his ignorance at that time averts the punishment of killing and imprisonment in this world. According to Abu Hanifa, the religion of the disbeliever — that is, his belief in rulings that are subject to rational change like selling wine and other things whose opposite is established in Islam — is repelling confrontation, so that even if he does what he believes, he is not confronted at all; he is not punished for drinking wine because we are commanded to leave them and their religion. It is also repelling the evidence of the Law in the sense that his religion prevents the evidence of the Law from reaching him, so the address is not established in his regard as if it had not come down in his regard. This is not for leniency but for drawing him gradually (istidraj), bringing him closer to punishment without his awareness. According to al-Shafi'i, it is only repelling confrontation. And this type of ignorance is more severe. Regarding the attributes of Allah: like the ignorance of the Mu'tazila in denying attributes, such as their saying that He is knowing without knowledge and powerful without power. There is no difference between one saying 'He is not knowing' and their saying 'He has no knowledge.' And the ignorance of the Mushabbiha in their saying that His attributes are originated and subject to perishing like the attributes of creatures. And regarding the rulings of the Hereafter: like the ignorance of the Mu'tazila about the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, and the Balance. This category of ignorance is not a valid excuse because it contradicts the clear proof that is beyond doubt, both transmitted and rational. As for the transmitted: many verses and authentic hadith indicate His attributes of knowledge and power and others. He said: 'There is nothing like unto Him' (ash-Shura 11), and regarding the affirmation of the punishment of the grave, the Balance, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir as reported by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and the authors of the four Sunan. As for the rational: that contingent things as they indicate the existence of the Creator indicate that He is Knowing, Powerful, and other attributes. And the one who is the locus of events is originated, so it is not permissible that His attributes be originated because that would necessitate the origination of the Essence. So what the people of vain desire have held is false and ignorance after the clarity of the proof, so it is not a valid excuse in the Hereafter, like the ignorance of disbelief. And the ignorance of the rebel: it is a conjunction to his statement 'the ignorance of the follower of vain desire'. The rebel is the one who goes out of obedience to the true Imam, believing that he is upon the truth and the Imam upon falsehood, clinging to His statement: 'Indeed, the judgment is only for Allah' (al-An'am 57), and to His statement: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will admit him into a fire, abiding eternally therein' (an-Nisa 14), like those who went out of obedience to Ali (may Allah honor his face) with corrupt interpretations. So this ignorance also is not a valid excuse.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on a usul al-fiqh text, explaining the concept of 'acquired hindrances' (العوارض المكتسبة) with a focus on ignorance (الجهل). The commentator first distinguishes between simple ignorance (lack of knowledge) and compound ignorance (false belief). Ignorance is considered an acquired hindrance because a person could have removed it by seeking knowledge, even though it is originally innate. The passage then presents proof from the Quran (an-Nahl 78) that humans are born without knowledge, but they are expected to learn. The commentator emphasizes the clarity of proofs for God's existence and attributes, so denying them is obdurate rejection (جحود). Such ignorance is not an excuse in the Hereafter, but in worldly matters it may be an excuse. For example, a dhimmi who commits an act according to his own religion (like selling wine) is not punished by the Islamic state because his ignorance of the Islamic ruling is accepted. This is the Hanafi position: the unbeliever's religion repels both punishment and the law's address (due to the law not reaching him). The Shafi'i position is that it only repels punishment but does not prevent the law from addressing him. The passage then describes severe types of ignorance: the ignorance of theologians like Mu'tazila who deny God's attributes, and the ignorance of rebels (bughah) who fight against a just Imam based on misinterpretation. These types are not valid excuses in the Hereafter because the proofs are clear both from revelation and reason. The commentator cites Quranic verses and hadith to support the correct beliefs. In summary, this passage establishes the usul principle that ignorance after clear proof is not a defense, but ignorance in worldly matters due to lack of access to Islamic law may be excused temporarily, according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الجهل البسيط (al-jahl al-basīṭ): Simple ignorance: absence of knowledge of something knowable.
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): Compound ignorance: firm belief that does not match reality, with the belief that it matches.
العارض المكتسب (al-ʿāriḍ al-muktasab): Acquired hindrance: a condition that arises due to the servant's choice or negligence, such as ignorance, as opposed to celestial hindrances (like idiocy).
الجحود (al-juḥūd): Obdurate rejection: knowing something to be true but denying it out of arrogance or wrongdoing.
الاستدراج (al-istidrāj): Gradual drawing: a strategy where a person is left in ignorance so that their punishment accumulates in the Hereafter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the wisdom (according to the passage) behind the Hanafi view that a dhimmi's ignorance repels even the law's address, not just punishment?
A) To make Islam more attractive.
B) To gradually draw the dhimmi to punishment in the Hereafter without awareness (istidraj).
C) To avoid burdening Muslims with implementing punishments.
D) To give the dhimmi more time to learn Islamic law.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance is a valid excuse in worldly matters for non-Muslims who have not accepted Islam, but in matters of creed after clear proofs, ignorance is blameworthy and not excused in the Hereafter.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Legal Status of the Rebel and the One with Desire
States Hanafi rule on rebel's legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a rebel with invalid ta'wil remains subject to Islamic rulings, including liability for damages, and distinguish the Shafi'i counter-position.

Core Idea
A rebel's invalid ta'wil does not remove him from Islam — he remains liable under the law.

This passage from the chapter on Qiyas discusses acquired impediments to legal reasoning. It addresses the status of those who rebel or follow desire with a corrupt interpretation (ta'wil). While their interpretation is invalid, they are still considered Muslims as long as they do not go to extremes. Consequently, they are subject to all Islamic rulings, including liability for damages they cause. This lesson explores the Hanafi stance and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects of the rule
The passage deals with two categories: the rebel (al-bāghī) and the one who follows his desires (ṣāḥib al-hawā). Both make a ta'wil based on a semblance of proof.
Their ta'wil is considered invalid but does not remove them from Islam.
2
Recognize the condition of Muslim status
As long as they do not go to extremes (ghuluww) or exceed the limits, they remain Muslims. This is because the invalid ta'wil does not negate the core belief in Islam.
Contrast with extremists like the Ghulat Rafidah who are considered non-Muslim.
3
Apply the consequence: full subjection to rulings
Since they are Muslims (or claimants of Islam), all Sharīʿah rulings apply to them. This includes liability for damages to life and property if they have no military force (manʿa).
The condition of manʿa determines liability: without it, they must compensate; with it, liability drops due to practical inability.
4
Contrast with the Shāfiʿī position
Imam al-Shāfiʿī considers the rebel's ta'wil as a valid excuse, so liability is dropped after repentance. The Hanafī response is that the ta'wil is invalid and thus the excuse fails.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf) is whether compensation is required after repentance.
5
Determine the operative ruling (muftā bihī)
The Hanafī position is adopted: the rebel must guarantee damages if he had no manʿa, even after repentance.
This is based on the principle that the authority of compulsion remains unless blocked by actual force.

نعمل بتأويله الفاسد وقلنا إن الباغي إذا أتلف مال العادل أو نفسه ولا منعة له يضمن، وكذلك سائر الأحكام يلزمه، وكذلك جهل من خالف في اجتهاده الكتاب أو السنة المشهورة من علماء الشريعة، مخالف للدليل إلخ فإن الدليل على إمامة علي وسائر الخلفاء الراشدين وكونهم على الحق ظاهر، والمخالف مكابر معاند. إلا أنه: أي لكن الباغي وصاحب الهوى متأوّل بالقرآن: متمسكاً في ذلك بتأويل ومتعلق بظاهر النصوص كما عرف في موضعه، ولاية المناظرة والإلزام منقطعة عنه؛ لأنه لا يعتقد الإسلام حقاً، فلا يمكن أن نلزم عليه الأحكام بالأدلة الشرعية، وإذا كان صاحب الهوى والباغي ممن لم يترك على ما يعتقده بل يلزم عليه. يضمن : أي إذا أتلف Chapter of Qiyas. Acquired impediments: because it contradicts the clear proof without ambiguity, except that he makes a ta'wil based on the Quran, so it is below this first ignorance. But since he is from the Muslims or among those who claim Islam, we must debate with him and compel him by this approach. So we do not act upon his corrupt ta'wil, and we say: if the rebel destroys the property or life of a just person and he has no military force, he must guarantee it, and likewise all rulings apply to him. And likewise the ignorance of those who oppose in their ijtihad the Book or the famous Sunnah from the scholars of the Shariah is contradictory to the proof, etc. For the evidence for the imamate of Ali and the rest of the rightly-guided caliphs and that they are upon the truth is clear, and the opponent is obstinate. But: i.e., the ignorant one who is the one with desire and the rebel is from the Muslims, because by desire and by rebellion he does not leave Islam if he does not go to extremes and exceed the limit. He claims: i.e., he attributes himself to Islam and claims to be a Muslim even if in reality he is a disbeliever, like the extremists of the Rafidah, the Mujassimah, and the Nijariyyah. And if the one with desire and the rebel are not left upon what they believe but rather are compelled. Rather, he must guarantee if he has no military force, i.e., strength and army. And man'ah is the plural of mani', and the army prevents and repels the opponent. And when the rebel's military force is established, the authority of compelling by proof falls away from him in a sensory and real sense, so it is necessary by his corrupt ta'wil, so he is not held liable for guaranteeing life and property after repentance, just as the people of war are held liable for that after embracing Islam, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Likewise, "Sharh al-Badi'" says: he is obliged, i.e., just as he must guarantee, so must all rulings that obligate the Muslims apply to him, because he is a Muslim or a claimant of Islam, and the authority of compulsion remains upon him. And likewise: i.e., like the ignorance of the one with desire and the rebel. · And the Nijariyyah: a sect that arose in our time. They deny the blessings of Paradise and the modalities of punishment mentioned in the Quran, the existence of angels, the existence of Jibril and the jinn, miracles, and extraordinary events, and they cling to corrupt interpretations that are not supported by reason and revelation. That is by following the atheists of the Yoruba, and their leader in that is Sayyid Ahmad Khan al-Dihlawi. And they deny...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about the legal status of a rebel (baghi) or one who follows his desire (sahib al-hawa) in Islamic law. The author explains that despite their invalid interpretation (ta'wil) which is based on a semblance of Quranic proof, they are still considered Muslims because their deviation does not take them out of Islam as long as they do not go to extremes. Therefore, they must be held accountable for all Islamic rulings, including liability for damages they cause. The passage also discusses the obligation to debate with them and the difference between them and disbelievers. Additionally, it mentions the sect of النيجرية (a modern sect denying certain Quranic realities) as an example of extreme deviation. The key principle is that a Muslim who makes an invalid ta'wil is still a Muslim and subject to the law, unlike a disbeliever who is not bound by Islamic rulings in the same way.

Key Terms
الباغي (al-bāghī): The rebel who fights against the legitimate ruler based on a corrupt interpretation (ta'wil).
صاحب الهوى (ṣāḥib al-hawā): One who follows his desires in matters of religion, making invalid ta'wil.
التأويل (al-ta'wīl): An interpretation that deviates from the apparent meaning of the text based on a semblance of proof.
المنعة (al-man'a): Military force or power that enables a rebel to resist authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi position, what is the status of a rebel (baghi) who makes an invalid ta'wil?
A) He is considered a disbeliever and is not subject to Islamic rulings.
B) He is considered a Muslim and remains subject to all Islamic rulings, including liability for damages.
C) He is considered a Muslim but his liability for damages is dropped after repentance.
D) He is considered a non-Muslim because his ta'wil is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Invalid ta'wil does not remove a Muslim from Islam; the rebel remains fully subject to the law, including liability for damages, unless military force prevents enforcement.

Qasama and the Limit of Qisas
Explains Hanafi anti-qisas rule via qasama and contrasts with Shafi'i views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qasama never results in qisas and apply the principle of certainty (yaqeen) to distinguish between Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Qasama establishes diya, not qisas, because qisas requires certainty beyond oath-based suspicion.

This passage lays down a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: the method of establishing liability through collective oaths (qasama) can never rise to the level of certainty required for qisas. We will see how this principle leads to a clear ruling—only diya is due—and how it contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i's evolving views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
In the passage, locate the explicit Hanafi statement: qisas is never obligatory (لا يجب القصاص بحال). This is the core of the lesson.
Contrast with the opposing schools who allow qisas in certain conditions.
2
Understand the procedure of qasama
When a body is found in a locality but the killer is unknown, fifty men from that locality swear oaths. If they swear, diya is imposed on the locality; those who refuse are imprisoned.
No individual is singled out; the burden falls on the community.
3
Contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
Imam al-Shafi'i's old view allowed qisas if the heirs swore intentionally; his new view limits to diya. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The Hanafi school consistently rejects qisas in qasama.
4
Extract the underlying usul principle
The Hanafi reasoning rests on the principle that qisas requires certainty (yaqeen) or very strong proof; qasama is based on suspicion and circumstantial evidence (lawth), so it cannot meet that threshold.
This principle governs the entire area of criminal liability.
5
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Consider a scenario where heirs demand qisas after swearing fifty oaths. Per Hanafi law, their demand is rejected; only diya is possible. This demonstrates the principle in action.
This prevents the taking of life based on mere oaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقصاص بالقسامة: فإذا وجد الرجل مقتولاً في محلة ولا يدرى قاتله حلف خمسون رجلاً من أهل المحلة، فإن حلفوا فعلى أهل المحلة الدية وحبس الآبي حتى يحلف، ولا يجب القصاص بحال، هذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي: إذا كان هناك لوث استحلف الأولياء خمسين يميناً ويقضى لهم بالدية على المدعى عليه، سواء عمدا كانت الدعوى أو خطأ، وهذا قوله الجديد. وفي القديم : إذا حلفوا أنهم قتلوه عمداً فلهم القصاص، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، وإن نكل الأولياء عن اليمين استحلف أهل المحلة، فإذا حلفوا برثوا، وإن نكلوا حكم عليهم بالدية، هذا تحرير المذهبين، وأما أدلتهم فمذكورة في المطوّلات وكل واحد يجهل الآخر فيما خالفه، ويقول: إنه مخالفة للسنة.
And qisas by qasama: If a man is found killed in a locality and his killer is unknown, fifty men from the people of that locality swear; if they swear, the diya is upon the people of the locality, and the one who refuses is imprisoned until he swears, and qisas is never obligatory. This is our view. Al-Shafi'i said: If there is lawth (suspicion), the heirs swear fifty oaths and judgment is given for them for diya against the accused, whether the claim is for intentional or accidental killing. This is his new view. In his old view: If they swear that he killed him intentionally, then they have qisas, and Malik and Ahmad said the same. And if the heirs decline the oath, the people of the locality are made to swear; if they swear, they are exonerated; if they decline, judgment is given against them for diya. This is a summary of the two schools. As for their proofs, they are mentioned in lengthy works, and each one declares the other ignorant in what he opposes, and says that it is a contradiction of the sunnah.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage discusses the institution of qasama (oath-taking in cases of homicide) and its legal consequences. In Hanafi law, qasama never leads to qisas (retaliatory execution); it only results in diya (blood money) being imposed on the inhabitants of the locality where the body was found, and those who refuse to swear are imprisoned. The Hanafi view is contrasted with Imam al-Shafi'i's two positions: his old view allowed qisas if the heirs swore that the killing was intentional, while his new view restricts the outcome to diya. The passage notes that the full proofs are found in extended works, and each school claims the other contradicts the sunnah.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasāmah): A procedure of oaths taken by fifty men from the locality where a corpse is found, to avoid liability.
اللوث (al-lawth): Suspicion or circumstantial evidence pointing to the guilt of a particular person or group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the outcome of qasama?
A) The killer is executed if the heirs swear.
B) The people of the locality pay diya, and no qisas is imposed.
C) If the heirs swear, the accused must pay diya; if not, the accused goes free.
D) The imam can choose between qisas and diya.

Key Takeaway
Qasama in Hanafi law is a mechanism for imposing collective diya, never for retributive execution, underscoring the high evidentiary standard for qisas.

Ignorance That Constitutes a Valid Legal Excuse (Shubha)
Defines the third type of ignorance that is a valid excuse and divides it into two subtypes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of ignorance that constitute a valid legal excuse (shubha) and apply the distinction to new cases.

Core Idea
Ignorance is a valid excuse only when it arises from genuine legal ambiguity or from an area of valid scholarly disagreement.

We have seen that not all ignorance excuses liability. This passage introduces the third type—ignorance that does constitute a valid excuse, called shubha. The author distinguishes two distinct grounds for such an excuse: when the ruling is open to valid ijtihad, and when the situation itself is legally ambiguous. We will explore each with concrete examples from Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two subtypes of valid ignorance
The passage states two categories: jahl fī mawḍiʿ al-ijtihād al-ṣaḥīḥ and jahl fī mawḍiʿ al-shubha. Clarify the difference in your mind.
The first involves scholarly disagreement; the second involves factual ambiguity.
2
Analyze the condition for the first subtype
The ijtihad must be ṣaḥīḥ – not contradicting the Qur’an and Sunnah, and the matter must not be textually stipulated (manṣūṣ). Understand why ignorance is excused here.
If a text exists, there is no excuse because one could have sought it.
3
Trace the dispute on cupping
The cupping example shows how the first subtype works: al-Awzāʿī held cupping invalidates the fast; Hanafis hold it does not. Because both positions have evidence, the matter is subject to ijtihad, so ignorance excuses kaffārah.
The dispute map in the toolbox details the dalīl on each side.
4
Analyze the second subtype
The second subtype (shubha) does not require ijtihad but arises from legal ambiguity. The son and the slave-girl example shows how overlapping ownership and mutual benefit create confusion.
Shubha is based on mistaken belief that something is evidence (dhann mā laysa bi dalīl dalīlan).
5
Distinguish between shubha and mere ignorance
Not every doubt removes liability. The doubt must be based on a plausible legal reason or genuine ambiguity. Contrast with the first two types of ignorance that do not excuse.
The text implies that ignorance of a clear text is not excused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث جهل يصلح شبهة، وهو الجهل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح، أو في موضع الشبهة كالمحتجم إذا أفطر على ظنّ أن الحجامة فطرته لم تلزمه الكفارة، لأنه جهل في موضع الاجتهاد، ومن زنى بجارية والده على ظن أنها تحلّ له لم يلزمه الحد؛ لأنه جهل في موضع الاشتباه. يصلح شبهة: دارئة للمحدود والكفارات وما هو في معنى العقوبة. الجهل في موضع إلخ: وهو أن يكون المقام موقع اجتهاد المجتهدين، ولا يكون منصوصاً عليه بشرط أن لا يكون الاجتهاد مخالفاً للكتاب والسنة، وهو المـــراد بالصحيح، فالجهل في هذا الموضع عذر ؛ لأنه غير مخالف للكتاب والسنة، والرأي محتمل، وفيه خفاء بخلاف مــــا لو كان المحلّ منصوصاً عليه فإنه لا عذر له بالجهل لتقصيره في طلب النص. موضع الشبهة: والثاني جهل في موضع لم يوجد فيه اجتهاد ولكنه موضع الاشتباه، فيضح عذراً؛ لانه موضع خفاء واشتباه كالمحتجم إلخ : هذا نظير للنوع الأول. صورته أن الصائم احتجم في رمضان ثم غلب على ظنه أن صومه فسد بالحجامة، فأفطر عمداً بعد الحجامة فلايلزم عليه الكفارة؛ لأن هذا المحل موضع للاجتهاد الصحيح؛ لأن الأوزاعي قد ذهب إلى أن الحجامة تفطر الصوم لقوله علي: 'أفطر الحاجم والمحجوم'. رواه الترمذي، [رقم: ٧٧٤] ولنا ما رواه البخاري وغيره وهو أن النبي يحتجم وهو محرم، ويحتجم وهو صائم. [البخاري، رقم: ۱۹۳۸] . ومن زنى بجارية إلخ : هذا نظير للنوع الثاني، وهو أن الولد زنى بجارية أبيه على ظنّ أنها تحلّ له، فلا يجب عليه الحد؛ لأن الأملاك متصلة بين الولد ووالده، والمنافع دائرة بينهما، ولهذا لا يجوز شهادة أحدهما للآخر، ولا أداء الزكاة، فربما يشتبه على الولد أنها لما كانت حلالاً للأصل يكون حلالا للجزء، كما يجوز انتفاع أحدهما بمال الآخر، أما لو قال: ظننت أنها حرام عليّ فيحد. ف: اعلم أن الشبهة الدارئة للحد على نوعين: أحدهما شبهة في الفعل، وتسمّى شبهة اشتباه؛ لأنها تنشأ من الاشتباه، وهو ظنّ ما ليس بدليل دليلا، ولا بدّ فيها من الظنّ ليتحقق الاشتباه كهذه الصورة المذكورة.
And the third is ignorance that constitutes a valid excuse (shubha), which is ignorance in a place of valid ijtihad, or in a place of ambiguity. For example, the cupped person who breaks his fast thinking that cupping breaks his fast: no expiation is required upon him, because it is ignorance in a place of ijtihad. And one who fornicates with his father's slave-girl thinking she is permissible for him: no hadd is required upon him, because it is ignorance in a place of ambiguity. 'Constitutes a valid excuse': repelling from hudud, kaffarat, and what is in the meaning of penalty. 'Ignorance in a place' etc.: That is that the place is a site of ijtihad for mujtahids, and it is not textually stipulated, with the condition that the ijtihad does not contradict the Book and sunnah, and this is what is meant by 'valid'. So ignorance in this place is an excuse, because it does not contradict the Book and sunnah, and opinion is probable, and there is obscurity in it, unlike if the matter were textually stipulated, then there is no excuse for ignorance because of his negligence in seeking the text. 'Place of ambiguity': And the second is ignorance in a place where ijtihad does not exist but it is a place of ambiguity; so it is an excuse because it is a place of obscurity and ambiguity. For example, 'the cupped one' etc.: this is parallel to the first type. Its form is that a fasting person is cupped in Ramadan, then he strongly assumes that his fast is broken by cupping, so he intentionally breaks his fast after cupping; no expiation is required upon him, because this place is a place of valid ijtihad, because al-Awza'i went to the view that cupping breaks the fast, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The cupper and the cupped break their fast.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi [no. 774]. And we have what al-Bukhari and others narrated, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, is cupped while in ihram and is cupped while fasting. [Bukhari, no. 1938]. And 'one who fornicates with a slave-girl' etc.: this is parallel to the second type, that is, a son fornicates with his father's slave-girl thinking she is permissible for him, so no hadd is required upon him, because ownerships are connected between the son and his father, and benefits circulate between them, and for this reason it is not permissible for one of them to testify for the other, nor to pay zakat. So perhaps it is ambiguous to the son that since she is permissible for the origin (the father), she is permissible for the part (the son), just as one of them is permitted to benefit from the other's property. But if he said: 'I thought she was forbidden to me,' then he is punished. So: Know that the shubha that repels hadd is of two types: one is shubha in the act, and it is called shubhat ishtibah, because it arises from ambiguity, and it is considering what is not evidence as evidence, and there must be a presumption to confirm the ambiguity, as in this mentioned example.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on types of ignorance as impediments to liability. After addressing ignorance that is not an excuse, the author now defines the third type: ignorance that does constitute a valid legal excuse (shubha). This type is divided into two subcategories. The first is ignorance in a matter that is a valid subject of ijtihad — that is, where there is no definitive text, and the mujtahid may legitimately differ. In such a case, if someone acts based on a plausible but erroneous ijtihad (e.g., thinking cupping invalidates the fast), he is excused from penalties like kaffarah because the matter is open to interpretation. The second is ignorance in a place of genuine ambiguity (shubha), where the ruling is unclear due to overlapping legal considerations (e.g., the son thinking his father's slave-girl is permissible for him due to the close relationship between father and son's ownership rights). The author uses the example of cupping (hijama) to illustrate the first subtype: a person who is cupped and then breaks his fast thinking his fast is already invalid does not have to pay kaffarah because the ruling on cupping and fasting is a matter of ijtihad (some scholars like al-Awza'i held it invalidates the fast, though the Hanafi view is that it does not). Similarly, the son who fornicates with his father's slave-girl thinking she is halal for him is exempt from the hadd punishment because the situation involves ambiguity (shubha) in the permissibility. The passage concludes by defining shubha that repels hadd as twofold: shubha in the act itself (shubhat ishtibah) which arises from mistaking something as evidence, and requires a genuine belief to constitute the ambiguity.

Key Terms
شبهة دارئة (shubha dāri'a): A legal ambiguity that repels the ḥadd penalty or similar punishments.
اجتهاد صحيح (ijtihād ṣaḥīḥ): Valid ijtihad that is not contrary to explicit texts and is within the scope of scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is a person who fornicates with his father's slave-girl exempt from the hadd punishment?
A) Because he was coerced
B) Because he thought she was permissible due to the ambiguous ownership relationship
C) Because he was ignorant of the law entirely
D) Because the father gave permission

Key Takeaway
Ignorance that excuses from penalties must arise from a valid ijtihad dispute or from genuine legal ambiguity (shubha), not from mere ignorance of a clear text.

Hazl (Jest): Definition and Effect on Contracts
Defines hazl and explains its effect on different types of dispositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of hazl (jest) in Hanafi usul and distinguish between rulings that are affected by jest and those that are not.

Core Idea
Hazl negates only approval (rida); divorce and manumission take effect even when jested.

This lesson unpacks the concept of hazl (jest) as a technical term in Hanafi legal theory. We will examine how jest nullifies certain legal effects while leaving others intact, based on the distinction between actions that depend on the agent's approval (rida) and those that do not. The text also clarifies the condition for invoking hazl and its analogy to option stipulations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of hazl
Read the passage to extract the technical definition: hazl is intending something other than what the utterance was placed for, linguistically and in legal terminology. Note the refinement to exclude metaphor.
The definition is attributed to Fakhr al-Islam and later refined to avoid including majaz.
2
Understand the key concepts: mubashara vs. rida/ikhtiyar
Hazl does not negate the agent's choice and approval of the direct action (mubashara), but it does negate choice and approval of the legal ruling (ikhtiyar al-hukm and rida). This difference is crucial.
Mubashara means the performance of the utterance itself; rida is satisfaction with the ruling.
3
Apply the rule: classify acts
Determine which legal effects depend on rida (e.g., sale, hire) and which do not (e.g., divorce, manumission). Hazl nullifies the former but not the latter.
Rulings that require rida and ikhtiyar are not established; those that do not are established.
4
Note the condition for hazl
Hazl must be explicitly declared verbally (e.g., 'we intend jest') and cannot be inferred from circumstances. It can be stated before the contract, not necessarily within it.
This differs from khiyar al-shart, which must be stipulated within the contract.
5
Categorize the types of acts affected
The text divides acts into three categories: creation of a disposition, information, and matters of belief. Each category has subcategories that either admit or do not admit recision.
For creation, acts that admit recision (like sale) are affected; those that do not (like divorce) are unaffected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهزل وحكمه ] وأما الهزل فتفسيره اللعب، وهو أن يراد بالشيء غير ما وضع له، لغة وفي الاصطلاح أي باللفظ كما مر تقريره واجب شرعاً مقيدا بأمر غير واجب ينصرف إلى غير الواجب، فلايتم الاستدلال، فالاستدلال بالإجماع، فإن قيل: هذا مخالف لقولهم: "فهم المكلّف الخطاب شرط التكليف، والسكران لايفهم لتعطل عقله المميز بين الأمور الحسنة والقبيحة" على قول التفتازاني له أقول على قول من قال: إن العقل لا يزول في السكر وهو يفهم الخطاب فلايرد، وأما على قول غيره فالجواب أنه مكلف زجراً له لارتكابه المحظور، وعليه نص التقى السبكي في شرح المنهاج: أن العاصي بسكره يكلف تغليظاً عليه، وقد نص الشافعي لله على هذا، فإذا ثبت أن السكران مكلف كما مرّ، فلا يبطل شيئا من الأهلية.. أحكام الشرع من الصلاة والصوم وغيرهما. تصرفاته كلها كالطلاق والعتاق والبيع والشراء. إلا الردة استحساناً إلخ: فإنه إذا ارتد السكران وتكلّم بكلمة الكفر في حالة السكر لا يحكم بكفره استحساناً، وجه الاستحسان أن الردة تبنى على القصد، والسكران إن كان مخاطباً ومكلفا في الأحكام زجراً له ولكنه لا قصد له، والكفر إنما يتحقق ببدل الاعتقاد لا يرتفع ولا يثبت إلا بالقصد، وكذا إذا أقرّ بالحدود الخالصة لله تعالى كشرب الخمر والزنا والسرقة لايحد؛ لأن الحد إنما يجب إذا ثبت على إقراره والسكران لا يثبت على شيء. ألا ترى أن العلماء اتفقوا على أن السكر لا يتحقق إلا بزوال عقله حيث لا يميز بين الأشياء ولا يعرف الأرض من السماء، وفي هذه الحالة كيف يثبت على شيء؛ لأنه إنما يتحقق بالعقل والقصد فيعمل: السكر في إسقاط الحد بسبب الرجوع. يحتمل الرجوع وهو الحدود الخالصة لله تعالى بخلاف ما لو أقر بالحدود الغير الخالصة لله كالقذف والقصاص، فإنه لا يصح الرجوع لتعلقه بحقوق العباد، فالسكر لا يعلم فيها، فيؤاخذ بالحدّ والقصاص. اللعب: ضد الجد. غير ما وضع له هذا التفسير مروي عن فخر الإسلام له، فأورد عليه بأنه يشمل المجاز، وقد تكلّف في جوابه بعضهم، فقال: ليس المراد بالوضع هنا وضع اللغة بل وضع العقلاء، وقيل: المراد بالوضع المنفي هنا ما هو أعم من وضع اللفظ للمعنى، ومن وضع التصرفات الشرعية لأحكامها، والمراد بوضع اللفظ ما هو أعم من الوضع الشخصي كوضع الألفاظ لمعانيها الحقيقية، ومن النوعي كوضع الألفاظ لمعانيها المجازية، فخرج المجاز. وبعضهم= فلاينافي الرضاء بالمباشرة، ولهذا يكفر بالردة هازلاً لكنه ينافي اختيار الحكم أي الهزل والرضاء به بمنزلة شرط الخيار في البيع، فيؤثر فيما يحتمل النقض كالبيع والإجارة، فإذا تواضعا على الهزل بأصل البيع ينعقد البيع فاسدًا غير موجب للملك. كلمات زاد قيداً آخر وهو ما لايصلح له اللفظ استعارةً يعني ما لا يحتمله اللفظ لا باعتبار الحقيقة ولا باعتبار المجاز، والأوضح أن يقال في تعريفه : هو أن لايراد باللفظ معناه الحقيقي ولا المجازي. بالمباشرة : أي الهزل لا ينافي الاختيار ،والرضاء والمباشرة نفس الهزل الذي هو سبب الحكم؛ لأنه باشر السبب وهو التكلم بما هزل به عن اختيار ورضي من غير إكراه هازلا لأنه استخف بالدين الحق وهو كفر، فيصير مرتداً بنفس الهزل؛ لأنه أصدر كلمة الكفر بالرضاء والاختيار، فالهزل لا يمنع الرضاء والاختيار بالمباشرة. اختيار الحكم أي ينافي اختيار الهازل حكم ما هزل به الرضاء به أي رضاه بذلك الحكم؛ لأنه لم يقصده و لم يستعمله له بل قصد به خلاف ذلك، فلايكون مختاراً له ولا راضياً به. والحاصل أن الهزل ينافي إرادة الحكم والرضاء به، فلا يثبت بالهزل الأحكام الموقوفة على الرضاء والاختيار، ولا ينافي الرضاء بما تكلّم به من الهزل؛ لأنه باشر بقصده واختياره بلا إكراه فيثبت به ما لا يتوقف على الرضاء والإرادة وإنما جمع بين الرضاء والاختيار ولم يكتف بأحدهما ؛ لأن الاختيار قد ينفك عن أحدهما؛ إذ الاختيار هو القصد إلى الشيء وإرادته، والرضاء إيثاره واستحسانه، ولذا قيل: إن المعاصي والقبائح بإرادة الله تعالى ولا يقال: برضاه؛ لأن الله لا يرضى لعباده الكفر والهزل في تفويت اختيار الحكم والرضاء به وفي إثبات الرضاء بالمباشرة. بمنزلة شرط إلخ : فكما أن الهزل يعدم اختيار الحكم والرضاء به فكذلك شرط الخيار يعدم الرضاء بحكم البيع الذي هو سبب الحكم؛ لأن العاقل باشر السبب وهو قوله: بعت واشتريت باختياره ورضاه من غير جبر، ولكن فرق بينهما من حيث أن الهزل يفسد البيع بخلاف خيار الشرط. كالبيع والإجارة: فكل حكم يتعلق ولا يتوقف ثبوته على الرضاء والاختيار يثبت بالهزل ولايؤثر الهزل في إسقاطه ونقضه كالطلاق والعتاق وكل حكم يتعلق بالرضاء والاختيار ويتوقف ثبوته عليهما لا يثبت بالهزل ولايؤثر الهزل في إسقاطه ونقضه كالبيع والإجارة، ولكن شرط الهزل التصريح به قولا بأن يقول :الهازلان: نريد الهزل في العقد، بالسبب وهو التلفظ ولا يثبت ذلك بدلالة الحال إلا أنه لم يشترط ذكره في العقد بل يكفي ذكره سابقاً بخلاف خيار الشرط. ف: ثم جملة ما يدخل فيه الهزل ثلاثة أنواع، إنشاء تصرف والإخبار عن تصرّف وما يتعلق بالاعتقاد، ثم الإنشاء على وجهين ما يحتمل النقض كالبيع والإجارة وما لا يحتمله كالطلاق والعتاق وكذا الإخبار على وجهين: ما يحتمل النقض وما لا يحتمله، وما يتعلق بالاعتقاد أيضا على وجهين: حسن كالإيمان وقبيح كالكفر، ثم الهزل في القسم الأول وهو الإنشاء القابل للنقض على ثلاثة أوجه إما أن هزلا بأصل العقد أو بقدر العوض فيه أو بجنس=
Jest and its ruling. As for jest, its interpretation is play, and it is that something is intended other than what it was placed for, linguistically and in terminology, i.e., by the wording, as previously established. Wajib by Sharia bound by a non-obligatory matter diverts to the non-obligatory, so the inference is not complete, so inference is by consensus. If it is said: this contradicts their statement: 'The understanding of the obligated person of the address is a condition of obligation, and the drunk does not understand...' [then long repetition of the drunk discussion]. Play: the opposite of seriousness. 'Other than what it was placed for' this interpretation is narrated from Fakhr al-Islam, it was objected that it includes metaphor (majaz), and some strained to answer it, saying: the intended 'placement' here is not the linguistic placement but the placement of rational people. And it was said: the intended 'placement' negated here is more general than the placement of the word for the meaning, and the placement of legal dispositions for their rulings, and the intended 'placement of the word' is more general than personal placement (like placing words for their real meanings) and generic placement (like placing words for their metaphorical meanings), so metaphor is excluded. And some inserted an additional restriction: that the wording is not suitable for metaphor, meaning that it does not admit it either as reality or metaphor. The clearest definition is: it is that the literal meaning of the wording is not intended, nor the metaphorical. 'Does not negate approval of the direct action': i.e., jest does not negate choice and approval of the direct action itself, because he performed the cause (the utterance) with choice and approval without coercion, jokingly, because he made light of the true religion, which is disbelief, so he becomes an apostate by the jest itself. 'But it negates choice of the ruling': i.e., it negates the jester's choice and approval of the ruling of what he jested about; because he did not intend it and did not use it for that purpose but intended something else. The summary: jest negates the intention and approval of the ruling, so rulings that depend on approval and choice are not established by jest. It does not negate approval of the utterance itself because he performed it with his intention and choice. Therefore, rulings that do not depend on approval and choice are established by jest (like divorce and manumission), while those that depend on them are not (like sale and hire). The condition of jest is that it is explicitly stated verbally, e.g., the two jesters say, 'We intend jest in the contract,' and it is not established by circumstantial evidence. However, it is not required to mention it in the contract; mentioning it beforehand is sufficient, unlike the option stipulation. Then the totality of what enters into jest is three types: creation of a disposition, information about a disposition, and matters related to belief. Creation is of two types: what admits recision (like sale and hire) and what does not (like divorce and manumission). Similarly, information is of two types. Belief is of two types: good (like faith) and evil (like disbelief). Then jest in the first category (creation that admits recision) is on three faces: either jest concerning the original contract, or concerning the amount of the consideration, or concerning the type.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines hazl (jest) and explains its effects on various legal acts. The definition is attributed to Fakhr al-Islam: hazl is intending something other than what the word or act was placed for, i.e., using a statement or action without intending its literal consequence but rather playfully. However, this definition was criticized for including metaphor, so they refined it: the wording must not admit any real or metaphorical meaning. The essential principle is that jest does not affect the performer's choice and approval regarding the direct action (mubashara) of uttering the words; thus, if someone jests by uttering words of disbelief, he becomes an apostate because he performed the action with choice (he was not coerced). However, jest negates the choice and approval of the legal ruling that normally results from the utterance. For example, in a contract of sale, which requires the parties' approval and intention to be valid, jest invalidates the contract because the necessary consent is missing; such a contract is concluded as fasid (invalid). In contrast, acts like divorce (talaq) and manumission (itaq) do not require the approval of the legal ruling to take effect; they are based solely on the utterance and choice, so even if jested, they are valid and binding. The author analogizes jest to an option stipulation (khiyar al-shart) in that both negate the approval of the ruling, but they differ in effect: jest invalidates the contract outright, while a valid option stipulation does not. A critical condition for jest to affect a contract is that it must be explicitly declared verbally (e.g., 'we are jesting'), and it is not inferred from circumstances. However, it can be stated before the contract, not necessarily within it. Finally, the passage categorizes acts subject to jest into three types: creation (contracts like sale or rent, and status changes like divorce), information (reports), and matters of belief (faith or disbelief). In each, jest applies only to those that admit recision (nuqd) if contract, or that involve choice/approval. This nuanced treatment exemplifies the Hanafi approach to balancing outward acts with inward intent.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or playful speech/action where the speaker intends something other than the literal meaning, or does not intend the legal effect.
الرضاء (al-rida): Approval or satisfaction with the legal ruling; required for contracts like sale but not for divorce.
الاختيار (al-ikhtiyar): Choice or free will; the capacity to intend an action. Jest negates ikhtiyar of the ruling but not of the utterance.
المباشرة (al-mubashara): The direct action of utterance; jest does not negate the performer's choice and approval of this direct action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person jests in a contract of sale by saying 'I sell you this for $100' but intends no sale, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid because the words are clear.
B) The sale is void (batil) and has no effect.
C) The sale is invalid (fasid) because the required approval (rida) is missing.
D) The sale is valid only if the buyer knows it is a jest.

Key Takeaway
Jest nullifies only those legal effects that depend on the agent's approval (rida); effects like divorce and manumission are established despite jest.

The Effect of Jest on Mahr in Marriage
Usul rule on jest in mahr and refutation of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between marriage and sale to determine the ruling on jest in mahr, and evaluate the qiyas of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid without mahr specification, so jest in mahr does not invalidate; mahr al-mithl applies.

This passage from Muntakhab al-Husami addresses a classic usul problem: when two parties jest about the mahr, does the marriage remain valid? The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith 'Three things: their seriousness is serious, their jest is serious', holds that marriage is valid, but the mahr may revert to mahr al-mithl. This ruling is derived by distinguishing marriage from sale, where jest could invalidate. The discussion also involves the two companions' qiyas, which is refuted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the nature of jest
The act is marriage, and the jest is about the mahr (amount or type). The question: does jest affect the validity of marriage or the mahr obligation?
Jest (hazl) is a joking intention while uttering contract terms.
2
Distinguish marriage from sale
Marriage is valid without specifying mahr, whereas sale requires a specified price. This difference is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that jest in mahr does not invalidate marriage.
3
Apply the hadith
The hadith 'Three things: their seriousness is serious, their jest is serious' establishes that marriage, divorce, and manumission are binding even if done in jest.
The hadith is a dalil naqli with zanni thubut but qati dalala.
4
Work through the four scenarios
According to the text, there are four scenarios: agreement on abandonment, agreement on construction (building on the jest), silence, and disagreement. In each, derive whether the named mahr or mahr al-mithl applies.
Mahr al-mithl is the standard dowry for a woman of her status.
5
Refute the opposing qiyas
The Sahibayn analogized marriage to sale, arguing that jest invalidates. The Hanafi response: marriage is valid without mahr specification, so the two conventions (seriousness in marriage, jest in mahr) can be combined; in sale they cannot.
The refutation is based on the possibility of combining the two conventions (al-muwaḍa'atayn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأمكن العمل بالمواضعتين ولو ذكرا في النكاح الدنانير وغرضهما الدراهم يجب مهر المثل؛ لأن النكاح يصحّ بغير تسمية بخلاف البيع، ولو هزلا بأصل النكاح فالهزل باطل والعقد لازم. فيحب مهر المثل. قوله عليها ثلاث جدهن جدّ، وهزلهنّ......] وكذلك الطلاق والعتاق والعفو عن القصاص واليمين والنذر؛ صحيح. العمل بالمواضعتين إحداهما المواضعة بالجد بأصل النكاح والأخرى المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار المهر، والعمل على تلك المواضعة لاينافي العمل بالمواضعة بالجد بأصل النكاح؛ لأن مقتضى الأولى تصحيح النكاح، وتلك المواضعة لاتنافي صحة النكاح؛ إذ غايتها أنها شرط فاسد يخل بالمهر ، والنكاح لا يفسد بالشرط الفاسد بل لا يضره عدم تسمية المهـــر، فأمكن الجمع بينهما، فالعمل بالأولى أفاد صحة النكاح، والعمل بالأخرى أفاد وجود أقل المهر وهو الألف الألف، فاندفع قياس الصاحبين، حيث قاسا البيع على النكاح؛ لأن البيع يفسد بالشرط الفاسد، فلا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعتين فيـــه كما مر تقريره منا، أو سكتا أي اتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شيءٌ أو اختلفا في البناء والإعراض فالمعتبر و المسمّى فيجب ألفان كما في البيع، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف ولو ذكرا أي الزوج والزوجة أو وليها. وغرضهما الدراهم إلخ هذا نظير للهزل في جنس البدل، وهذا أيضا على أربعة أوجه والنكاح في كل الوجوه بالاتفاق، وإنما الكلام في وجوب المسمّى الوجه الأول: هو إن اتفقا على الإعراض عن الهزل فالمهر هــو المسمّى، وهو مائة دينار لبطلان المواضعة بالإعراض والوجه الثاني: هو إن اتفقا على البناء فمهر المثل بالاتفاق؛ لأن المسمّى لا يصلح مهراً لقصدهما الهزل به والمال لا يثبت بالهزل، وكذا الدراهم التي تواضعا عليها؛ لأنهما لم يذكراها في العقد، وبدون الذكر فيه لايصير مهراً، فصار كأنه تزوجها على غير المهر ولكن لايفسد النكاح بخلاف البيع: حيث لا يصح بغير تسمية الثمن، فإذا خلا البيع عن الثمن فسد فلا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعتين في الهزل بجنس الثمن، وفي الجد بأصل البيع كما مرّ تقريره، وهذا الوجه بينه المصنف في الكتاب والوجه الثالث هو السكوت، والوجه الرابع هو التخالف، ففي هذين الوجهين يجب مهر المثل اتفاقاً في رواية عن أبي حنيفة له، وهو رواية محمـــد لله لأن المهر تابع، فيجب العمل بالهزل كيلا يصير المهر مقصوداً بالصحة؛ إذ لا حاجة لانعقاد النكاح إلى صحته.
So it is possible to act on both conventions. If in marriage they mentioned dinars but intended dirhams, the mahr of the like is obligatory because marriage is valid without specification, unlike sale. If they jest in the foundation of marriage, the jest is void and the contract is binding. So the mahr of the like is obligatory. His statement: 'three things: their seriousness is serious, their jest is serious...' and likewise divorce, manumission, pardon for qisas, oath, and vow are valid. Acting on both conventions: one convention is the serious convention in the foundation of marriage, and the other convention is the jest in the amount of the mahr. Acting on that convention does not contradict acting on the serious convention in the foundation of marriage because the implication of the first is validating the marriage, and that convention does not contradict the validity of marriage; its limit is that it is an invalid condition that affects the mahr, but marriage is not invalidated by an invalid condition, nor is it harmed by the lack of specification of the mahr. So it is possible to combine them. Acting on the first gives the validity of marriage, and acting on the other gives the existence of the least mahr, i.e., one thousand. So the analogy of the two companions is repelled, where they analogized sale to marriage because sale is invalidated by an invalid condition, so it is not possible to combine the two conventions in it as we have previously explained. Or they remained silent, i.e., they agreed that nothing was present to them, or they differed regarding construction and abandonment, then the named [amount] is considered and two thousand is obligatory as in sale, and this is a narration from Abu Yusuf. And if they, i.e., the husband and wife or her guardian, mentioned the dinars but intended dirhams, etc., this is analogous to jest in the type of the substitute. This also has four aspects, and marriage in all aspects is agreed upon, but the discussion is concerning the obligation of the named [mahr]. The first aspect: if they agree on abandonment of the jest, then the mahr is the named, which is one hundred dinars, because the convention is invalidated by abandonment. The second aspect: if they agree on construction, then the mahr of the like is unanimously agreed; because the named mahr is not valid as mahr due to their intention of jest with it, and wealth is not established by jest. Similarly, the dirhams they agreed upon because they did not mention them in the contract, and without mention in it, they do not become mahr. So it is as if he married her without a mahr, but the marriage is not invalid, unlike sale: where it is not valid without specifying the price, so if the sale lacks the price, it becomes invalid, so it is not possible to combine the two conventions in jest with the type of price, and in seriousness in the foundation of sale, as we have previously explained. This aspect is clarified by the author in the book. The third aspect is silence, and the fourth aspect is disagreement. In these two aspects, the mahr of the like is obligatory, by consensus in a narration from Abu Hanifa, and it is a narration from Muhammad, because the mahr is subsidiary, so acting on the jest is obligatory so that the mahr does not become intended for validity; since there is no need for its validity in the conclusion of marriage.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on analogy, discussing the effect of jest (hazl) on the amount or type of mahr in marriage. The key principle is that marriage is valid even if the mahr is not specified, unlike sale which requires a specified price. Therefore, if a man mentions dinars as mahr but both intend dirhams (jest in the type), or if they jest about the amount (e.g., saying a large sum but meaning only a symbolic one), the marriage is still valid. The woman receives mahr al-mithl (standard dowry) unless both parties clearly abandon the jest, in which case the named amount applies. The text outlines four scenarios (agreement on abandonment, agreement on construction, silence, disagreement) and the resulting obligations. This ruling distinguishes marriage from sale, following the Hanafi school, and refutes the analogy of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who analogized sale to marriage. The hadith 'Three things: their seriousness is serious, their jest is serious' is cited as evidence that marriage is binding even if jested.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or joking, which does not affect the validity of certain foundational acts like marriage
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dowry for a woman of her status, used when the specified mahr is invalidated by jest

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says 'I marry you for 100 dinars' but both intend 100 dirhams (jest in the type of mahr), and they agree on the jest, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid because the mahr is jested
B) The marriage is valid and the woman receives 100 dinars
C) The marriage is valid and the woman receives mahr al-mithl
D) The marriage is valid and the woman receives 100 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Jest in the mahr of a marriage does not invalidate the contract; the woman receives mahr al-mithl unless the parties agree to abandon the jest.

Huzl Invalidates Iqrar and Shuf'a
Rulings on huzl invalidating iqrar and shuf'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that huzl invalidates iqrar and taslim al-shuf'a by identifying the rational evidence (dalil aqli) and explaining its wajh al-dalalah.

Core Idea
Huzl invalidates a confession because jest negates the truthfulness required for a report.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text examines the effect of huzl (jest) on two specific legal acts: iqrar (confession) and taslim al-shuf'a (delivery of preemption). While contracts are also affected by huzl, the author focuses on these unilateral declarations to illustrate how the principle of huzl operates. The key proof is a rational inference: huzl indicates the non-existence of the reported matter. In this lesson, we will trace the derivation of this ruling and understand its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the ruling
Locate in the source the specific acts mentioned: iqrar (confession) and taslim al-shuf'a (delivery of preemption). Note that huzl invalidates both, whether the subject of the confession admits rescission or not.
2
Extract the rational evidence (dalil aqli)
Find the phrase: 'لأن الهزل يدلّ على عدم المخبر به' (because huzl indicates the non-existence of the reported matter). This is the core proof. Recognize that it is a rational inference, not a transmitted text.
The dalil is aqli (rational) rather than naqli (textual).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the phrase proves the ruling: a confession is a report of a fact; huzl (jest) contradicts the truthfulness of that report; thus the confession cannot be taken as evidence. The same applies to taslim al-shuf'a, which is a conveyance of a right.
The illa (effective cause) is the contradiction between jest and truthfulness.
4
Distinguish from contracts
Note that the passage also mentions a broader discussion on contracts (khul') where there is ikhtilaf. For iqrar and shuf'a, the ruling is clear and undisputed. Understand why huzl operates similarly here despite the acts being unilateral.
Contracts involve mutual consent; iqrar and shuf'a are unilateral declarations.
5
Apply the principle to new cases
Using the rational evidence, derive the ruling for a scenario where someone jokingly confesses to a debt. Conclude that the confession is invalid, so no liability arises.
This illustrates the consistency of Hanafi usul across different acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمور التي يبطلها الهزل]
العقد
وأما الإقرار فالهزل يبطله، سواء كان الإقرار بما يحتمل الفسخ أو بما لا يحتمله؛ لأن الهزل
يدلّ على عدم المخبر به، وكذلك تسليم الشفعة بعد الطلب والإشهاد يبطله الهزل؛
...
فيجب المال في الحال ويلزم العقد بالاتفاق، وإنما الاختلاف في تخريجها كما يشير إليه المصنف بقوله: أما إلخ. لم يحضرهما شيء إلخ: وهذا على ثلاثة أوجه أحدها أن يكون الهزل في أصل العقد، والثاني أن يكون بقدر البدل، والثالث بجنسه اختلفا في البناء والإعراض، وهذا أيضا على ثلاثة أوجه الأول الهزل في أصل العقد ويقع الاختلاف، والثاني بقدر البدل ويقع الخلاف والثالث بجنسه ويقع الخلاف في البناء والإعراض، ففي تلك
